1601 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Fyksen v. Dakota County Cmty. Dev. Agency


A08-0372


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 252



March 10, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator participant sought review of the termination of her Section 8 housing-assistance benefits by respondent county agency.


OVERVIEW: The participant received housing-assistance benefits for more than two decades, with one interruption around 1991. In April 2001, the participant pled guilty to misdemeanor fifth-degree assault related to a February 2001 incident for which she served three days in jail. The participant's recertification applications for her housing-assistance benefits included a question as to whether she had participated in a violence related activity, and the participant marked no every time. In 2007, an criminal background check revealed the 2001 conviction, and the county agency decided to terminate the participant's housing-assistance benefits based on the alleged repeated misrepresentations. The court ruled that the participant's fifth-degree assault did not have as one of its elements the infliction of serious bodily injury, and the participant could reasonably conclude that the fifth-degree assault conviction was not within the scope of the recertification applications. Mere bodily harm, as was required for a conviction of fifth-degree assault, was not serious bodily injury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1602 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Skerjance


A08-0065


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 214



March 3, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Skerjance, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 291 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. K2-07-427.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of first-degree driving while impaired (DWI).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of DWI. The district court enhanced the offense from second-degree to first-degree DWI, based on his prior DWI conviction in Alaska in 1999 and the resulting revocation of his Alaska driver's license. Defendant challenged the enhancement of his offense by arguing that his 1999 Alaska plea of nolo contendere was entered in violation of his right to counsel; the district court properly held that defendant validly waived his constitutional right to counsel prior to his plea. The district court properly rejected defendant's challenge to the factual basis of the plea; under Alaska law, it was impermissible for a trial court to inquire into the factual basis of a plea of nolo contendere. The Court of Appeals of Minnesota held that defendant's DWI charge could be enhanced based on a foreign state's revocation of his driver's license, even if he was not given the opportunity to consult with an attorney before he submitted to an alcohol-concentration test.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1603 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Ali v. Dakota County Cmty. Dev. Agency


A08-0112


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 235



March 3, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator program participant challenged the termination of her Section 8 housing benefits by respondent Dakota County Community Development Agency (CDA), Minnesota.


OVERVIEW: The hearing officer concluded that the participant violated her program obligation of cooperating with the CDA due to her failure to attend a required annual recertification appointment, and that her Section 8 participation should be terminated as proposed by the CDA. The participant argued that the CDA misapplied the law to conclude that she did not comply with disclosure obligations, the record did not support the conclusion that she refused or failed to make required disclosures, and the hearing officer's findings were inadequate. The court ruled that the CDA's stated basis for terminating the participant's benefits was legally insufficient, and the evidence did not support a finding that the participant failed to cooperate with the CDA. The CDA's administrative plan did not provide the CDA with authority to terminate benefits for missing an appointment, because the Code of Federal Regulations (C.F.R.) declared that the administrative plan bound the CDA, not the participant, and the C.F.R. requirements of the administrative plan did not include provisions for mandatory attendance at annual reexamination appointments.


OUTCOME: The termination of Section 8 housing benefits was reversed.

 

1604 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dugan


A07-2457


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 230



March 3, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota County District Court File No. K9-07-177.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his motion to suppress evidence of drugs found in his car after a traffic stop.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that police unlawfully expanded the scope of a stop and that the evidence from the stop was inadmissible. On appeal, the court held that defendant's nervousness, the nervousness of his passengers, a report of a suspicious vehicle, dishonesty in answering a simple question, change of an answer, and the out-of-place nature of defendant's car, all logically provoked the police officer's suspicion of illegal activity after stopping defendant's car for failing to signal a lane change. The court held that the officer had reasonable, articulable suspicion, and that the stop's expansion was adequately supported. Each incremental intrusion on defendant's liberty was justified as Minn. Const. art. I, § 10 required. The court found that the officer's efficient, five-minute investigation lacked any constitutional infirmity. Furthermore, the expansion of the substantive scope and duration of the traffic stop was justified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order.

 

1605 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mohamed


A07-2081


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 211



February 24, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 06026206.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of fifth-degree possession of cathinone. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that Minn. Stat. § 152.025, subd. 2(1) (2006) was void for vagueness. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the State did not need to prove that the quantity of the cathinone present in the khat had a stimulant effect; khat contained cathinone, which was illegal to possess. The omission of "khat" from the controlled substance law did not preclude a conviction under Minn. Stat. § 152.02, subd. 2(6) (2006), which prohibited possession of cathinone. The district court did not err in determining that the State satisfied the requirement that defendant knowingly possessed a controlled substance. Prior caselaw made it clear that Minnesota law prohibited the possession of khat because it contained cathinone. Therefore, the fair warning requirement was satisfied. Minnesota's scienter requirement overcame any vagueness concern that a person of ordinary intelligence would expose himself to criminal penalties due to the vagueness of the controlled substances schedules with respect to khat. The State presented sufficient evidence to satisfy all three of the elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1606 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


A07-1978


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 213



February 24, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Anderson, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 314 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota County District Court File No. K8-07-672.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motion to suppress the drug evidence found on his person during a search, the Dakota County District Court, Minnesota, convicted him of third-degree possession of a controlled substance and imposed a 45-month executed prison term. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the district court erred when it admitted evidence obtained as the result of an unconstitutional stop and search; defendant also argued that the district court failed to make requisite findings of fact pursuant to Minn. R. Crim. P. 26.01, subd. 4. The appellate court disagreed in part, holding first that, based on the totality of the circumstances (the place, time of night, defendant's mannerisms, actions, how he was carrying himself, how he was dressed, and his nervousness), the police sergeant had a reasonable, articulable suspicion to suspect that defendant was involved in a burglary of the closed businesses and, therefore, the investigatory stop was justified. Further, the sergeant had a reasonable basis for the pat-down search based on defendant's furtive movements, avoiding eye contact, refusing to answer, not complying with police requests by continuing to reach his hands into his pockets, and acting nervously. However, the appellate court agreed that the district court erred by failing to make any findings as to each element of the offense, as required by Minn. R. Crim. P. 26.01, subd. 4.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but the case was remanded to the district court to make findings of fact as to each element of the offense.

 

1607 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Hassan v. Dakota County Cmty. Dev. Agency


A08-0373


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 204



February 24, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota County Community Development Agency.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator program participant challenged the judgment of respondent Dakota County Community Development Agency (CDA), Minnesota, terminating her Section 8 public housing benefits, and demanding that she repay $ 4,584 in rental assistance benefits she received from July through December 2007.


OVERVIEW: The CDA terminated the participant's benefits, alleging that she failed to provide proper 2006 tax documents, and failed to report that her husband had moved into her rent-assisted unit in June 2007. The court ruled that the CDA's decision was not supported by substantial evidence that the participant failed either to provide proper tax documents or that her husband had moved into her rent-assisted unit. The CDA had not produced evidence that the participant's husband was actually living in her rent-assisted unit from July to December 2007. Also, the participant made two attempts to submit what she thought was her tax information, and the record did not show whether she had sufficient income to necessitate filing a tax return in Minnesota. Furthermore, the court found that the CDA decision was arbitrary and capricious because it failed to consider evidence of the participant's poor English proficiency, and the effect that termination of her rental assistance would have on her five young children. The CDA decision was arbitrary and capricious because it failed to consider these mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

1608 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Sandstrom v. Dakota County Cmty. Dev. Agency


A08-0374


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 210



February 24, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator program participant challenged the termination of her Section 8 housing benefits by respondent county agency.


OVERVIEW: The participant had been involved in the Section 8 rental assistance program through the county agency since 2005. In October 2007, the participant was notified that her participation in the program would be terminated for failing to report employment. The participant requested an informal hearing, and the hearing officer found that the participant's termination was justified because her failure to report three separate places of employment established a pattern of failure to report employment. The court ruled that the participant failed to meet her burden of demonstrating that the hearing officer's decision was unsupported in light of the record considered as a whole. The participant did not contest that she failed to report the income. The record demonstrated that the program required participants to annually recertify. In her July 2007 recertification application the participant listed no current or previous work history. The regulations made no distinction between minor and serious violations. The participant had a responsibility to correctly report household income, and she signed statements affirming that she understood the consequences of failing to do so.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1609 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nason


A07-1187


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 153



February 3, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Itasca County District Court File No. 31-CR-07-1043.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Itasca County District Court (Minnesota) that convicted him of fifth-degree possession of a controlled substance under Minn. Stat. § 152.025, subd. 2(1) (2006), arguing that trial counsel was ineffective and that the evidence was insufficient to establish that he possessed methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: During a blizzard, a police sergeant saw two vehicles parked in the middle of a road. He approached, thinking that one of the driver's might be having car trouble and need assistance. He noticed three men standing beside a truck exchanging something. Suspecting that they were engaged in a drug transaction, the sergeant began walking quickly toward the vehicles. When the men attempted to get into the truck, the sergeant drew his gun and ordered all of the men to exit the vehicles. When defendant did so, he tossed a baggie away. The baggie was retrieved, and testing revealed that it contained methamphetamine. On review, the court rejected defendant's argument that the evidence showed that he had only momentary control of the drugs and held that the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction. The statutory language did not require defendant to possess the drugs for any specific period of time, and Minnesota did not recognize a "fleeting possession" exception to the offense of drug possession. Because Minnesota did not recognize the fleeting possession defense, counsel was not ineffective for failing to request a fleeting possession jury instruction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

1610 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Huntsman v. Huntsman


A08-0313


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 83



January 20, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Motion denied by Huntsman v. Huntsman, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 163 (2009)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Huntsman v. Huntsman, 2011 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 515 (Minn. Ct. App., May 31, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Washington County District Court File No. 82F798002231.
Huntsman v. Huntsman, 2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 650 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a divorce action in Washington County District Court (Minnesota), appellant husband filed a motion to vacate an order directing respondent county to withhold income from the husband and pay it to respondent wife. The district court denied the motion to vacate, and the order was affirmed on appeal. Following the issuance of a new income-withholding order, the husband filed another motion to vacate, which was also denied. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the case was on appeal from the original denial of the motion to vacate, the husband's child support obligation ended, leaving only his maintenance obligation. Therefore, the county issued a new income-withholding order and began imposing a $ 15 fee for collecting the income. The husband argued that any standing and authority that county had to withhold income ended when his child-support obligation ended. The court held that the husband's standing claims were barred by the res judicata effect of the prior judgment on appeal because the claims and parties were identical, and the husband had a full opportunity to litigate his claims. The court held that there was no statutory support under Minn. Stat. § 518A.53, subd. 3 (2008), or Minn. Stat. § 518A.50(b) (2008) for the husband's argument that the wife was required to reapply for withholding-only services before the county could impose the service fee. The husband's challenge to the county's status as an intervenor under Minn. R. Civ. P. 24 was also barred by res judicata.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the withholding order to the extent that it did not require the husband to pay the wife's health insurance premiums and remanded the case for issuance of a new order. The court affirmed as to the remaining issues.

Pittman v. Dakota County Cmty. Dev. Agency


A07-2063


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 92



January 20, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Pittman v. Dakota County Cmty. Dev. Agency, 2010 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 548 (Minn. Ct. App., June 15, 2010)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Realtor claimant challenged the judgment of a hearing officer, Minnesota, upholding the decision of respondent public housing authority (the authority), terminating her eligibility to receive public housing assistance.


OVERVIEW: The claimant had received housing assistance since 1997. Beginning in September 2006, the claimant received housing assistance through a voucher program administered by the public housing authority. The public housing authority terminated the claimant's housing assistance effective August 31, 2007, after the claimant allegedly failed to report that another adult was living with her. At that time, the claimant had five children, including one with profound disabilities, and was pregnant with her sixth child. The court ruled that the public housing authority failed to make findings of fact to support its decision to terminate the claimant's public housing benefits, and that the legal basis for termination was unclear. The claimant presented evidence indicating that she had numerous children and that she and her children would be homeless if she lost her housing assistance. The record further indicated that the claimant was pregnant at the time of the hearing, and that one of her children suffered from profound disabilities and could not walk. The hearing officer's decision did not reflect a consideration of these circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

1612 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Gorokhova


A08-0271


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 47



January 13, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Barkhudarov v. Dakota County CDA, 2010 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 504 (Minn. Ct. App., June 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota Community Development Agency.
Barkhudarov v. Rensenbrink, 2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 981 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator claimants, a husband and a wife that received housing assistance, challenged the calculation of family income for public-housing-subsidy purposes by the Dakota Community Development Agency (Minnesota) (CDA).


OVERVIEW: The claimants received housing assistance through the Section 8 voucher program, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1437f(o). The claimants were required to submit to annual review of income by the CDA, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1437f(o)(2)(A), because the amount of assistance received was based on family income. The claimants challenged the CDA's calculation of family income, arguing that the CDA should have given them a standard $ 20 exclusion. The court held that exclusions of the first $20 of unearned income did not apply in the Section 8 context. The claimants next contended that the CDA erred in failing to exclude a special dietary allowance from his income. The regulatory definition of medical expenses, under 24 C.F.R. § 5.603(b) (2008), did not exclude medical-diet allowances. The court held that, if the special diet was medically necessary as prescribed by a licensed physician, relators could receive a Minnesota Supplemental Aid medical-diet allowance, under Minn. Stat. § 256D.44, subd. 5(a) (2008).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment with respect to the exclusion and reversed the judgment with respect to the dietary allowance. The court remanded for further findings on whether the dietary allowance was a medically prescribed diet.

 

1613 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Iverson v. State


A08-0366


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 6



January 6, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Iverson v. State, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 94 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. K3-97-2703.
State v. Iverson, 1998 Minn. App. LEXIS 1254 (Minn. Ct. App., Nov. 17, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a pro se appeal challenging a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) summarily denying his fourth postconviction petition seeking to correct his sentence, under Minn. R. Crim. P. 27.03, subd. 9.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree assault, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.221 (Supp. 1997), and first-degree burglary, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.582, subd. 1(c) (1996). He was sentenced to 68 months for the burglary and 200-months for the assault, which was an upward departure based on a four-week pattern of harassment and stalking of the victim prior to the assault. Following his conviction, petitioner was diagnosed with paranoid schizophrenia. In his fourth postconviction petition, petitioner argued that his sentence should be reduced to the presumptive sentence because of his mental illness and memory loss and because he learned that the stalking charges against him had been dismissed. The court held that petitioner was not entitled to further review of the claims based on his mental illness because they were raised in his earlier petitions. A claim known at the time of a direct appeal and not raised at that time will not be considered in postconviction proceedings. The court also held that the upward departure was not based on a conviction for stalking. The fact that the charges were dismissed did not, by itself, demonstrate that no stalking occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

1614 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Patterson


A07-1912


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1523



December 30, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. T2-06-611306.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, which convicted him for violating an order for protection (OFP) under Minn. Stat. § 518B.01, subd. 14 (2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in declining to instruct the jury that intent is an element of the crime of violating an OFP. The instant court concluded that the trial court did not err in declining to instruct the jury on intent. Because defendant had telephone contact with the complainant, knowing of the OFP, the trial court determined that a jury could reasonably conclude that defendant violated the OFP. This was not a situation in which accidental contact was a defense and a jury instruction was necessary to avoid a wrongful conviction. However brief defendant's telephone contact with the complainant was, he engaged in conversation with her, knowing of the OFP, and that prohibited contact resulted in his conviction. The OFP statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad or vague because it defined the violation of an OFP with sufficient definiteness and was properly limited in scope. Defendant was not entitled to a new trial. Although defendant contended that there were irregularities at trial, he failed to show that he was prejudiced or that his substantial rights were affected by these irregularities.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1615 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Tuff v. Winona County


A08-0696


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1521



December 30, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Winona County District Court File No. CV-07-3408.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner filed an action against defendant county in the Winona County District Court (Minnesota), alleging (1) illegal taking by wrongful enforcement of a zoning ordinance; (2) unconstitutional taking; (3) discriminatory enforcement; and (4) wrongful taking of nonconforming use. The district court granted summary judgment in favor of the county, and the landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1976, the landowner purchased the land for the purpose of advertising his museum; the land was then zoned R-2 residential. In 1984, he had the property rezoned to C-3 commercial. In 1988, the county enacted a comprehensive zoning ordinance under which the property was zoned agricultural/natural-resource. The landowner argued that the 1988 ordinance was enacted without the proper procedural, legal, and statutory safeguards and violated his right to due process. The zoning ordinance was signed by the chairman of the county board of commissioners and the county clerk. The county auditor stated that the zoning ordinance had been compiled in the official ordinance books since 1989. The landowner's complaint was not filed until 2007. Therefore, the ordinance was conclusively valid under Minn. Stat. § 599.13 (2006) and not subject to challenge based on alleged notice and publication defects under Minn. Stat. § 462.357, subd. 3 (1988), and Minn. Stat. § 375.51, subd. 3 (1988). The landowner's inverse condemnation claim was barred by the six-year limitations period. His evidence of other advertisements in the area was legally insufficient to sustain a discriminatory-enforcement claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the county.

 

1616 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Larson


A07-2145


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1525



December 30, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Larson, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 232 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Carlton County District Court File No. CR-06-3146.
State v. Larson, 2006 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 235 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by a jury in the Carlton County District Court (Minnesota) for two counts of failure to register as a predatory offender in violation of Minn. Stat. § 243.166, subd. 5 (2006). The district court sentenced appellant to 30 months and 40 months, respectively, to be served concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to convict him because the State failed to prove that his time to register had elapsed and because he was not required to register with his prison case manager. The court held that § 243.166, subd. 3a, concerned offender registration when a person lacked a primary address. For defendant to claim that the incorrect person sought his compliance with the law put form over substance. Defendant was required by law to register as a sex offender, and he did not. Defendant next argued that by filing his 1994 Bureau of Criminal Apprehension (BCA) registration form, he was no longer required to comply with the statute (i.e., the time period in which he was required to register ended in 2004). The court held that this 1994 form, filled out by defendant's correction agent, required defendant's signature, among other things, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 243.166, subd. 4, and defendant did not comply with any of these requirements, including a fingerprint, a photograph, and a consent form. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to convict defendant. The court also rejected defendant's double jeopardy claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions. However, the court reversed the sentences and remanded for consideration of defendant's correct score under the correct sentencing guidelines.

 

1617 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Oates v. State


A07-2169


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1516



December 30, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Oates v. State, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 207 (Mar. 17, 2009)
Petition denied by, Review denied by State v. Oates (In re Oates), 2009 Minn. LEXIS 323 (May 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 98124740.
State v. Oates, 611 N.W.2d 580, 2000 Minn. App. LEXIS 600 (June 20, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of assault under Minn. Stat. § 609.11 (1998) in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota). The conviction was affirmed on appeal in 2000. Defendant filed four petitions for postconviction relief, all of which were denied. He filed his fifth petition in 2007. The district court denied the postconviction petition in its entirety, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose out of a nightclub shooting. He was sentenced in 1999 under § 609.11, which provided a mandatory minimum sentence for each conviction of second-degree assault with a deadly weapon. Defendant argued that a jury should have determined the aggravating factors, such as sentencing enhancement and mandatory minimum statutes, beyond a reasonable doubt. Minn. Stat. § 609.11 was modified in 2006 to require the finding that a defendant used a dangerous weapon be made by the jury; defendant argued that the amendment should be applied retroactively. However, the court held that defendant not receive an upward departure in his sentence; therefore, the Blakely rule and Minn. Stat. § 244.10 did not apply to defendant's sentences. Moreover, in convicting defendant, the jury found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant assaulted the victims with a dangerous weapon, a firearm. Therefore, the sentence imposed was based on jury findings, not on the judicial finding under § 609.11. The court held that many of defendant's were barred because they could have been brought on direct appeal, because they were brought in a previous petition, or because they were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's summary denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief.

 

1618 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Schroeder v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety


A07-2247


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1498



December 23, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Schroeder v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 216 (Minn., Mar. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Cass County District Court File No. 11-CV-07-1550.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Commissioner of Public Safety revoked appellant driver's license under the implied-consent law after he was stopped by a police officer and refused to take a breath test. The driver petitioned for review of his license revocation. The Cass County District Court, Minnesota, sustained the license revocation. The driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the driver contended his right to counsel was violated because what he said to his attorney was not only heard but recorded; he argued that the police officer violated his constitutional rights when he did not turn off the recording device while he was contacting his attorney on the telephone. The appellate court disagreed, holding that the driver was not entitled to a private telephone conversation; thus, his limited right to counsel was fully vindicated notwithstanding the officer's recording of the driver's side of the conversation. Further, the driver did not dispute that he was read the implied-consent advisory and informed of his right to consult with an attorney. The record indicated that he did not ask the officer to stop recording his statements, which would have given the officer an opportunity to address the driver's concerns. Under these circumstances, the appellate court concluded that the drivers right to counsel was vindicated and there was no statutory or constitutional basis for rescinding the license revocation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1619 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Masieniec


A07-2390


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1505



December 23, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Masieniec, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 71 (2009)
Related proceeding at Masieniec v. State, 2010 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 694 (Minn. Ct. App., July 20, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
St. Louis County District Court File No. CR-06-1324.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a Lothenbach proceeding, the St. Louis County District Court, Minnesota, found defendant guilty of possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, in the second degree in violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.022, subd. 2(1) (2006). Defendant challenged the district court's denial of his pretrial motion to suppress evidence obtained by an allegedly illegal entry, search, and seizure.


OVERVIEW: The officers observed a young woman tending flowers near the front door of the residence. The officers first asked the woman if defendant was there; she said she did not know. The officers then asked if defendant's father was home, and she told the officers that he was inside and that they could go inside to speak to him. The Court of Appeals of Minnesota concluded that the facts available to the officers did not afford them reasonable grounds to believe that the woman had common authority over the premises. Accordingly, the resulting seizure of defendant and the evidence ultimately obtained after execution of a search warrant, which was based upon facts obtained after the illegal entry into the home, were constitutionally invalid and had to suppressed.


OUTCOME: The district court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress was reversed.

State v. Johnson


A07-1903


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1465



December 16, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
McLeod County District Court File No. CR-06-924.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the McLeod County District Court (Minnesota) of first-degree controlled substance crime, possession of methamphetamine, under Minn. Stat. § 152.021, subd. 2(1) (2006), and fifth-degree controlled substance crime, possession of marijuana, under Minn. Stat. § 152.025, subd. 2(1) (2006). He was sentenced to 81 months for the first-degree offense; no sentence was imposed for the fifth-degree offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: An officer obtained information that defendant was engaged in drug dealing from two confidential reliable informants, one of whom made a controlled purchase of a substance containing amphetamine from defendant. The officer searched garbage containers outside defendant's home that were partially on the curb and partially on the end of the driveway. He found empty rolling paper containers, plastic baggies and corners of plastic baggies, evidence of drug use, green stems, green leaves, and a substance that later tested positive for THC. Based on this information, the officer obtained a warrant for a no-knock search of defendant's home. The court rejected defendant's argument that the search of his garbage was unconstitutional because the containers sat partially on his driveway. Defendant still had no reasonable expectation of privacy. The court held that the information of the two informants, the controlled buy, and the garbage search all provided probable cause for the warrant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence.

State v. Beutz


A07-1526


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1399



December 9, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Mille Lacs County District Court File No. K104778.
State v. Beutz, 2006 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 60 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Mille Lacs County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted her of four counts of first-degree controlled-substance crime, fourth-degree controlled-substance crime, and use of a police radio during a crime.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from her conviction of four counts of first-degree controlled-substance crime, fourth-degree controlled-substance crime, and use of a police radio during a crime, defendant argued that the district court erred in rejecting her Batson challenge to the peremptory strike of a Native American veniremember and abused its discretion by allowing the state to introduce Spreigl evidence. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that the district court did not commit clear error in upholding the peremptory strike. Defendant overlooked the fact that the State did not inquire about the circumstances surrounding any of the convictions disclosed by the veniremembers, and the veniremember in question was the only veniremember who had a close family member with multiple criminal convictions. Moreover, the district court found that the venireman might have had "some possible knowledge" of the case after reading a news article. Further, the appellate court was satisfied that the Spreigl evidence was relevant for the purposes of proving knowledge of the drug operations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1622 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mikkelson


A08-1245


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1429



December 9, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Stearns County District Court File No. 73-K9-06-004263.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Stearns County District Court (Minnesota) denying his pretrial motion to suppress evidence obtained as a result of a traffic stop. Defendant was subsequently convicted of committing a controlled substance crime in the first degree under Minn. Stat. §152.021 (2006).


OVERVIEW: A trooper stopped defendant's car after seeing it weave within its own lane and cross the fog line. After becoming suspicious that defendant was under the influence of a controlled substance, the trooper requested and received defendant's consent to search his car, which yielded drug paraphernalia and cocaine. On appeal, the court held that the trooper's request to search defendant's car was not an unconstitutional expansion of the stop because, even though he may have begun the traffic stop with a hunch insufficient to form a basis for reasonable suspicion that drug use was afoot, he did not ask to expand the search until after making further observations of defendant's behavior and motor skills at close proximity and determining that defendant's behavior and apparent impairment were not the result of being under the influence of alcohol. Defendant had multiple signs of impairment, including weaving and crossing the fog line while driving, slow and deliberate movements, and confusion. There were other suspicious factors, including copious cigarette smoke emanating from defendant's car, his refusal to make eye contact, and his nervous fidgeting and scratching.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

1623 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Craig v. State


A07-1949


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1409



December 9, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-CR-07-043231.
State v. Craig, 2007 Minn. Dist. LEXIS 194 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, denying his postconviction petition to withdraw his guilty plea to the misdemeanor offense of disorderly conduct. Amici curiae filed an amicus brief challenging the constitutionality of the disorderly conduct statute, Minn. Stat. § 609.72, subd. 1(3) (2006).


OVERVIEW: The complaint stated that appellant peered into a restroom stall occupied by an officer who observed appellant tap his foot several times and move his foot closer to the stall occupied by the officer. Appellant moved his right foot so that it touched the officer's left foot; appellant was within the stall area of the stall occupied by the officer. Appellant was convicted on a plea of guilty to disorderly conduct. Without a transcript of the plea proceeding, it could not be determined whether the district court erred by denying appellant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea. The failure of the complaint to acknowledge entrapment as a defense based on the officer's conduct did not justify withdrawal of the guilty plea. In postconviction proceedings, the Court of Appeals of Minnesota upheld the constitutionality of the disorderly conduct statute against an overbreadth challenge. Appellant's conduct was invasive of the privacy of another and could be prohibited as disorderly conduct under Minn. Stat. § 609.72, subd. 1(3). The disorderly conduct statute did not require that anyone other than the officer be disturbed by appellant's conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1624 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hotzler


A07-1575


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1388



December 2, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Hotzler, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 99 (Minn., Feb. 25, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Mower County District Court File No. 50-CR-06-3193.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Mower County District Court, Minnesota, found defendant guilty of second-degree burglary, third-degree burglary, possession of burglary or theft tools, and fleeing a peace officer in a motor vehicle. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the burglary convictions under Minn. Stat. § 609.582 (2006). The evidence showed that defendant was the only person near a scrap yard when police arrived soon after someone or something triggered a silent alarm. Someone had cut a gate chain, and police found bolt cutters in defendant's car, which was parked at that same gate. The warehouse door had been opened and a forklift driven from the warehouse out into the scrap yard loaded with a box of copper. Defendant fled the scene. The court also held that none of the acts of prosecutorial misconduct alleged by defendant merited reversal. Counsel was potentially rendered ineffective under Minn. Const. art. I, § 6 by conceding guilt on the charge of fleeing a peace officer in both the opening statement and closing argument, but the court could not determine on the appellate record whether defendant consented or acquiesced. Finally, a consecutive sentence for possession of burglary tools was vacated because it arose out of the same behavioral incident as the burglary and thus violated Minn. Stat. § 609.035, subd. 1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed on the issue of consecutive sentences for burglary and possession of burglary tools, vacated the sentence for possession of burglary tools, and remanded for the district court to amend the sentence. The court otherwise affirmed the judgment.

 

1625 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baumgart


A07-1726


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1359



November 25, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Clay County District Court File No. TX-07-1620.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Clay County District Court (Minnesota) that convicted him of driving while impaired, arguing that the district court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained from a warrantless search of his residence.


OVERVIEW: A witness reported to police that pickup truck collided with a street-light pole, left the scene, and drove to a residence. After an investigating officer learned that defendant's brother was listed as the property owner/occupant, he contacted the brother and informed him of the accident. The brother arrived at the home and admitted the officer. The brother went to defendant's bedroom to see if he needed medical attention; the officer followed the brother, observed that defendant was intoxicated, and arrested defendant. On review, the court held that the search was permissible under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Minn. Const. art. I, § 10, because the brother consented. The brother was listed with the utility company as the owner/occupant of the residence, told the officer that he lived at the residence, voluntarily met the officer at the house, had a key and unlocked the door, and led the officer directly to defendant's bedroom. In light of these facts, it was reasonable for the officer to conclude that the brother had authority to consent to the warrantless entry and search of the residence. Therefore, the brother validly consented to the entry and search of defendant's residence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Rinzin v. Olmsted County Hous. & Redevelopment Auth.


A07-2344


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1371



November 25, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Olmsted County Housing and Redevelopment Authority.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator father sought review of the decision of a hearing officer of respondent Olmsted County Housing and Redevelopment Authority (OCHRA) that the father was ineligible to participate in the Section 8 rental-assistance program.


OVERVIEW: The father's daughter continued to live with the family, and her income made the family ineligible for Section 8 assistance. The daughter testified that she moved out of her parents home, but upon learning that her family was excluded from the Section 8 program, she moved back in with her family. The issue was whether the determination by the OCHRA hearing officer that the father's family was not income-eligible for public housing assistance was supported by substantial evidence. The single dispositive question was whether there was substantial evidence for the hearing officer to conclude that the daughter was residing in the father's unit on a certain date. The father and the daughter testified that the daughter had moved out of the home. There was no evidence at the hearing that daughter was actually living in the home on September 1. OCHRA and the hearing officer proceeded on the assumption that, absent the requested documentary evidence of a move, the daughter was still there, and she intended to stay. The hearing officer's decision was unsupported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the decision.

Froehle v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety


A07-2299


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1353



November 18, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Aitkin County District Court File No. 01CV07309.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order from the Aitkin County District Court (Minnesota), which sustained the revocation of his driver's license by respondent, the Minnesota Commissioner of Public Safety.


OVERVIEW: A police officer arrived at the scene of petitioner's single all-terrain vehicle accident. The officer observed petitioner to be somewhat incoherent. The officer noticed that petitioner had an odor of alcohol emitting from him. While petitioner was in the hospital, the officer, concluding that petitioner was incapable of responding to a request for a blood draw, ordered a blood-alcohol test. Petitioner's driver's license was revoked due to the results of the blood test. On appeal, the court found that the one-vehicle accident, in combination with the indications of intoxication observed by the officer, supported a finding of probable cause to suspect that petitioner was driving while intoxicated. The implied consent statute, Minn. Stat. § 169A.51, subd. 1(a) (2006), was constitutional and was constitutionally applied in the case. The trial court's finding that the Commissioner made a prima facie case that the test result was reliable under Minn. Stat. § 634.15, subds. 1(b) and 2 was supported by evidence that a medical technologist administered the blood draw, a Minnesota Bureau of Criminal Apprehension (BCA) kit was used, and the sample was analyzed by the BCA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Larson


A07-0146


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1336



November 18, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Larson, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 233 (Minn., Mar. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Aitkin County District Court File No. K6-04-4.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Aitkin County District Court (Minnesota) of first-degree controlled-substance crime (attempted manufacture). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the deputy conducted an unlawful pat frisk because there was no evidence that defendant was armed, dangerous, or posed a threat to the officers. The court of appeals disagreed. A limited protective frisk of defendant was justified under the circumstances. It was early in the morning and there were only two officers present at the time of the pat frisk. One of the passengers in defendant's car had an active warrant for her arrest, had escaped from a locked squad car just moments before the pat frisk, and her whereabouts were unknown. The deputies suspected that defendant and others might have aided the prisoner's escape. The deputy reasonably believed that defendant had tried to distract him during the vehicle search by continually interrupting and by failing to follow directions to stand back. The deputy had also discovered an open container of alcohol and a butane torch in defendant's vehicle. Those facts reasonably implied that defendant might have been involved in more dangerous criminal activity and might have presented a threat to the officers' safety.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Denham v. State


A07-2268


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1313



November 10, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Denham v. State, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 18 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 98013930.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: In 1998, the inmate entered guilty pleas to two counts of first-degree criminal sexual conduct. At the sentencing hearing, the prosecutor identified aggravating factors warranting an upward departure from the sentencing guidelines, which included invasion of the victims' zone of privacy, multiple penetrations, presence of a child, and the repeated stabbing of one of the victims. The district court stated why it thought an upward departure was appropriate, and then it adopted the reasons given by the prosecutor. Later, the inmate sought postconviction relief. The request was denied, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the district court was required to state its reasons for a departure on the record, pursuant to Minn. R. Crim. P. 27.03, subd. 4(C) and the Williams case. This standard was satisfied in this case. Moreover, the plea agreement alone was sufficient to support an upward departure in this case because the Misquadace decision applied only prospectively. An issue relating to the failure to state severe aggravating circumstances not presented to the district court. Finally, the Blakely decision did not apply retroactively.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1630 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Bailey v. Minn. Pollution Control Agency


A07-2255


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1323



November 4, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Lake of the Woods County District Court File No. 39-C5-04-000209.
Bailey v. United States Army Corps of Eng'rs, 2002 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 23272 (D. Minn., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged a summary judgment entered by the Lake of the Woods County District Court, Minnesota, which dismissed his taking and negligent and intentional misrepresentation claims against respondents, a county, the Minnesota Pollution Control Agency (MPCA), and the Minnesota Department of Natural Resources (DNR). The case centered on the landowner's efforts to develop his property and the regulation of wetlands on the property.


OVERVIEW: The court held that summary judgment for the county was appropriate under both a categorical and an ad hoc taking analysis under U.S. Const. amend. V and Minn. Const. art. I, § 13 because the landowner failed to raise genuine issues of material fact regarding whether his entire 86-acre parcel was rendered valueless and whether he was deprived of all reasonable use of his parcel. The landowner's misrepresentation claims were barred under the doctrine of res judicata. Even if the claims were not barred, summary judgment was appropriate based on the county's defense of official and vicarious immunity. The trial court did not err in granting judgment as a matter of law for the DNR because the landowner failed to raise a genuine issue of material fact as to the complete diminution in value, or elimination of all reasonable use, of his entire property. Similarly, the landowner's claim that the order for fill removal deprived him of the right to access to his property via a public road was without merit. Because the MPCA's revocation of the certification under 33 U.S.C.S. § 1341 was an effort to prevent a nuisance and potential harm to human health, no taking occurred as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1631 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Hippler v. State


A07-2020


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1291



October 28, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Hippler v. State, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 699 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by , , 2009 U.S. LEXIS 3936 (U.S., May 26, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. KX03814.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner pleaded guilty to third-degree criminal sexual conduct, subsequently failed to appear at the scheduled sentencing hearing, and was later sentenced to the presumptive 33-month term, followed by a five-year conditional-release period. The petitioner sought postconviction relief challenging the imposition of the conditional-release period. The Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, denied the petition, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the petitioner contended the district court erred in denying him postconviction relief when the five years of conditional release were not part of his earlier plea agreement, and the imposition of the five-year conditional-release period violated his constitutional rights under Blakely. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that it was undisputed that the petitioner pleaded guilty to third-degree criminal sexual conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.344, subds. 1(b), 2 (2002). Thus, the imposition of the five-year conditional-release period was mandatory. His claim that his plea was not intelligent failed because he was deemed to have been aware of the law since it was enhanced several years before he entered his plea, and he failed to object to the imposition of the conditional-release term at sentencing. Because the petitioner's sentence was final before the ruling in Blakely, and because Blakely did not apply retroactively, the petitioner was not entitled to benefit from the rule in Blakely. Moreover, even if Blakely applied retroactively to the petitioner's sentence, the conditional-release period did not constitute an upward departure.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1632 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Muraski


A07-1705


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1231



October 21, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part, Review denied by, in part State v. Muraski, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 722 (2008)
Review denied by State v. Muraski, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 202 (Minn., Mar. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Washington County District Court File No. K3-06-1589.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota) convicting him for refusing to submit to chemical testing, under Minn. Stat. § 169A.20, subd. 2 (2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the test-refusal statute, under Minn. Stat. § 169A.20, subd. 2 (2006), violated the Fourth Amendment prohibition against unreasonable searches and seizures. The court held that Minn. Stat. § 169A.20, subd. 2, did not authorize an unreasonable search and did not condition a privilege on surrendering a constitutional right. Defendant also argued that the test-refusal statute violated his constitutional right to privacy. The test-refusal statute served the State's compelling interest in protecting residents from intoxicated drivers and provided officers with the means to test those that they had probable cause to believe drove while intoxicated. The balancing test favored intrusion by the State on the privacy rights held by defendant. The court also held that the State could use defendant's prior unchallenged license revocations to enhance the current charge without violating his due-process rights. A prior impaired-driving-related loss of license was a qualified prior impaired-driving incident for enhancement purposes, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169A.03, subd. 22 (2006).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

State v. Farleigh


A07-1872


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1199



October 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Review denied by State v. Farleigh, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 696 (Minn., Dec. 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Aitkin County District Court File No. 01-T3-06-3060.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Aitkin County District Court, Minnesota, found defendant guilty of failure to provide proof of insurance, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 169.791 (2006). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped while driving another individual's pickup truck, was unable to produce evidence that the truck was insured, and he did not disclose to the deputy the owner's name and address. He argued that Minn. Stat. § 169.791 (2006)--the no-proof-of-insurance law--was unconstitutional on its face and as it applied to a driver of a motor vehicle owned by someone else. The reviewing court disagreed. The legislature could properly define a non-owner driver's failure to provide proof of insurance as a strict liability crime, and it could condition the State's need to prove scienter on a pre-arraignment defense notice of the owner's identity. The court also held that defendant had waived his due process argument by failing to raise it in the trial court but considered the issue in the interests of justice, as permitted by Minn. R. Crim. P. 28.02 subd. 11, because the constitutionality of the provision had not been taken up before, as related to a defendant who was not the owner of the vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1634 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hosley


A07-1017


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1104



September 30, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Hosley, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 674 (Minn., Dec. 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 05073277.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) of first-degree criminal sexual conduct, third-degree criminal sexual conduct, and kidnapping. Defendant appealed, challenging his conviction of first-degree criminal sexual conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree criminal sexual conduct in an attack on the victim. The court affirmed. The trial court acted within its discretion in admitting evidence under Minn. R. Evid. 609(a). Through the admission of a false-imprisonment conviction in conjunction with three crimes of dishonesty, the jury was in a better position to evaluate defendant's credibility as a repeat offender, the false imprisonment conviction was less than 10 years old, and defendant's credibility was an important issue in the case. The prosecutor's statement that it was "every woman's worst nightmare" was improper, but the likelihood of prejudice to defendant was remote because the evidence against defendant was strong and reversal was not required. For purposes of Minn. R. Evid. 404(b), evidence of a prior sexual assault was relevant to the State's case. The similarities between the prior assault and current assault were sufficient to permit admission of the prior assault. Witnesses testified that exhibits fairly and accurately represented the victim's injuries and the floor plan of her apartment, and thus there was proper authentication for purposes of Minn. R. Evid. 901(a), (b)(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Acosta


A07-1709


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1117



September 30, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Acosta, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 714 (Minn., Dec. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota County District Court File No. K4-06-1470.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Dakota County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of one count of controlled substance crime in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was unreasonably detained by the officers and the subsequent search of his vehicle was not justified because the officers lacked probable cause. Specifically, defendant argued that the officers lacked probable cause to believe that his vehicle contained cocaine, because the tip from the informant was stale and therefore, the detention and search were unlawful. The appellate court ruled that the tip was not stale, and that the officers had probable cause to believe that defendant's vehicle contained cocaine based on the detailed and credible information the informant provided. The information provided by the informant indicated that there was ongoing criminal activity, selling two kilos of cocaine. A lapse of approximately 24 hours between when two individuals in the vehicle solicited the informant to purchase cocaine and the search of a matching vehicle driven by defendant did not preclude a probable-cause determination. Since the officers had probable cause to believe that the vehicle contained cocaine, the district court properly determined that it was reasonable for the officers to detain defendant while waiting for the drug-sniff dog.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1636 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Weiland


A07-1553


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1071



September 9, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Weiland, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 598 (Minn., Oct. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Jackson County District Court File No. KO-04-1089.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Jackson County District Court, Minnesota, revoking his probation and executing his 48-month sentence for driving while impaired (DWI).


OVERVIEW: In 2005, the district court imposed a 48-month prison sentence on defendant after he pled guilty to a charge of driving while impaired, but the district court stayed execution of the sentence and placed defendant on probation. In 2007, the district court revoked the stay and executed the sentence. Defendant appealed, challenging the district court's findings of fact and its ultimate decision to revoke the stay. The appellate court ruled that the district court did not abuse its discretion by revoking defendant's probation and executing his prison sentence. The record reflected that defendant had five prior DWI convictions. The record reflected that defendant had been on probation on at least two prior occasions. Although the district court could have imposed jail time in response to the probation violations, it was not unreasonable to decline to do so in light of defendant's multiple probation violations and his recidivist behavior. Thus, the district court did not abuse its discretion by concluding that the need for confinement outweighed the policies favoring probation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1637 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Taveras


A07-0747


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1072



September 9, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Taveras, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 585 (Minn., Oct. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Becker County District Court File No. K0-06-1154.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Becker County District Court (Minnesota) that convicted him of two counts of first-degree controlled substance crime based upon his purchase of cocaine, arguing that the district court erred in denying his motion to suppress because the security guards who searched his tent at a music festival were acting as agents of the state and conducted their search in the absence of defendant's consent.


OVERVIEW: Security guards employed by operators of a music festival saw defendant approach a man they suspected of selling cocaine. Three security guards followed defendant to his tent and eventually requested permission to search the tent. After the search uncovered 90 grams of cocaine, the security guards handed defendant over to the county sheriff's department. On review of defendant's conviction, the court concluded that the district court did not err in denying defendant's suppression motion because the security guards could not be viewed as acting as state agents where there was no showing that the government knew of and acquiesced in the search and where the search was not conducted to assist law enforcement efforts. The evidence established that the county sheriff's department did not know of or acquiesce in the search; the county sheriff's department did not have a role in hiring the security firm, nor did it have control over the security guards. Further, the search was conducted for private purposes; the searches were largely conducted to shield the festival operators from liability, not to assist any local law enforcement agency.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

1638 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Alford


A07-1025


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1053



September 2, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Alford, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 596 (Minn., Oct. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. K0-06-318.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) of two counts of second-degree murder and the lesser-included offense of accomplice after the fact. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the district court abused its discretion in denying his request to modify the jury instruction regarding defense of others from a "reasonable person" standard to a "reasonable juvenile" standard. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant's requested modification was not an accurate statement of current law in Minnesota. Even if the district court erred in denying defendant's requested instruction, that error was harmless. Defendant was given wide latitude to present his theory of the case, which was that he acted in defense of his brother. But little evidence was presented from which the jury could have concluded that defendant's actions were reasonable for a juvenile but not reasonable for an adult. Defendant did more than just get the victim off the brother: he admitted to police that he hit the victim with a hammer, stabbed him with a barbeque fork, and kicked him. The physical evidence showed that the victim sustained multiple, severe injuries, some of which were consistent with having been beaten with the metal rod on which defendant's bloody fingerprints were found.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1639 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Dahlstrom v. Robbinson


A07-1740


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 967



August 12, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-CV-06-22122. Hon. Heidi S. Schellhas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant potential buyer of real estate sued respondent sellers, alleging they had breached the purchase agreements by refusing to convey the properties to her. The Hennepin County District Court granted the sellers' summary-judgment motion, concluding that the buyer failed to satisfy the conditions precedent of the purchase agreements. The buyer appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the buyer contended the trial court erred in granting summary judgment to the sellers. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the parties' purchase agreements required the buyer to provide the sellers with a letter from a bona fide mortgage lender indicating that the lender had reviewed the buyer's credit report and that the buyer was preapproved to purchase the properties; but there was no evidence that the buyer met this condition precedent. Further, the financing addendum to each purchase agreement required the buyer to provide the sellers with evidence that she had secured financing by a certain date. Each addendum specified that if the buyer failed to comply with this term, the sellers had the right to terminate the purchase agreement by giving the buyer written notice of their intent to do so. Because the buyer failed to satisfy the condition precedent regarding financing, she was not entitled to any relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1640 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Schneider v. State


A07-1569


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 912



August 5, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-FA-07-1874. Hon. Patricia Kerr Karasov.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandparents sought review of an order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed their petition against respondents, State, county human services and public health department, and adoptive parents, for visitation with their grandchildren pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 257C.08, subd. 4 (2006).


OVERVIEW: The grandchildren had lived with their mother and the grandparents until they were placed in foster care. The foster care parents were an uncle and his wife and were the adoptive parents. On appeal, the court held that the district court had to grant a petition for third-party visitation if it found that (1) visitation rights would be in the best interests of the children; (2) the grandparents and the grandchildren had established emotional ties creating a parent and child relationship; and (3) visitation rights would not interfere with the relationship between the adoptive parents and the grandchildren. Minn. Stat. § 257C.08, subd. 4(1)--(3) (2006). Although the documents filed by the grandparents presented a basis for their claims under factor one and factor two, the grandparents did not address factor three. Furthermore, the court did not agree with the grandparents' assertion that on the day set for the hearing the district court was only going to consider the county's motion to dismiss for lack of standing. Accordingly, the court held that the district court did not abuse its discretion by dismissing the petition before conducting an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order.

In re Welfare of C. P. T.


A07-1405


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 929



August 5, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Carver County District Court File No. 10-JV-05-972. Hon. Kevin W. Eide.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a decision from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which adjudicated him delinquent for an offense of criminal sexual conduct and thus, required him to register as a predatory sex offender under Minn. Stat. § 243.166 (2004).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile asserted that the district court abused its discretion in adjudicating him a delinquent. In addition, the juvenile challenged the constitutionality of § 243.166. He argued that it violated due process and the doctrine of the separation of powers. On appeal, the court held that the district court did not abuse its discretion when it adjudicated the juvenile delinquent on the charge of third-degree criminal sexual conduct as the adjudication was based on admissions by the juvenile and several violations of the juvenile's probation, including two new offenses involving inappropriate sexual conduct. Furthermore, the violations were of core conditions of probation such as completion of sexual-offender training and remaining law abiding with no sexual offenses. In addition, the court held that § 243.166 requiring lifetime registration was to not punitive as applied to juveniles because it did not violate the due process clauses of the U.S. Constitution or the Minnesota Constitution or the separation of powers doctrine of the Minnesota Constitution, Minn. Const. art. III, § 1. Accordingly, § 243.1966 was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.
