Hess v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety


A07-1361, A08-0166


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 868



July 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Hess v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 551 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Lyon County District Court File No. 42-CV-07-32, CR-07-16. Hon. George I. Harrelson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, defendant challenged a decision from the Lyon County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of second-degree driving while impaired (DWI) and third-degree DWI. He also challenged the revocation of his driver's license for refusal to submit to a chemical test.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant for committing a traffic violation. A preliminary breath test showed that defendant had an alcohol concentration of.139. Defendant refused to submit for further field sobriety tests. He was arrested and later convicted for DWI. The revocation of his driver's license was also sustained. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that defendant did not reasonably refuse to submit to a chemical test under Minn. Stat. § 169A.53, subd. 3(c) (2006). Defendant did not show that he intended to plead guilty at the time that he refused testing, and he failed to enter a guilty plea at the first available opportunity. As to the constitutionality argument regarding forfeiture, defendant failed to indicate which provision of the constitution Minn. Stat. § 169A.63 (2006) allegedly violated. At any rate, the statute had been established as constitutional under both the United States and Minnesota Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1643 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wencl


A07-0954


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 870



July 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Wencl, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 535 (Minn., Sept. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Steele County District Court File No. 74-KO-06-563. Hon. Casey J. Christian.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Steele County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of three counts of being a felon in possession of an explosive device.


OVERVIEW: After several explosions involving similar devices, defendant was charged with three counts of violating Minn. Stat. § 609.668, subd. 2(b) (2004). Defendant was convicted, and he sought review. In affirming, the appellate court rejected the argument that the MacGyver bombs used in this case were not explosive devices because they did not produce destructive effects. It was not necessary to show that the bombs actually produced the destructive effects; to meet the definition of an explosive device, it was only necessary that the device be capable of doing so. The evidence at trial established that the bombs were capable of producing destructive effects. There was testimony that any MacGyver bomb that exploded was capable of causing destructive effects if it went off near a person or highly flammable material. Moreover, there was other testimony from witnesses about the effect of a bomb actually created by defendant. A vagueness argument was waived because it was presented for the first time on appeal. Finally, the district court's decision that the convictions did not arise from a single behavioral incident was not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1644 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Branson


A07-0987, A07-1184


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 871



July 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Sub nomine at State v. Molick, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 542 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 07-006157. Hon. Gary R. Larson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, defendants challenged rulings from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) which denied their motions to suppress evidence of intoxication obtained during a joint stop of defendants for operating their snowmobiles in excess of the legal speed limit.


OVERVIEW: The arresting officer did not use a radar or laser device to determine the speed of the snowmobiles before concluding that defendants were violating the speed limit and stopping them. He testified that his conclusion was based on his experience visually estimating speeds and verifying those estimates with a radar or laser device. The court held that the stop was not unreasonable under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Minn. Const. art. I, § 10. The arresting officer had a reasonable, articulable suspicion that defendants were exceeding the speed limit, based on his observation of the snowmobiles and his training and experience in law enforcement. Misstatements within the district court's conclusions of law constituted harmless error under Minn. R. Crim. P. 31.01. Although one defendant passed field sobriety tests, there was probable cause for arrest based on his slurred speech and odor of alcohol. An alleged failure to provide posted notice of the speed limit did not affect the reasonableness of the stop. Testimony that was premised on misrepresentation of the officer's testimony and challenged its reasonableness was properly excluded as irrelevant under Minn. R. Evid. 401.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's denial of defendants' motions to suppress evidence.

 

1645 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. LaFon


A07-0708


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 848



July 15, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Crow Wing County District Court File No. T4-04-7076. Hon. David J. Teneyck, Hon. John M. Roue and Hon. Richard A. Zimmerman.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a neighbor complained to the sheriff about a lakefront dock on the owner's property, the State charged defendant, the owner's son, of violating a county water-surface-use ordinance. The Crow Wing County District Court, Minnesota, found defendant guilty and sentenced him to 30 days in jail, but stayed the sentence for one year on the condition that he remove the dock or confine it to the property's riparian zone. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant raised several issues challenging the constitutionality of the ordinance, arguing that it violated the owner's right to continue a preexisting, nonconforming use, and that the State failed to prove that defendant engaged in any conduct that violated the ordinance. The appellate court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutional as it did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause, was not unconstitutionally vague, and was not unreasonable. Statutory authorization for regulation of the placement of docks was not defeated by the fact that the ordinance and the enabling state statute used slightly different language. Because the surface water and lakebed were held in trust by the State, the owner did not, by prescription, acquire a property right to the current location of the dock. However, the appellate court agreed that the district court erred by finding defendant guilty as the prosecution infringed on the owner's right to continue a preexisting, lawful, nonconforming use, and the evidence was insufficient to prove that defendant engaged in conduct amounting to a failure to "confine" the dock to his father's (the owner's) riparian zone.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1646 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Griffin v. State


A07-1539


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 793



July 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 02101945. Hon. William R. Howard.
State v. Griffin, 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 994 (Minn. Ct. App., Aug. 31, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) of first-degree criminal sexual conduct, kidnapping to facilitate a felony or flight thereafter, and kidnapping resulting in great bodily harm or terrorizing the victim. Following an appeal and resentencing, petitioner sought postconviction relief. The district court denied petitioner's motion, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner first argued that his mandatory minimum sentence of 144 months' imprisonment was unconstitutional because it constituted an upward departure without a jury determination in violation of Blakely. The court rejected this argument because, under Minn. Stat. § 609.342, subd. 2(b), the only fact essential to the imposition of a 144-month sentence was conviction of first-degree criminal sexual conduct. When the jury convicted petitioner of first-degree criminal sexual conduct, it also found the relevant facts for sentencing as required by Blakely. Similarly, a five-year conditional-release period of Minn. Stat. § 609.109, subd. 7 (2002), was authorized on the basis of the jury verdict and did not require any additional findings of fact to be made by the district court. Because the sentence imposed complied with Blakely decision, petitioner's counsel did not have a legal basis to object to the sentence. Therefore, petitioner's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of petitioner's motion for postconviction relief.

Bucknell v. County of Fillmore


A07-1768


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 762



July 1, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Bucknell v. County of Fillmore, 2010 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 249 (Minn. Ct. App., Mar. 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Fillmore County District Court File No. 23-C2-04-000695. Hon. James A. Fabian.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent property owners sued defendant county and appellant township in a zoning matter. The Fillmore County District Court, Minnesota, denied cross-motions for summary judgment. The township appealed, and the property owners filed a notice of review.


OVERVIEW: The property owners sought a conditional-use permit to create a subdivision. The property owners also sought a zoning variance. The township instituted an interim zoning ordinance, and the property owners later moved to amend their complaint. The district court issued an order that denied the request to add new claims against the township. Three issues were raised: (1) what was the relationship between the township and the county with respect to zoning authority; (2) whether the property owners and the township lacked standing because the township was no longer a party; (3) whether the claims the property owners raised were moot because the interim ordinance was replaced by a final ordinance. The appellate court determined that the two entities had independent zoning authority; therefore, the property owners' argument that the township had no power to act was rejected. As to standing, there was no basis for the determination that the township was dismissed from the suit. Finally, if the district court had a basis for concluding the claims against the interim zoning ordinance were moot, it would have no basis for denying leave to amend the complaint.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment, and the matter was remanded.

Frazier v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety


A07-0997, A07-1004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 773



July 1, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Mille Lacs County District Court File No. 48-CV-07-183. Hon. Randall J. Slieter.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver was arrested for driving while intoxicated (DWI) and brought a suppression motion prior to both the implied-consent hearing and his criminal trial. These motions were denied. The Mille Lacs County District Court, Minnesota, then sustained respondent Commissioner of Public Safety's revocation of the driver's driver's license and subsequently found him guilty of DWI in a bench trial. The driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: In a consolidated appeal, the driver challenged the district court's order sustaining the revocation of his driver's license and the subsequent (DWI) conviction, arguing that the arresting police officer did not have a reasonable, articulable suspicion to stop and detain him. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the officer was justified in stopping the driver's vehicle because the license plate was partially obstructed by snow, making it impossible for the officer to read the license plate or see the license tabs from his squad car; this violated Minn. Stat. § 169.79 (2006) and constituted a reasonable basis for the traffic stop. The driver had an affirmative duty to keep his bumper and license plate free of snow, especially since it had stopped snowing for several hours. Further, the traffic violation justifying the stop was not rectified prior to the officer's making contact with the driver. The driver was not unlawfully detained because he first gave the officer his wife's license, only gave his license after the officer's prompting, smelled of alcohol, and admitted to being at a bar and having several beers before driving.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Stevens v. Ludeman


A07-1195


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 764



July 1, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Review denied by Stevens v. Ludeman, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 503 (Sept. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Nicollet County District Court File No. CV06423. Hon. Allison Krehbiel-Baskfield.
Stevens v. State, 1997 Minn. App. LEXIS 403 (Minn. Ct. App., Apr. 8, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient was indeterminately committed as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) to the Minnesota Sex Offender Program (MSOP), and his direct appeal of his commitment was dismissed as untimely. The patient subsequently filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus challenging his continued confinement. The Nicollet County District Court, Minnesota, granted respondent Commissioner of Human Services' motion to dismiss. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient contended sex-offender treatment would not be provided until he forfeited his U.S. Const. amend. V right against self-incrimination, and there was insufficient evidence that he suffered from a mental disorder. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the patient failed to demonstrate that he necessarily had to incriminate himself to participate in treatment or that he had suffered any consequences related to a failure to self-incriminate. He also did not demonstrate compulsion to trigger a claim of violation of his Fifth Amendment privilege as he did not identify any adverse consequence or disciplinary action imposed by MSOP as a direct result of refusing treatment. Testimony that if the patient did not receive treatment, he would have to be supervised and kept away from the community showed that there was no less-restrictive alternative to MSOP that met his need for treatment and protected public safety. The patient's failure to timely appeal his commitment was a procedural bar to his current argument that the district court clearly erred in finding that, at the time of commitment, he suffered from a mental disorder that supported commitment as a SDP.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Mata-Woodruff


A07-0117


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 720



June 17, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Mata-Woodruff, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 458 (Minn., Aug. 5, 2008)
Related proceeding at State v. Avila, 2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 985 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Polk County District Court File No. K3-06-53.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before the Polk County District Court (Minnesota), of first-degree possession of a controlled substance in violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.021, subd. 2(1) (2004). Defendant appealed the convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the district court erred by refusing to suppress evidence found on her person after a stop of the vehicle in which she was a passenger. She further argued that the district court violated her right to confrontation by admitting a laboratory report without supporting testimony from the analyst who prepared it. The appellate court concluded that a totality of all the circumstances provided the officer with sufficient independent, reasonable, articulable suspicion of additional criminal activity, and the officers were justified in expanding the scope of the search. The admission of the report, however, violated defendant's rights under the Confrontation Clause. Defendant was not given an opportunity to cross-examine the analysts who generated the reports used as evidence against defendant. The trial court's error significantly affected the verdict because the lab report was presented as definitive evidence on the weight and identity of the substance found on defendant. Finally, the appellate court agreed that defendant should be given a new trial to ensure the fairness and integrity of the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part, with respect to the admission of the report, and the matter was remanded for a retrial.

Werpy v. McDonald Homes, Inc.


A07-0748


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 682



June 10, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota County District Court File No. C7-05-9908. Hon. Leslie May Metzen.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, homeowners, sued respondent construction company for breach of warranty, alleging that the company had constructed the homeowners' house defectively. The Dakota County District Court, Minnesota, granted the company's motion to dismiss, and the homeowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners brought a pro se conciliation-court action against the company and defendant company owner. The conciliation court found in favor of the homeowners on their claim against the company and awarded damages, but dismissed their claim against the company owner with prejudice. The company then removed the matter to district court. The homeowners argued that the district court erred in dismissing their complaint because the district court considered facts outside of the pleadings. The appellate court ruled that the district court erred in considering facts outside the complaint without providing the homeowners the opportunity to be heard on the issue that the district court found to be decisive. Also, the district court erred when it dismissed the complaint on the ground that the complaint failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. When the homeowners pled that they advised the company of major construction defects in the home related to non-compliance with building standards and demanded correction of the defects, their pleading averred that they gave the company legally sufficient notice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

State v. Zielske


A07-2136


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 686



June 10, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Freeborn County District Court File No. 24VB071873. Hon. James E. Broberg.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Freeborn County District Court, Minnesota, convicting her of failure to reduce speed in violation of Minn. Stat. § 169.14, subd. 3(a) (2006).


OVERVIEW: The officer testified that he was stopped on the shoulder of the highway completing paperwork from a previous traffic stop, with his emergency lights activated, when defendant's vehicle passed in the lane closest to him and "rocked" his squad car. The officer testified that the speed limit at that location was 70 miles per hour, and that when he activated his radar just as defendant passed, he obtained readings that indicated defendant was traveling at 69 and 70 miles per hour. The appellate court ruled that as applied to the facts of the case, Minn. Stat. § 169.14, subd. 3(a) (2006) was not vague in any sense useful to defendant. Any person of ordinary intelligence or common sense was at least put on notice that reduced speed would require a driver traveling at or near the maximum speed limit to exercise caution and slow down in the face of such circumstances. Also, the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The district court viewed the videotape of the incident recorded from the dashboard of the officer's squad car, and the district court heard the testimony and had an opportunity to assess the credibility of the officer, who was the only witness to testify.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1653 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ancel


A07-0195


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 638



June 3, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Ancel, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 756 (Minn., Aug. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota County District Court File No. K9-06-1786. Hon. Richard G. Spicer.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of two counts of burglary in the first degree in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.582, subd. 1(a) (2004).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for two counts of burglary in the first degree, but the appellate court reversed and remanded for a new trial. At defendant's trial, his cousin testified for the prosecution that defendant was the one who had entered the homes and taken the stolen property. A jury found defendant guilty. However, the appellate court concluded that the evidence of defendant's prior contacts with police and the police surveillance was admitted in error, requiring reversal for a new trial. A lengthy explanation of the evidence leading up to the officers' observations was unnecessary and, because the officers arrested defendant and his cousin in a taxicab while they were in possession of stolen property, it made it unnecessary to present prior police contacts to prove that defendant was one of the two persons who worked in concert on the burglaries. Also, none of the officers was able to identify defendant as the person who actually entered the two victims' homes. Moreover, the evidence was likely prejudicial because it naturally would have led a jury to believe that defendant was the type of person who often was in trouble with the law.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded for a new trial.

 

1654 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re City of St. Paul


A07-1512, A07-1513, A07-1514


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 606



May 27, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by In re a Petition for Instructions to Construe Basic Resolution 876 of the Port Auth., 2008 Minn. LEXIS 630 (2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by In re A Petition for Instructions to Construe Basic Resolution 876 of the Port Auth. of St. Paul, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 596 (Minn., Sept. 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File Nos. C5-06-200031; CX-04-200070; C2-02-200043. Hon. Teresa R. Warner.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent port authority petitioned the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) under Minn. Stat. § 501B.16(23) for an instruction approving its plan to liquidate a repayment fund and to discharge a percentage of its debt to appellant bondholders. The bondholders filed a motion to dismiss the petition on the ground of lack of subject matter jurisdiction and to appoint a receiver. The bondholders appealed the denial of their motions.


OVERVIEW: The port authority, to finance development of an area over which it had authority, issued bonds under Basic Resolution 876 (resolution). When economic circumstances made it evident that the fund would be depleted before all of the bondholders would be paid off in full, the port authority petitioned under Minn. Stat. § 501B.16(23) and Minn. Stat. § 501B.25 for instructions on the management and liquidation of the fund. The court held that the district court had authority to issue instructions in response to the port authority's petition. Two earlier orders of the district court, which also approved actions of port authority, were not vacated for lack of subject matter jurisdiction under Minn. R. Civ. P. 60.02(d) because the motions to vacate were not made within a reasonable time. The court also found that the denial of the bondholders' motion for the appointment of a receiver, under Minn. Stat. § 576.01, subd. 1 (2006), was also not an abuse of discretion. The resolution did not provide that the bondholders were automatically entitled to the appointment of a receiver upon application, and there was no evidence that the port authority disregarded court orders or committed waste.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

1655 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kyte


A07-0587


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 610



May 27, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota County District Court File No. K8-04-3010. Hon. Michael Sovis.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of possession of child pornography in violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.247, subd. 4(a) (2004), in the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota). Defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained from his hard drives was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Local police received a tip that defendant had used a credit card to access child pornography on the internet. A detective went to defendant's home and met him in the yard, where they talked. The detective testified that defendant admitted having child pornography and consented to a search of his computer. The detective went into the home and removed two hard drives without objection from defendant. Defendant argued that his consent was not voluntary. The court rejected defendant's arguments, accepting the district court's conclusion that consent was not coerced. The detective was dressed in plain clothes and did not touch, handcuff, or threaten defendant, and their conversation was cordial. The court rejected defendant's argument that the district court relied on Minn. Stat. § 617.247, subd. 8 (2004), which was later declared unconstitutional. Because the detective testified that he found 5,894 images depicting sexual acts with children 18 months to 13 years of age and described his training and methodology in determining the children's age range, the district court's rejection of a constitutional challenge to subdivision 8 was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the denial of his motion to suppress evidence.

 

1656 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Ficocello v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety


A07-1248


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 561



May 20, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Anoka County District Court File No. 02-C2-07-000525.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged an order from the Anoka County District Court, Minnesota, sustaining the revocation of his driver's license under the implied-consent law.


OVERVIEW: Several inches of snow had fallen when the officer was on patrol. The officer noticed fresh tire tracks in the snow going off the roadway and heading toward a pond. The officer investigated; he saw a pickup truck submerged in a holding pond. The officer saw a set of footprints in the snow from the pond. The officer noticed that defendant was stumbling and having a hard time walking. The officer testified that he ordered defendant to stop because he was concerned about his medical condition. Defendant argued that the officer's seizure of him was unconstitutional. The commissioner argued, however, that the seizure was justified under the emergency exception to the warrant requirement. The record demonstrated that the officer was motivated by a need to determine whether it was necessary to aid or assist defendant when the officer ordered defendant to stop. Defendant's argument simply raised a credibility issue, and the district court found the officer's testimony to be more credible and reasonable. The appellate court concluded that the emergency exception applied and that the officer's conduct in seizing defendant was reasonable under that exception.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1657 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Menne v. Phillips


A07-0564


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 564



May 20, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Office of Administrative Hearings File No. 8-6312-17667-CV.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator candidate challenged the decision of respondent Office of Administrative Hearings (OAH) , Minnesota, finding that the candidate violated Minn. Stat. § 211B.07, in the action filed by respondent claimant, and ordered to pay a civil penalty of $ 600.


OVERVIEW: The candidate, the claimant and a third individual were running for city council. The candidate distributed anonymous campaign flyers in the newspaper boxes of 90 residents displaying lawn signs in support of the claimant. The OAH found that the campaign flyers threatened voters in violation of Minn. Stat. § 211B.07 (2006). The candidate denied that he intended to intimidate anyone with the flyer. Rather, the candidate maintained that it was intended to provide individuals who obviously supported the claimant with information about him that might not be generally available to the citizenry at large. The court ruled that at most, the language at issue constituted an ultimatum for the claimant's supporters to take down their signs "or else." The court was unable to discern what, if anything, the candidate was threatening to do to individuals whose refusal to remove their signs would not go unnoticed in the future. Vaguely ominous-sounding language, without more, did not amount to a violation of Minn. Stat. § 211B.07. While the candidate's actions were far from admirable political-campaign practices, they did not meet the standard for a sanction under the statute.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed.

 

1658 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rourke


A07-0937


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 602



May 20, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Request granted State v. Rourke, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 470 (2008)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Rourke, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 705 (Minn., Oct. 22, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Stevens County District Court File No. 75-K3-03-17. Hon. Gerald J. Seibel.
State v. Rourke, 2006 Minn. LEXIS 458 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's sentence on his first-degree assault conviction (based on a plea agreement) was reversed and remanded for a Blakely trial. After dismissal of the aggravating factor of "particular cruelty," no aggravating factor existed to justify a durational departure. The Stevens County District Court, Minnesota, sentenced defendant to 103 months' imprisonment, the high end of the presumptive range, and ordered restitution. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State challenged the sentence imposed by the district court and sought reversal of the district court's order that the aggravating factor of "particular cruelty" was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court held that because defendant challenged an aggravating factor not used to impose a death sentence and because no cruel-and-unusual-punishment argument was made, the district court erred by applying a vagueness analysis to the Minnesota Sentencing Guidelines. As there was a valid reason to depart that the district court incorrectly ruled was invalid and failed to consider, the appellate court held that a remand for resentencing was warranted. The district court also abused its discretion in its refusal to submit the aggravating factor of "abuse of a position of power" to the jury and in its ruling that aggravating factors not specifically enumerated in the sentencing guidelines could not be used. Although the district court improperly defined the term, because "particular vulnerability" was rejected by the jury, a retrial of this aggravating factor would have violated double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was reversed and the case was remanded for a new Blakely trial and resentencing.

 

1659 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Willis


A06-2443


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 536



May 13, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
St. Louis County District Court File No. CR-06-3531.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial, the St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota), convicted defendant of separate felony counts of selling, possessing, and importing a controlled substance, in violation of Minn. Stat. §§ 152.021, subd. 1(1), 2(1), and 152.0261, subd. 1 (2004), and sentenced him to concurrent 98-month (importation) and 122-month (sale) prison sentences. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that the use of a Minnesota Bureau of Criminal Apprehension lab report at trial violated his confrontation rights under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Minn. Const. art. I, § 6. Plain error review under Minn. R. Crim. P. 31.02 applied. The lab report had probative value as to both the nature and the weight of the suspected narcotics--two elements of each of defendant's alleged offenses. Such reports were inadmissible without the testimony of the analyst who prepared them. Thus, defendant established plain error. He also showed a reasonable likelihood that the erroneous admission of the report had a significant effect on the district court's finding of guilt. The lab report was the only evidence on the weight of the seized cocaine apart from its packaging, and the district court expressly and specifically relied on the lab report when finding defendant guilty. The plain error justified reversing the convictions because the lab report was admitted in clear violation of defendant's constitutional rights, and without the lab report, the remaining evidence establishing the weight and nature of the narcotics was either of questionable accuracy or equivocal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

1660 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Borrero v. Gustafson


A07-0273


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 527



May 13, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. C9-06-002133. Hon. Edward J. Cleary.
United States v. Borrero, 149 Fed. Appx. 573, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 21939 (8th Cir. Minn., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed an action against defendants, officers and others attendant on his arrest, in the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), alleging false imprisonment, battery, and the denial of constitutional rights. The inmate sought to add additional named defendants, but leave to amend was denied. The district court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment on the basis of the statute of limitations, and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed his motion for leave to amend to add additional named defendants. Defendants filed a motion to amend their answer to plead the statute of limitations as a defense. Defendants then filed their motion for summary judgment. The inmate filed an amended complaint, although leave had not been granted, that named the additional defendants and also added a claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, a claim that was not addressed in his motion to amend his complaint. The court held that summary judgment for defendants was proper. The two-year statute of limitations, Minn. Stat. § 541.07(1) (2006), ran from the date of the inmate's arrest, not his conviction, and precluded his claims against the original defendants. The same limitations period would have barred the inmate's claims against the defendants he sought to add; therefore, denial of his leave to amend was proper. The district court was not required to consider the inmate's section 1983 claims because they were not properly before the court, having been raised only in the inmate's brief in response to defendants' motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants.

 

1661 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Haus


A07-0206


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 531



May 13, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES. 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Washington County District Court File Nos. T2-06-6587/T3-06-6615.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged in the Washington County District Court (Minnesota) for fishing with more than two lines in violation of Minn. Stat. § 97C.315 (2004) and fishing with an extra line in violation of Minn. R. 6266.0500, subpt. 4 (2005). Following denial of their motion to suppress, defendants proceeded to trial on stipulated facts. The district court found defendants guilty of both counts and fined them. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: A conservation officer approached defendants' ice-fishing house and saw through a window that someone was fishing inside. He knocked on the door and said, "Game warden, I'm checking licenses." After a pause, someone said, "Come on in," and opened the door. The officer entered and observed defendants using eight ice-fishing lines, one more each than allowed. Defendants' motion to suppress this evidence was denied. On appeal, defendants argued that the officer seized them when he knocked on their door and said, "Game warden, I'm checking licenses," and that this seizure was not supported by reasonable, articulable suspicion. Because defendants did not raise this argument in the district court it was waived on appeal. The court refused to consider it in the interest of justice because it implicated the constitutionality of statutes allowing conservation officers to check licenses and providing penalties for failure to comply. However, because, prior to proceeding to trial on stipulated facts, defendants did not personally waive any of their trial rights as required by Minn. R. Crim. P. 26.01, subd. 3, their convictions were required to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions and remanded the case for a new trial.

State v. Radichel


A07-0511


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 559



May 13, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Blue Earth County District Court File No. VB-05-1767. Hon. Kurt D. Johnson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Blue Earth County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of fourth-degree driving while impaired (DWI).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of fourth-degree DWI. On appeal, defendant claimed that the breath test results revealing his alcohol concentration should have been suppressed because the Minnesota Supreme Court ruled that the 2003 version of the implied-consent statute violated a driver's right to due process. The court found that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress the results of his breath test. The portion of the implied-consent law that was declared unconstitutional by Fedziuk, tardy judicial review of the administrative action to revoke the license, did not have any effect on the evidence obtained for the related criminal DWI proceeding. Because the unconstitutional provision of the implied-consent statute did not affect the evidence obtained for a related criminal DWI proceeding, the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress the results of his breath test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1663 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Urman


A07-0031


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 504



May 6, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES. 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. KX-06-1427. Hon. Michael F. Fetsch.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of a firearm by an ineligible person, and commission of a crime while possessing a bullet-resistant vest. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence of the gun and the bullet-resistant vest, which were obtained during the warrantless search of the vehicle he was driving. The Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, denied defendant's motion. Defendant was convicted. Defendant appealed the denial of his motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the stop of his vehicle was pretextual and, therefore, unconstitutional. The court found that police officers had probable cause for the stop because of the multiple traffic violations that the officers observed. Thus, the officers' subjective intent was irrelevant to the court's analysis under the Fourth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution. Defendant's argument that the stop was pretextual and, therefore, invalid under Minn. Const. art. I, § 10 failed. The record as a whole contained ample evidence to establish probable cause for the search of the vehicle because (1) the officers knew that a gas station was a place where multilevel drug dealing was common, (2) the police department received numerous calls for police assistance to the gas station because of criminal activity, (3) the officers saw defendant in the company of a known gang member, (4) a confidential informant's information was sufficiently reliable for inclusion in the totality of the circumstances establishing probable cause; and (5) the officers observed a bullet-resistant vest, a ski mask, gloves, and suspected marijuana in the vehicle. It was not error to deny defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1664 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Theusch v. Berg


A07-848


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 520



May 6, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Theusch v. Berg, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 406 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Theusch v. Berg, 129 S. Ct. 1526, 173 L. Ed. 2d 656, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 1738 (U.S., 2009)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Theusch v. Berg, 2010 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 374 (Minn. Ct. App., Apr. 27, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Todd County District Court File No. 77-C3-05-000492. Hon. William E. Walker.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sued respondent township and others, alleging trespass, the unlawful removal of trees, failure to give the required Minn. Stat. § 160.22, subd. 5 (2006) notice of the removal of trees, and a taking. The Todd County District Court (Minnesota) dismissed the taking and trespass claims, but awarded the landowners damages for the failure to give notice as to the tree removal. The landowners and township cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court did not err in concluding that the trespass and taking claims were time-barred under Minn. Stat. § 160.05, subd. 1 (2006), where the finding that there had been public use and maintenance of the drive by a road authority for the required six years was not clearly erroneous. Moreover, the district court's determination of the width of the drive did not exceed the width of actual use. Thus, the drive, including its supporting slopes and structure, was established as a public road, and the landowners were estopped from asserting a taking claim. Since the removal of trees along the drive was limited to the property that was established as a public road under § 160.05, subd. 1, the landowners' trespass-to-land claim was likewise barred. However, the district court erred in concluding that the landowners were entitled to damages for the township's violation of Minn. Stat. § 160.22 (2006) because although the landowners benefitted from the statute, there was no implied private right of action under the statute given that Minn. Stat. § 561.04 (2006) expressly provided a private cause of action for the township's failure to provide notice before removing the trees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the award of damages for the township's failure to notify the landowners before it cut down trees, but was otherwise affirmed. The case was remanded for further proceedings to consider the landowners' claim for damages related to the removal of trees under Minn. Stat. § 561.04 (2006).

 

1665 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Chase v. City of Plymouth


A07-0312


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 443



April 29, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES. 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-CV-05-18642. Hon. John L. Holahan.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner brought a claim for unlawful appropriation of personal property against respondent city in conciliation court and was awarded $ 3,375 in damages. The city appealed to the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) and counterclaimed for declaratory relief that the owner did not have the right to maintain a dock on a lake. The district court granted judgment for the city, and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner's home was separated from the lake by a road and a row of residential properties. The city right of way in the road abutted the shoreline of the lake. The owner had a dock on the lake that had been used by his predecessor since 1931. Despite repeated warnings by the city that the dock was in the city's right of way, the owner failed to remove his dock, boat, boat lift, and other personal property. The city removed it all to an impound facility. The court rejected the owner's argument that the district court did not have subject-matter jurisdiction to consider claims regarding ownership of real estate in a case removed from conciliation court, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 491A.01, subd. 4(1) (2006). The city had standing to assert its counterclaim based on its injury-in-fact from the owner's continuing trespass and the expenditure of city funds for the removal and storage of his personal property. The district court did not err in concluding that the owner did not have a legal right to maintain a dock on the lakeshore. Because the owner did not have a property right in the dock, his constitutional claims stemming from that claimed right were properly rejected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

1666 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Bushey v. State


A07-0787


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 447



April 29, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Bushey v. State, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 375 (Minn., July 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
St. Louis County District Court File No. 69-K5-03-100123. Hon. Gary J. Pagliaccetti.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner sought postconviction relief. The St. Louis County District Court, Minnesota, denied the request. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner entered a guilty plea to first-degree driving while impaired (DWI). The petitioner challenged the denial of his petition for postconviction relief on the ground that a five-year conditional-release portion of his sentence was unconstitutional. The petitioner alleged a violation of the Double Jeopardy Clauses of the United States and Minnesota Constitutions. The petitioner also argued that the conditional-release was an upward departure of his sentence. By its plain language, Minn. Stat. § 169A.276 required a district court to impose a five-year conditional-release term when there was a commitment to the Commissioner of Corrections. The district court did not abuse its discretion by imposing the conditional release term because the executed sentence and conditional-release period constituted one punishment for the same offense, so there was no violation of the Double Jeopardy Clause. Further, there was no abuse of discretion because the trial court was allowed to make an individual determination and order an appropriate sentence. Finally, no aggravating factors needed to be proved to apply the conditional-release term.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1667 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moore


A06-2346


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 416



April 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES. 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Moore, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 335 (Minn., June 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Chisago County District Court File No. CR-05-3086. Hon. Robert G. Rancourt.
State v. Moore, 493 N.W.2d 606, 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 1209 (Minn. Ct. App., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a bench trial, the Chisago County District Court, Minnesota, found defendant guilty of failing to register as a sex offender because he did not notify law enforcement authorities at least five days before moving from his primary address, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 243.166, subd. 3(b) (2000), and of failing to return the annual address-verification forms sent to him, in violation of § 243.166, subd. 4(e)(2). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: As to the charge of failing to register, the court held that the State's exercise of jurisdiction was not unconstitutional because an element of the crime occurred in Minnesota. The case met the constitutionally allowable jurisdictional reach of the first paragraph of Minn. Stat. § 609.025 (2000), which required that part of the offense occur within the state, because an essential element of failing to register was that defendant was a predatory offender, based on criminal conduct that occurred in Minnesota. Alternatively, it met the jurisdictional condition of the third paragraph of § 609.025, which required that the offense caused a criminal result within the state, because a predator's willful failure to register his whereabouts had the same detrimental impact within the state regardless of where the predator resided at the time of the failure. However, the evidence was not sufficient to support defendant's conviction for failing to return annual address-verification forms because the State did not present evidence that he ever received any of the forms. It would have been speculative to infer that he continued to live at the address to which the verification forms were sent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction for failing to return the annual address-verification forms sent to his address, otherwise affirmed the judgment, and remanded the case.

 

1668 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Perry


A07-0429


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 394



April 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Perry, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 444 (Minn., June 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Scott County District Court File No. CR-06-21912. Hon. Mary Jean Theisen.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before the Scott County District Court, Minnesota, of a fifth-degree violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.025, subd. 2(1) (2006). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police dispatch advised an officer of a report of a suspicious vehicle with three occupants. A woman informed dispatch that a black male approached her residence looking for someone who did not live there. The officer approached a vehicle and the officer stated that the occupants made furtive movements. Another officer arrived, and a passenger identified himself. The officer ran a warrant check on defendant. An officer found methamphetamine in his search of defendant. At issue was whether defendant was properly seized. The appellate court concluded that merely questioning defendant about their reasons for being in the area was not a seizure. Nevertheless, when the officer took defendant's license to run a warrant check, without a reasonable basis for doing so, the seizure was improper. The officers had no sequence of events that would give rise to probable cause for arrest and search until long after the suspicion of criminal activity should have been dispelled. The district court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress the methamphetamine.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the district court's decision, and the matter was remanded.

 

1669 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Jabr v. Jabr


A07-2003


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 422



April 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES. 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. F1-01-1586. Hon. Gary W. Bastian.
Jabr v. Jabr, 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 71 (Minn. Ct. App., Jan. 20, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father filed a motion to modify child custody, which had been granted to respondent mother. The Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) concluded that the child was not endangered and denied the father's motion. The district court continued a protective order but expanded it, forbidding the parties to make certain statements. The district court awarded the mother need-based attorney fees. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parties were married less than a year when their son was born and separated soon after. The mother had a son from a prior marriage who was 8 years older than their child. During the divorce proceedings, the district court ordered that neither party could use information obtained through the discovery process outside of the legal proceeding. The court held that the record supported the district court's finding of no endangerment and its denial of modification of custody. Despite claims of physical violence and inappropriate behavior between the parties' child and his older half brother, professionals testified that the parties' child showed no signs of physical or sexual abuse and that the half-brother did not pose a threat. The district court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion to discontinue the $ 250,000 life insurance obligation, although the remaining maximum child-support obligation was approximately $ 183,468. The new, expanded protective order prohibiting publishing "anything" about the mother or her family went beyond protecting the child's interests. It was an unconstitutional, overly broad, content-based restriction of the father's right to free speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's denial of the father's motion to modify custody, the award of attorney fees, and the ordered continuation of the $ 250,000 life insurance obligation. The protective order prohibiting the father from publishing anything about the mother was overbroad and was reversed.

 

1670 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gibson


A07-0720


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 361



April 15, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES. 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. K2-05-1122. Hon. Joanne M. Smith.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence. Defendant was convicted of possession of a firearm by an ineligible person. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Officers responded to a dispatch call advising them of multiple shots being fired and saw four men leave a group of people in the front yard of a house, get into a car, and drive toward the officers' squad car. The officers blocked the car, activated their emergency lights, left the squad car, drew their guns, and ordered the occupants of the car to put their hands somewhere visible. Defendant was an occupant of the car, and a loaded handgun was found on him. The appellate court determined that the stop of the car was justified based on the officers' reasonable suspicion that the occupants of the car were attempting to flee after having been involved in criminal activity and that there was a weapon in the car. Regarding defendant's argument that the officers arrested him without probable cause based on the officers' approach with guns drawn, the fact that the officers lacked probable cause at the time of the stop to arrest defendant did not provide a basis for suppressing the evidence of the gun, because the officers were not required to risk their lives by approaching, without their guns drawn, four men at a location where shots had been fired.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

 

1671 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kuhnau


A06-2115


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 356



April 15, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Crow Wing County District Court File No. K7-05-1959. Hon. Richard A. Zimmerman.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Crow Wing County District Court (Minnesota), defendant was convicted of fifth-degree possession of a controlled substance. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court should have suppressed controlled-substance evidence.


OVERVIEW: Under the Minnesota Constitution, a person was seized if in view of all the circumstances surrounding the incident, a reasonable person would have believed that the person was neither free to disregard the police questions nor free to terminate the encounter. The appellate court concluded that the district court properly determined that a seizure occurred only when a police officer ordered defendant to stop, while running after him. Before that time, the officer had made no show of authority that would cause a reasonable person to believe that he was not free to disregard the officer or to terminate the encounter. There was reasonable suspicion of criminal activity to support that seizure because defendant exhibited evasive conduct and he was in an area late at night that had a history of criminal activity. Because the officer ordered defendant several times to stop but he did not comply and the officer had to physically force defendant to the ground and pin his arms behind his back, a custodial arrest of defendant for a misdemeanor was authorized under Minn. R. Crim. P. 6.01, and the subsequent search incident to that arrest was proper.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1672 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Meredith


A06-2234


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 324



April 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Scott County District Court File No. 70-CR-05-22859. Hon. Mary Jean Theisen.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. *



* Retired judge of the district court, serving as judge of the Minnesota Court of Appeals by appointment pursuant to Minn. Const. art. VI, § 10.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of child endangerment, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.378, subd. 1(b)(1) (2004). The Scott County District Court (Minnesota) imposed sex-offender-based sentencing provisions that required him to register as a predatory sex offender and undergo a psychosexual evaluation. Defendant challenged the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's argument that his child endangerment conviction did not require him to register as a predatory offender under Minn. Stat. § 243.166, subd. 1b (Supp. 2005), was rejected where the complaint detailed the facts of defendant's ongoing, interconnected pattern of conduct having sexual overtones that involved the child victim and the same time period. Defendant's acquittal of the criminal sexual conduct charges did not extinguish the connection between the alleged conduct and the conduct supporting his conviction. Thus, defendant was subject to predatory-offender registration. The district court had the authority to require defendant to undergo a psychosexual evaluation as it was imposed as a condition of probation rather than pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 609.3457 (2004). Defendant's constitutional challenge to Minn. Stat. § 243.166, subd. 1b (Supp. 2005), was rejected as the statute was not punitive. Thus, the Apprendi and Blakely rules did not apply. The statute also did not violate defendant's substantive or procedural rights. The evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction given the victim's testimony about defendant's physical contact and invasion of privacy.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1673 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Yusuf


A06-2060


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 330



April 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE C ITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Olmsted County District Court File No. K1-05-3731. Hon. Jodi L. Williamson.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Olmsted County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of possession of six grams or more of cocaine, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.022, subd. 2(1) (2004).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of six grams or more of cocaine. On appeal, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to permit the jury to reasonably conclude that there was a strong probability that he was consciously exercising dominion and control over a bag containing the cocaine. Officers saw the bag in close proximity to defendant, lying on the ground about a foot away from him. Defendant stated to one officer that he knew that the bag contained cocaine. However, the trial court violated defendant's right to confrontation by admitting a Minnesota Bureau of Criminal Apprehension (BCA) report without the testimony of the analyst who prepared the report. An officer's testimony was insufficient to satisfy the scientific reliability requirement. The officer's estimate of the number of rocks in the bag did not establish the precise weight of the cocaine, and the weight of the bag and the cocaine together did not establish the weight of the cocaine alone. Thus, without the BCA report, the evidence was insufficient to satisfy the State's burden of proving the weight of the cocaine beyond a reasonable doubt, and the third prong of the plain-error test was satisfied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1674 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Civil Commitment of Jannetta


A07-2049


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 238



March 11, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Jannetta, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 269 (Minn., May 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-MH-PR-06-1222. Hon. H. Peter Albrecht.
State v. Jannetta, 355 N.W.2d 189, 1984 Minn. App. LEXIS 3592 (Minn. Ct. App., 1984)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a decision from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which committed him as a sexually dangerous person.


OVERVIEW: While the patient was in prison for child pornography, the State filed a petition for civil commitment under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18c(a) (2006). The patient was ordered indeterminately committed, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court held that the district court did not err by finding that the patient had manifested a sexual, personality, or other mental disorder or dysfunction under § 253B.02, subd. 18c(a)(2). Expert testimony revealed that the patient suffered from pedophilia, paraphilia, and a personality disorder. These did not allow the patient to adequately control his sexual impulses. Moreover, the evidence showed that the patient was highly likely to engage in future harmful sexual conduct. The patient had returned to his offense cycle after prison terms and offender treatment. The patient also offered no evidence of another less-restrictive treatment facility that was available to accommodate him and still meet the public safety requirements. Finally, there was no substantive due process violation, and difficulties in treatment did not render the civil commitment unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

In re Civil Commitment of Williams


A07-1813


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 237



March 11, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civ. Commitment of Williams, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 242 (Minn., Apr. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Anoka County District Court File No. P5-04-4750. Hon. Barry A. Sullivan.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Anoka County District Court (Minnesota) indeterminately committed appellant offender as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) under Minn. Stat. §§ 253B.18, subd. 1(a), based on determinations that the offender met the statutory criteria for commitment and evidence of new sexual conduct that the offender had engaged in while residing at a security hospital awaiting his review hearing. The offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: The offender argued that: (1) the evidence was insufficient to prove that he was highly likely to reoffend; (2) his current in-prison treatment program was an adequate, less-restrictive alternative to commitment; and (3) the statute allowing him to show that there was a less-restrictive alternative was unconstitutional and impossible of execution. However, the appellate court determined that: (1) the offender continued to engage in inappropriate sexual behavior even while residing in a secure facility; (2) due to the offender's numerous past failures in sex offender treatment, and his lack of empathy and insight into his behaviors, there was no evidence to suggest that he would follow through with treatment; (3) although two examiners initially indicated that the offender could be treated in a program other than a secure facility, that program was no longer recommended by the examiners, and thus the commitment statute providing for the least-restrictive alternative was not impossible of execution; and (4) civil commitment under the SDP statute did not violate double jeopardy because such commitment was remedial, and its purpose was treatment rather than punishment.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

Johnson v. City of Shorewood


A06-2353


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 181



February 19, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Johnson v. City of Shorewood, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 219 (Apr. 29, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Johnson v. City of Shorewood, 555 U.S. 886, 129 S. Ct. 281, 172 L. Ed. 2d 149, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 5471 (Oct. 6, 2008)
Related proceeding at City of Shorewood v. Johnson, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28534 (D. Minn., Jan. 12, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-CV-04-016195. Hon. John L. Holahan.
Johnson v. City of Shorewood, 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 442 (Minn. Ct. App., May 17, 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this, his fifth lawsuit, appellant alleged the unlawful regulatory and physical taking of his property by respondents, including a city, in violation of his rights to due process and equal protection. He brought claims under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1985, for breach of contract, and sought declaratory relief. The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, granted summary judgment for respondents. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Among the claims resolved on appeal, the appellate court found no error in the denial of appellant's motion for a declaratory judgment/partial summary judgment related to the city's alleged taking of a 33-foot road easement, the construction of a fence and a walking trail, and the installation of a fiber optic cable because appellant did not establish that the takings occurred. He did not show that he had an interest in the portion of road, and he did not deny the city's allegations of a prescriptive easement, Minn. Stat. § 160.05, subd. 1 (2006). The silt fence was on his property for less than a week. The walking trail was not graded or constructed. The fiber optic cable, while permanent, was installed by a private company operating without a permit. Appellant's claims of breach of contract, third-party beneficiary breach of contract, promissory estoppel, fraud, misrepresentation, negligence, and joint concerted tortious conduct, brought in response to a third-party's entry of a restrictive covenant encumbering property that appellant had allegedly contracted to buy, were barred by the six-year statutes of limitations, Minn. Stat. § 541.05, subd. 1(1), (5), and (6) (2006).


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Liimatainen


A07-0078


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 157



February 12, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Liimatainen, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 225 (Minn., Apr. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
St. Louis County District Court File No. K8-03-601071. Hon. Gerald C. Martin.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner challenged the judgment of the St. Louis County District Court, Minnesota, denying his motion for sentence correction.


OVERVIEW: In 2004, the petitioner pled guilty to first-degree felony driving while impaired, and was sentenced to the presumptive guidelines sentence of 54 months' imprisonment based on a severity level of seven and a criminal-history score of three. The petitioner's criminal-history score included one point for a 1989 felony conviction of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle (UUMV), for which he received a stay of imposition of sentence. The petitioner maintained that because the district court stayed the imposition of his sentence for the UUMV conviction and he served less than two years on probation, his criminal-history score for the offense should reflect a misdemeanor disposition. The petitioner sought a modification of his criminal-history score to two. The appellate court ruled that under Minn. Sentencing Guidelines II.B.1, the district court correctly assigned one felony point for the UUMV conviction. The classification of the UUMV conviction as a misdemeanor under Minn. Stat. § 609.13, subd. 1(2) (2002), did not preclude the district court's later decision in a different context to characterize the conviction as a felony.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Welfare of B.L.R.


A06-2246


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 165



February 12, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Brown County District Court File No. 08-JV-05-231. Hon. John R. Rodenberg.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of an order from the Brown County District Court (Minnesota), which imposed an adult sanction after his probation was revoked.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was arrested after fleeing officers in a vehicle. A delinquency petition was filed. The State asked the trial court to designate the case as extended jurisdiction juvenile (EJJ). The juvenile pled guilty to fleeing a police officer in a motor vehicle. The trial court imposed a juvenile disposition and advised the juvenile that if he violated the terms of his probation, it would impose an adult sentence. A probation revocation hearing occurred after the juvenile was involved in a traffic accident with indications that he might have been driving under the influence of alcohol. The trial court revoked the juvenile's probation and imposed a stayed adult sentence of one year and one day and a 60-day term in jail. On appeal, the court found that because the juvenile did not consent to an adult sanction under Minn. Stat. § 260B.130, subd. 4(b) (2004), the trial court retained juvenile jurisdiction only and could not impose an adult sanction against him. Even after the probation violation, juvenile jurisdiction was not terminated. While the trial court could impose new juvenile dispositions pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 260B.198, it had no authority to impose new adult sanctions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.
