Amina, Inc. v. City of Minneapolis


A06-2172


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 91



January 29, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Minneapolis City Council.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On writ of certiorari from revocation of its business licenses by respondent city, relator business owner sought to have the city's revocation decision remanded for further proceedings or reversed because it was based on unlawful procedure, illegal grounds, or other error of law, and was unsupported by substantial evidence.


OVERVIEW: The business owner was not denied due process when the city revoked its licenses where it received reasonable notice, a hearing before an impartial administrative law judge, and a hearing by the public safety and regulatory services committee before the revocation. The city did not violate Minn. Stat. § 14.61, subd. 1, where a majority of the committee conducted a hearing and allowed the business owner to present written and oral arguments. The committee's recommendation was properly part of the record the city council considered in rendering its decision. Even though the council should have re-voted following a motion for reconsideration, the council's intent to revoke the licenses was patently clear from the transcript. The revocation decision was supported by substantial evidence where the owner failed to meet the voluntary conditions it had agreed to and had violated the Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances. Finally, the constitutional claims failed as the owner had adequate notice of the alleged violations and received due process, the surveillance camera requirement was not unconstitutionally vague, and imposition of voluntary conditions did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The city's decision was affirmed.

 

1680 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Neng Por Yang v. Nutter


A07-232


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 10



January 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Neng Por Yang v. Nutter, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 76510 (D. Minn., May 27, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-CV-06-5454. Hon. Heidi S. Schellhas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Family members called the police out of concern that appellant patient was dangerous and was threatening the family. The police took the patient away and he was sent to a hospital for two months. Upon his release, the patient sued respondent police department (City) on 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and state-law tort claims. The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, granted the City's motion for summary judgment. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient contended the district court erred by granting the City's motion for summary judgment. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the patient's complaint was devoid of any allegations that police policy required the officers to act in a manner that violated his constitutional rights. Because the patient did not allege an unconstitutional municipal custom, he necessarily did not allege a pattern of misconduct to which the officers' supervisors could have acted with deliberate indifference or tacitly authorized. Because the patient's complaint lacked the specific allegations were required to maintain a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim against the City, the district court did not err by granting summary judgment to the City. And as the officers were performing discretionary, not ministerial, acts when they detained the patient and transported him to the hospital, the officers were protected by official immunity. The officers had reason to believe that the patient was a danger to himself and others; no reasonable jury could have found that the officers' acts were willful or malicious wrongs.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Morris v. State


A06-1950


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 13



January 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Morris v. State, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 172 (Minn., Mar. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File Nos. K7-96-4038; K5-96-4040; K9-96-4042; KO-96-4043. Hon. James H. Clark, Jr.
State v. Morris, 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 100 (Minn. Ct. App., Feb. 4, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant postconviction petitioner pleaded guilty to four counts of criminal defamation, served his probation, and was discharged early. The petitioner's request for postconviction relief was denied. His appeal from the denial was dismissed and the matter was remanded. The Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, appointed counsel to represent the petitioner and subsequently denied his motion to withdraw his pleas. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the petitioner argued that the district court abused its discretion when it denied his petition to withdraw his pleas of guilty. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the petitioner was competent to enter his guilty pleas; the judge who accepted the pleas was able to observe and assess the petitioner's general demeanor, his manner of responding to questions, the content of each response, and the petitioner's ostensible understanding of both the context and the particulars of the criminal proceedings, including the rights he was waiving by pleading guilty. The picture that the petitioner presented to the judge was that of an intelligent and lucid individual who was able to follow the questions asked and to give responsive answers. Further, there was nothing in the record to suggest that the petitioner's attorney failed to answer any legal questions for him, or that he failed to discuss defenses as well as charges. Therefore, the district court did not abuse its discretion in ruling that the petitioner's ineffective-assistance-of-counsel claim failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Morris v. State


A06-2101


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 47



January 15, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Morris v. State, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 137 (2008)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Morris v. State, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 295 (Minn., May 14, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File Nos. 99001287, 99020103.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the order of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, denying his motion requesting that legal counsel be appointed to represent him in his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: In March 1999, the petitioner waived his right to counsel and pled guilty to three counts of misdemeanor theft. The petitioner did not file a direct appeal of the convictions. In December 2005, the petitioner filed a petition for postconviction relief, seeking to withdraw his guilty plea, arguing that he was not competent to plead guilty or waive legal counsel due to his bipolar disorder. The petitioner requested that legal counsel be appointed to represent him. The state public defender declined representation on the ground that Minn. Stat. § 611.14(2) (2004) did not provide for representation in misdemeanor postconviction proceedings. The petitioner argued that the statute was unconstitutional. The appellate court ruled that Minn. Stat. § 611.14(2) (2004) was not unconstitutional. Minn. Stat. § 611.14(2) addressed the right to the appointment of legal counsel in a postconviction proceeding, which allowed for the appointment of counsel for indigent individuals convicted of a felony or gross misdemeanor. The statute did not extend the appointment of counsel for misdemeanor postconviction proceedings.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

1683 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pernell


A06-1128Fp


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 45



January 15, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part, Review denied by, in part, Review pending at State v. Pernell, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 132 (2008)
Review denied by State v. Pernell, 2009 Minn. LEXIS 198 (Minn., Mar. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. K1-05-600867.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) of second-degree test refusal, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 169A.20, subd. 2 (2004). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under Minn. Stat. § 169A.51, subd. 1(a) (2004), any person who operated a motor vehicle consented to a chemical test for the purpose of determining the presence of alcohol, a controlled substance or its metabolite, or a hazardous substance. Therefore, defendant's Fourth Amendment rights were not violated because she consented to submit to a chemical test by driving a motor vehicle. Further, Minn. Stat. § 169A.20, subd. 2, did not violate an individual's Fourth Amendment rights. Defendant also argued that her Miranda rights were violated. Because defendant's statement, "I do not think I should have to take a test" was not in any way incriminatory, the district court's admission of that evidence, even if made in error, was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Further, defendant did not raise a reasonable-refusal defense in the district court and had not identified on appeal the grounds on which she could have raised such a defense; therefore, she had not been prejudiced by the admission of the evidence, and the court declined to address the need for a Miranda warning.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

1684 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Civ. Commitment of Foster


A07-1564


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 22



January 15, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by In re Civ. Commitment of Foster, 2013 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 889 (Minn. Ct. App., Sept. 16, 2013)
Decision reached on appeal by Foster v. Jesson, 857 N.W.2d 545, 2014 Minn. App. LEXIS 110 (Minn. Ct. App., 2014)
Related proceeding at, Motion granted by, Petition denied by In re Civ. Commitment of Foster, 2016 Minn. LEXIS 376 (Minn., June 21, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
St. Louis County District Court File No. 69HI-PR-06-37.
State v. Giishig, 2005 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 470 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a decision from the St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota), which committed him as a sexually-dangerous person (SDP) and a sexual-psychopathic personality (SPP).


OVERVIEW: The patient was involved in several sexual assaults of minor children. After he was committed for meeting the criteria of both a SDP and a SPP, this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the district court's finding regarding the patient's status as a SDP was not in error under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18c(a) (2006) because he was highly likely to reoffend in the future, even though the experts in the case reached different conclusions after considering the factors under Linehan I. The record showed that the patient had an ongoing attraction to minor females, he was unable to avoid contact with them, and he did not function well in an unstructured environment. The length of time since the last offense was not persuasive due to his incarceration and high degree of supervision in the community. Next, the patient fell under the criteria for the SPP under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18b (2006) because he lacked the power to control his sexual impulses. The patient's conduct likely caused significant psychiatric disorders, physical harm, and other problems. Finally, a constitutional issue was not heard since it was not presented to the district court.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1685 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Arango v. Dep't of Empl. & Econ. Dev.


A06-2382


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2008 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 86



January 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
COMMISSIONER. Department of Employment and Economic Development File No. 13084 06.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator claimant challenged the decision of the unemployment law judge (ULJ) for respondent Minnesota Department of Employment and Economic Development, finding that the claimant was not eligible for unemployment benefits during a period when he was attending school full-time.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was a member of a mechanics association. The association went on strike, and the claimant enrolled in a two-year, full-time program to retrain as a heavy-duty-truck mechanic. Unemployment benefits were denied. The ULJ determined that the claimant was ineligible for benefits because he had not satisfied the statutory weekly eligibility requirements of being able to work, being available for suitable employment, and actively seeking suitable employment. The claimant requested reconsideration, and the ULJ issued an order of affirmance. The appellate court ruled that substantial evidence supported the ULJ's finding. The claimant's testimony about his work history during the period for which he was seeking benefits supported the finding that he was focused on retraining rather than on finding a job. The claimant's testimony on his work history and effort to retrain himself conflicted with his testimony that he would quit school if a suitable job were offered to him. Unemployment benefits were intended to be a temporary wage replacement while individuals found new employment.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1686 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Gibbs v. Metro. Hous. & Redevelopment Auth.


A06-1612


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1242



December 31, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Metropolitan Housing and Redevelopment Authority.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator tenant sought certiorari review of a decision of respondent Metropolitan Housing and Redevelopment Authority (MHRA) to terminate her Section 8 rental assistance.


OVERVIEW: The tenant was responsible for paying a portion of her rent, and she received Section 8 rental assistance. After the tenant failed to pay rent for two months, her landlord filed an eviction complaint. The tenant was notified by MHRA that her rental-assistance benefits would be terminated because she was evicted, and an informal hearing was held. The tenant argued, on appeal, that: (1) the evidence did not support termination of her benefits; (2) the decision was arbitrary and capricious because MHRA failed to consider mitigating circumstances; (3) she was denied procedural due process; and (4) MHRA failed to make adequate findings of fact. 24 C.F.R. 982.552(b)(2) was the applicable provision because it specifically mentioned eviction. The hearing officer did not err in terminating the rental assistance under section 982.552(b)(2). Substantial evidence supported MHRA's decision, and the decision was not arbitrary and capricious. The tenant was not denied procedural due process, and the findings were sufficient to permit meaningful review. The record established that the tenant knew, or had reason to know, of the possible adverse consequence of termination if she was evicted.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the decision.

 

1687 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Minn. Dep't of Pub. Safety


A07-0004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1220



December 24, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. C5-06-5238.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought reinstatement of his driver's license, and filed a complaint seeking a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief. Respondent Minnesota Department of Public Safety moved to dismiss. The Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, granted the motion to dismiss. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Between 1970 and 1979, appellant was convicted of driving while impaired (DWI) four times, and his driving privileges were revoked, cancelled, and denied as inimical to public safety. Appellant's driving privileges were reinstated, revoked again in January 1987, and later reinstated. In October 2004, appellant submitted to a chemical test and failed. Appellant pled guilty to DWI, his driving privileges were revoked, cancelled, and denied as inimical to public safety. Appellant sought partial reinstatement of his driving privileges for work purposes. The Department argued that the review procedure, including the 180-day limitation in Minn. Stat. § 171.19 (2004), was the exclusive remedy for review. The appellate court ruled that the proper challenge for denial of a license as inimical to public safety or welfare was found in Minn. Stat. § 171.19. Minn. Stat. § 171.19 provided a legal remedy of judicial review within 180 days, a legal remedy that appellant failed to exercise. Appellant lacked the justiciable controversy required for a declaratory judgment because he lacked a legal interest in challenging the determination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1688 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Ness v. County of Crow Wing


A06-1690


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1202



December 18, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Crow Wing County District Court File No. C5-05-1278. Hon. David J. Teneyck.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sued appellee county and others, alleging that the county's denial of a construction permit was unreasonable, arbitrary and capricious, contrary to law, did not represent a legitimate public purpose, violated their rights to equal protection and due process, and constituted an uncompensated regulatory takings. The Crow Wing County District Court (Minnesota) found in favor of the county. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the owners purchased a contiguous parcel, their original parcel and the continuous parcel merged into a single, undivided parcel under Crow Wing County, Minn., Zoning Ordinance § 7.5(C)(4) (1972). Crow Wing County, Minn., Zoning Ordinance § 7.7 (1972) did not apply as the change referred to in that provision was the alteration of a physical characteristic of the property, not its legal status. Thus, the county had denied the owners' construction permit application based on a correct interpretation of its ordinance. The district court did not err in declining to permit relitigation of the arbitrary and capricious claim because even though it had not expressly directed a final judgment to be entered and could have reconsidered its ruling under Minn. R. Civ. P. 54.02, the record did not remain open for submission of new evidence. The equal protection claim failed because the neighbors' nonconforming parcel was not the same as the owners' newly created parcel. The county's action was not a taking since merging lots served a legitimate interest in phasing out nonconforming uses and the county's action did not interfere with the owners' investment-backed expectations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1689 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Kohl's Dep't Stores, Inc. v. County of Stearns


File No. 73-C0-06-2028


MINNESOTA TAX COURT, COUNTY OF STEARNS, SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, REGULAR DIVISION


2007 Minn. Tax LEXIS 26



December 18, 2007, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation filed a petition challenging respondent county's assessment of the corporation's department store. The county filed a motion to dismiss the petition, alleging that the corporation failed to comply with the 60-day rule set forth in Minn. Stat. § 278.05, subd. 6 (2007), because it failed to provide the net rentable area for the subject property to the county assessor as required by the 60-day rule.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the corporation failed to provide the net rentable area for the subject property as required by the 60-day rule. The corporation did not provide the 2000 amended lease, which stated an additional 22,000 square foot addition to the subject property. The corporation admitted that it did not provide net rentable area in the information submitted to the county. Instead, the corporation claimed that the county could determine the net rentable area by reviewing a rental components summary and locating the proper numerator and denominator and making the appropriate calculations. However, the corporation provided no information to suggest that the county needed to make any calculations in order to determine the net rentable area. The county could do nothing more than guess the net rentable area for the subject property.


OUTCOME: The county's motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1690 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Welfare of A.M.A.


A06-1611


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1164



December 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 304225/JV-06-6662. Hon. Tanya Mozell Bransford.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) adjudicated defendant juvenile delinquent for aiding and abetting first-degree burglary under Minn. Stat. §§ 609.582, subd. 1(a) and 609.05 (2004). The juvenile challenged the conviction.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile's Miranda waiver was voluntary and intelligent where the officer had read him his rights prior to the interrogation, the juvenile indicated that he understood the rights, and the officer had reiterated those rights later during the interrogation. The failure to tape record part of the interrogation did not warrant suppression where the juvenile did not dispute the facts surrounding his Miranda rights or waiver. The evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction where the juvenile's admission that he was in the garage where the golf clubs later identified as the victim's were stolen from allowed a jury to reasonably conclude that he was in the victim's garage the night it was burglarized. The trial court did not err in failing to secure the juvenile's express waiver of his right to testify as Minn. Stat. § 260B.163, subd. 9, did not establish a statutory right to testify. Thus, the presumption that the decision not to testify was made voluntarily and intelligently unless something in the record suggested otherwise applied. The trial court failed to make the findings required by Minn. R. Juv. Delinq. P. 15.05, subd. 2(A)(1)-(2) and Minn. Stat. § 260B.198, subd. 1(m).


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed to the extent that the district court failed to make additional findings addressing why the public safety and the juvenile's interests were not best served by maintaining his current custody and why a new placement was suitable. The judgment was otherwise affirmed. The case was remanded for additional findings.

 

1691 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Velez


A06-1034


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1158



December 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Velez, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 112 (Minn., Feb. 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Mower County District Court File No. K4-05-847. Hon. Donald E. Rysavy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pled guilty to first-degree assault, the Mower County District Court, Minnesota, imposed a 138-month executed sentence, an upward durational departure from the 86-month presumptive sentence under the Minnesota Sentencing Guidelines. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended his guilty plea was not was not made intelligently because at the time it was entered, Blakely mandated that the facts supporting an aggravated sentence be determined by a jury. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the amendment to Minn. Stat. § 244.10 (2004) authorizing the district court to convene a jury to make findings for upward departures applied to sentencing hearings, resentencing hearings, and sentencing departures sought on or after the effective date of the amendment, even though the offense may have occurred prior to the effective date. Thus, at the time of defendant's plea agreement, the court had the authority under the amended statute to impanel a sentencing jury. Nothing in the former language of the guidelines prohibited the district court from imposing a sentence based on facts found by the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1692 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Solomon


A06-1959


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1165



December 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Scott County District Court File No. 70-CR-05-2164. Hon. Carol Hooten.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Scott County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him for DWI.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with second-degree DWI. He had an alcohol-related license revocation from 1999 and a DWI conviction from 2002. These two prior incidents constituted aggravating factors that enhanced defendant's charge. On appeal, defendant's argument that the prior license revocation could not qualify as an aggravating factor because he was not fluent in English failed. While Minn. Stat. § 611.32, subd. 2 (2004) provided for an interpreter, this statute applied to criminal cases; the license revocation proceeding was civil in nature. The fact that defendant was not represented by counsel was irrelevant. Past uncounseled civil license revocations could be used to enhance subsequent DWI charges without violating the constitutional right to counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Civil Commitment of Harrison


A07-1181


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1186



December 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civil Commitment of Harrison, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 84 (Minn., Feb. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Meeker County District Court File No. 47-PR-06-1130. Hon. Kathryn N. Smith.
State v. Harrison, 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1031 (Minn. Ct. App., Aug. 9, 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon respondent State's petition, the Meeker County District Court, Minnesota, entered an order of an indeterminate commitment against appellant patient as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) and a sexual psychopathic personality (SPP). The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient contended, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to support the district court's findings that he was an SDP and an SPP. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that ample evidence existed in the record to support the district court's conclusion that the patient engaged in a course of harmful sexual conduct even without relying on the testimony of the seven Spreigl witnesses. In light of the testimony establishing that the patient sexually abused nine children over a period of more than 20 years in addition to the frequency of each child's abuse, there was overwhelming evidentiary support for the district court's determination that he engaged in a habitual course of sexual misconduct. Evidence that the patient lacked the ability to control his sexual impulses included his 20-year history of sexual abuse of children, his minimization of the offenses, his failure to take responsibility for sexually abusing two victims despite admitting the abuse, psychological test results that indicated a high risk of sexually reoffending in the future, his failure to participate in sex-offender treatment, and his lack of empathy or insight.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1694 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


P.G.M. v. J.M.A. (In re Baby Boy A.)


A07-452


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1189



December 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-PA-FA-05-278. Hon. Mary E. Steenson DuFresne.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, made a determination of parentage and custody in favor of respondent father. Appellant gestational surrogate challenged the decision.


OVERVIEW: The father decided to use a surrogate mother to carry his child. The parties entered into a gestational-surrogacy agreement (GSA) that called for the governance of Illinois law. The GSA was later modified. The district court concluded that, under the Illinois Parentage Act, the father was the child's father, and it denied the surrogate parental rights. The mother cited three reasons in support of her claim that it was unenforceable: (1) the GSA did not reflect the parties' actual agreement, (2) the father coerced the surrogate to sign the GSA, and (3) the GSA contravened the public policy of Minnesota. The record contained no evidence that, by selecting Illinois law, the parties acted in bad faith or with the intent to evade Minnesota law. The record contained significant evidence to support the district court's finding that the parties entered into a written contract and orally modified that contract. The district court also properly concluded that there was no fraud, misrepresentation, undue influence, or coercion by either party in the formation of the contract. Because the record supported the district court's findings, the findings were not manifestly contrary to the evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

 

1695 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Civ. Commitment of Christiansen


A07-1290


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1187



December 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by In re Civ. Commitment of Christiansen, 2017 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 488 (Minn. Ct. App., May 30, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
St. Louis County District Court File No. 69DU-PR-06-451. Hon. Shaun R. Floerke.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon respondent County's petition to have appellant patient committed, the St. Louis County District Court, Minnesota, entered an order for an indeterminate commitment of the patient as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) and as a sexual psychopathic personality (SPP). The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient argued that there was not clear and convincing evidence that he met the statutory definitions of an SDP or an SPP; and his indeterminate commitment violated the Double Jeopardy and Ex Post Facto clauses. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that the patient's sexual misconduct constituted a course of harmful sexual misconduct sufficient to meet the definition of an SDP; he had been resistant to change and because he reoffended after receiving prior punishment for his actions, his behavior was enduring. The patient sexually assaulted family members, which would result in serious emotional harm to his victims, and his offenses involved multiple acts of sexual contact and/or penetration. As the nature of his sexual offenses was such that they likely caused substantial mental harm to his victims, they were sufficiently egregious and violent in their nature to meet the dangerous-to-others requirement of the SPP definition. Because the patient did not provide any evidence indicating that his civil commitment, even if ineffective, constituted preventive detention, he failed to meet his burden to show that his indeterminate commitment was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1696 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Boeser v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety


A06-2032


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1138



December 4, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Scott County District Court File No. 70-CV-06-1565. Hon. Joseph T. Carter.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Commissioner of Public Safety cancelled petitioner's driver's license for violation of a no-alcohol restriction on the license. Petitioner sought judicial review. The Scott County District Court (Minnesota) sustained the cancellation, concluding that the Commissioner had sufficient cause to believe petitioner had consumed alcohol, and that the sufficient-cause-to-believe standard did not violate due process. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court's finding that petitioner drank alcohol was not clearly erroneous. Petitioner admitted that the officers found him slumped over the wheel of his pickup truck at two o'clock in the morning, parked just outside the two bars in which he had been socializing for the past six hours. He admitted that the officers smelled alcoholic beverages when they opened his door. He admitted that they noticed that he and the inside of his truck were covered with his vomit and that he vomited again as he stepped from the truck. Petitioner's argument that his illness was caused by exposure to paint fumes was heard and rejected by the district court, and the court deferred to the district court's credibility assessment and its weighing of evidence. Also, petitioner's constitutional challenge to the standard applied to cancel his driving privileges was not compelling. The sufficient-cause-to-believe standard provided a reasonably reliable basis to test the fact of petitioner's post abstinence consumption.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

1697 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Colliers v. Dakota County Dev. Agency


A06-1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1110



November 20, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota County Community Development Agency.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Finding that relator tenant's failure to report income and an apartment move was intentional, respondent Dakota County Community Development Agency (Minnesota) terminated the tenant's Section 8 housing benefits. The tenant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the tenant contended the record did not support the termination of benefits, the hearing officer's decision was arbitrary and capricious, and he was not given a reasonable accommodation. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that the Section 8 housing choice voucher program did not mandate that the agency prove fraudulent or intentional misrepresentation before terminating a participant's housing assistance; the termination decision was within the agency's discretion pursuant to 24 C.F.R. § 982.552(c) (2006). Further, the hearing officer's inference that the tenant's failure to report was intentional was buttressed by the evidence offered in support of the agency's termination decision, including his prior recertification applications which demonstrated his understanding that he was required to provide information about his employment and income. And the hearing officer's decision was not arbitrary or capricious as the hearing officer did consider whether the tenant's head injury caused his failure to report. Finally, the hearing officer properly found that the tenant never made a request for a reasonable accommodation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1698 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Hecimovich v. State


A06-2046


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1098



November 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Hecimovich v. State, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 54 (Minn., Jan. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
St. Louis County District Court File No. K9-05-300295. Hon. Mark M. Starr.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In accordance with a negotiated plea bargain, petitioner pled guilty to one count of making terroristic threats and received a stayed sentence of a year and a day, plus supervised probation for five years. After his release, the petitioner sought to withdraw his guilty plea. The St. Louis County District Court, Minnesota, denied the petition, and the petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the petitioner contended that he should be allowed to withdraw his guilty plea because, at the time he made the plea, he was deprived of his mental health medication and he pleaded guilty to get out of jail and have access to his medication. The appellate court disagreed, concluding that the district court's finding that the plea was knowing, voluntary, and intelligent (even though the petitioner's not receiving his medication caused him undue discomfort and anxiety) was supported by the evidence, including his own statements. On his written petition to plead guilty, he indicated that he did not decide to plead guilty in order to expedite his case; in response to questions from his attorney, he said that no one had promised him anything or made any threats to him to induce him to plead guilty; at the sentencing hearing, he admitted that he had told his mother he would burn the house down if she put it up for sale and that he did this to terrorize her and cause her anxiety; and he told the district court he understood the conditions of his probation. At no time did the petitioner ever mention being deprived of his medication.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1699 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


County of Freeborn v. Brue


A07-0263


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1086



November 6, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Freeborn County District Court File No. 24-CV-06-284. Hon. John A. Chesterman.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owners, challenged the judgment of the Freeborn County District Court, Minnesota, ordering them to allow respondent county to remove items from their property to bring it into conformity with the county's zoning and waste management ordinances.


OVERVIEW: The county received complaints about the condition of the owners' property. Unlicensed, inoperable vehicles, including piles of junk, scrap metal, automotive parts, and tires were among the items stored on the property. Over five years, the county tried unsuccessfully to have the property voluntarily cleaned up. The county's efforts included phone calls, letters, on-site visits, and providing a list of businesses that helped with cleanup. The county served the owners with a summons and complaint alleging violation of its zoning and waste management ordinances. The county was awarded default judgment against the first owner and summary judgment against the second owner. The county removed the items and brought the property into compliance with the ordinances. The appellate court ruled that the district court did not err by entering judgment without an eminent domain proceeding and without making the findings required for injunctive relief. Also, the owners were not deprived of due process of law. The state statutes and county ordinances provided a legal remedy for the county after it had attempted to have the property brought into compliance for five years.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1700 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Boyce


A06-2050


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1070



October 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Boyce, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 33 (Minn., Jan. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 05-3231. Hon. Robert M. Small.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of felony failure to use payment proceeds to pay for contributions to an improvement to real estate, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 514.02 (2004).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, the owner of a construction company, was charged with felony theft by swindle, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.52, subd. 2(4) (2004), and felony failure to use payment proceeds to pay for contributions to an improvement to real estate. He was acquitted of theft by swindle and convicted of failing to use payment proceeds to pay for an improvement to real estate. The trial court stayed imposition of sentence and placed him on probation. On appeal, he argued that Minn. Stat. § 514.02 was void for vagueness and failed to provide constitutionally adequate notice of what was criminal and what was not. The court found that defendant failed to sustain his burden of proving that § 514.02 was void for vagueness. The statutory language informed a person of ordinary intelligence of what was prohibited. Further, determining that defendant did not commit theft by swindling did not preclude the jury from also determining that he failed to use payment proceeds to pay for contributions to an improvement to real estate. A jury could have concluded that defendant violated Minn. Stat. § 514.02 without concluding that he obtained property by swindling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1701 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wooten


A06-1288


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1065



October 24, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Motion to strike denied by State v. Wooten, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 20 (Minn., Jan. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 06-000984. Hon. Marilyn J. Kaman and Thorwald H. Anderson.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his motion to suppress and convicted him of third-degree refusal to submit to a chemical test and fourth-degree driving while impaired (DWI). The State moved to strike defendant's appendix and a portion of his brief.


OVERVIEW: An officer observed a stalled car on a freeway ramp. Defendant was sitting in the driver's seat of the car. The officer pushed the car to the shoulder of the ramp. Defendant restarted the car and began to drive away, but the officer activated her spotlight to indicate to him that he needed to stop because the officer had not yet identified who he was. The officer smelled alcohol coming from defendant's breath and saw that his eyes were red and watery. Defendant was subsequently charged with third-degree refusal to submit to a chemical test and fourth-degree DWI. The trial court denied his motion to suppress. He was convicted of the charges. On appeal, the court concluded that the second encounter between defendant and the officer was a separate stop. The officer's second stop of defendant was not based on a reasonable, articulable suspicion of criminal activity. Other than defendant's apparent difficulty in rolling down his car window, which could indicate unfamiliarity with the car, the officer articulated no facts to support a suspicion that the car had been stolen. Before the second encounter, the officer had not smelled alcohol or asked defendant whether he had been drinking.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions. The court granted the State's motion to strike.

 

1702 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moehlenbrock


A06-2161


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1059



October 23, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
St. Louis County District Court File Nos. CR-06-428, 05-1819, 05-824, 05-290, 05-1884, 06-1099. Hon. Gary J. Pagliaccetti.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota), which sentenced him to 98 months in prison after guilty pleas were entered to the charges of fleeing a police officer in a motor vehicle, driving after cancellation, and two felony counts of driving while impaired (DWI).


OVERVIEW: After entering guilty pleas to several charges, defendant sought a downward dispositional departure. The motion was denied, and a sentence of 98 months in prison was imposed. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that, because the amended statute had come into effect before defendant was sentenced, he was entitled to application of the amended language set forth in Minn. Stat. § 169A.28, subd. 1(b) (2006). However, concurrent sentences were not mandated by the language of the amendment; the district court retained discretion to impose consecutive sentences. Next, the district court considered the Trog factors when it denied the request for a downward dispositional departure; it cited to defendant's lack of cooperation, his remorse, and his attitude. Defendant had shown that he was not amenable to probation due to previous attempts at treatment, and his mild mental illness was not a justification for a mitigated sentence. He did not present proof that his prior DWI convictions were unconstitutionally obtained, and a misstatement regarding the number of past DWI convictions did not play a part in the sentencing.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1703 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Unger v. County of Dodge


A06-1771


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1033



October 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Unger v. County of Dodge, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 27 (Minn., Jan. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dodge County District Court File No. 20-CV-05-400. Hon. Lawrence Agerter.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of the decision of the Dodge County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent county and denied a conditional use permit (CUP).


OVERVIEW: On appeal from summary judgment in a mandamus action challenging the denial of a CUP, the appellate court affirmed. The board of adjustment (board) determined that the evidence did not establish that the applicant's nonconforming use of the land continued for the relevant period. Additionally, the zoning ordinance was not void for vagueness. Further, it was uncontroverted that the applicant did not seek rezoning. And the board determined only that the applicant had discontinued his use of the property as a salvage yard and, therefore, lost his non-conforming-use status. The board's decision did not constitute a taking. The board's action did not deny the applicant residential or recreational uses of the property. If the applicant sought to rezone the property so that he could operate a salvage yard lawfully and the county denied the rezoning request, the applicant might have a cognizable takings claim. But the narrow decision by the board that the applicant had discontinued his use of the property as a salvage yard was not a taking. Thus, the appellate court affirmed on other grounds the district court's entry of summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1704 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Heinonen v. Student Experience LLC


A06-2023


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1043



October 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Department of Employment and Economic Development File No. 1058 06.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action against respondents, an employer and the Minnesota Department of Employment and Economic Development, relator employee sought certiorari review of a decision of an unemployment law judge (ULJ) that she quit her employment and therefore was disqualified from receiving unemployment benefits under Minn. Stat. § 268.095, subd. 1(1) (2005).


OVERVIEW: Relator worked as a personal-care attendant for an organization that typically employed only students. Relator, a non-student, was hired under a unique arrangement to provide care for her 16-year-old developmentally disabled granddaughter. Relator never worked for any other clients. When the Minnesota Department of Human Services terminated the child's medical-assistance funding, relator as a nonstudent, was no longer qualified for employment. Later, the employer lifted its restriction against nonstudents being employed as personal-care attendants, but did not communicate this change to relator. The ULJ misconstrued the law when it determined that relator was disqualified from receiving unemployment benefits based on her failure to ask the company if she could serve any of its other clients. Because a reasonable employee in relator's position would have believed that she was no longer allowed to work for the employer, relator was discharged from employment and not disqualified from receiving unemployment benefits.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1705 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Larson


A06-623


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1034



October 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Larson, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 804 (2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Larson v. Roy, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 90626 (D. Minn., Apr. 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Carlton County District Court File No. CR-05-991. Hon. Robert E. Macaulay, Jr.
State v. Larson, 2006 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 235 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Carlton County District Court (Minnesota) of failing to register as a predatory sex offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction because he could not be convicted for his failure to register because his prison case worker asked him to sign a change-of-information form rather than an actual registration form. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant was not convicted for failing to sign the form presented but for refusing to comply with his duty to register. Defendant acknowledged that his case worker repeatedly informed him of his duty to register as a sex offender, but he repeatedly refused to comply with any registration requirement. The fact that a prison official presented defendant with the wrong form did not establish that the State introduced insufficient evidence of his failure to register. A senior official with the predatory-offender registration unit testified that defendant had never registered, and defendant was reminded at least four times while incarcerated of his duty to register. That defendant continuously refused to provide any required information or otherwise facilitate registration supported his conviction despite the erroneous form.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1706 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gauster


A07-0488


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1024



October 9, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Motion granted by State v. Gauster, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 764 (2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Gauster, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 322 (Minn., July 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Otter Tail County District Court. File No. K9-06-1650. Hon. Steven J. Cahill.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Minnesota sought review of an order from the Otter Tail County District Court (Minnesota), which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence from an inventory search of his vehicle after it was impounded. Charges against defendant were dismissed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sitting in a parked car on a rural highway. An officer stopped to offer assistance. The officer decided to impound the vehicle based on defendant's inability to drive it, given the lack of proof of insurance and defendant's suspended driver's license. During an inventory search associated with impoundment, the officer found a glass pipe with drug residue. The officer also found two packages methamphetamine in the trunk. Defendant was charged with two first-degree controlled substance crimes. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress the evidence from the search of the vehicle. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in its determination that defendant's rights under the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution were violated. Because defendant could not demonstrate that his vehicle was insured, it could not be driven by him or anyone else under Minn. Stat. § 169.797, subd. 2 (2006). The State provided the trial court with the sheriff's department policy on inventory searches. There was no suggestion, much less any evidence, that the officer acted in bad faith or for the sole purpose of investigation by his course of conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for trial.

 

1707 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Papineau


A06-1505


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1017



October 2, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Papineau, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 778 (Minn., Dec. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 06029150. Hon. Daniel C. Moreno.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's motion to suppress was denied, she submitted the case under the Lothenbach procedure. The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of second-degree driving while-impaired (DWI), and she appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant argued that the arresting police officer lacked sufficient reasonable, articulable suspicion to ask for her driver's license and insurance information after a vehicle accident. She also contended that a portion of the implied-consent statute was unconstitutional. The appellate court disagreed, finding no indicia of a seizure in the record; the officer never blocked or obstructed defendant's vehicle; he never activated any emergency equipment; he never told defendant not to leave; and his purpose for coming back to her vehicle after he had walked away was to obtain information for an accident report he was obliged to complete. The reasonable person in defendant's position would not have concluded that she was not free to leave; thus, no seizure occurred. And even if it was determined that she was seized, the officer had a reasonable, articulable basis for the seizure based on the totality of the circumstances, which provided the officer with an objectively reasonable basis for to seize defendant to investigate a possible charge of careless driving. And Minn. Stat. § 169A.20, subd. 2 (2004) did not unconstitutionally deny defendant's U.S. Const. amend. IV rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1708 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cannedy


A06-979


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1013



October 2, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Cannedy, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 802 (Minn., Dec. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 05054934. Hon. Katherian D. Roe.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his motion to suppress and convicted him of being an ineligible person in possession of a firearm in violation of Minn. Stat. § 624.713, subd. 1(b) (2004).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for being an ineligible person in possession of a firearm, arguing that because he was unlawfully detained in the back seat of a squad car after law-enforcement officers stopped his car, the district court erred by not suppressing the gun, magazine, and ammunition that were found in his car during that detention. The appellate court affirmed however, concluding that the challenged evidence was not discovered as a result of defendant's detention in the squad car. Defendant did not dispute that the stop of his car was lawful, and he conceded that the officers were likely justified in asking him to step out of his car. That concession was supported by caselaw. Because discovery of the gun did not result from the fact that defendant was sitting in the squad car, but from the fact that he was not sitting in the driver's seat of his own car, the appellate court agreed that the gun and accessories were not discovered as a result of defendant's detention in the squad car.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Martinez v. Martinez


A06-1715


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1003



September 25, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Washington County District Court File No. F5-04-05431. Hon. Gregory G. Galler.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Washington County District Court, Minnesota, dissolved appellant husband's marriage. The district court ordered him to pay monthly child support and maintenance. The district court denied the husband's motions. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband argued that the district court erroneously denied, deferred, or failed to decide his motions. The appellate court deemed the majority of the husband's issues waived where he did not cite a single statute, rule, or case to support his assertions of error. However, the district court did not rule on the husband's motions demanding access to the county's files. The requirement that the husband pay respondent wife's attorney fees before filing future motions was too broad because it precluded potentially legitimate motions bearing on the welfare of the parties' minor child or otherwise relating to dissolution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for the district court to consider the husband's motions demanding access to the county files and to modify the requirement that the husband pay the wife's attorney fees before filing future motions.

In re Civ. Commitment of Lentz


A07-670


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1009



September 25, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Olmsted County District Court File No. 55-P1-05-005138. Hon. Jodi L. Williamson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a civilly committed individual, sought review of the decision of the Olmsted County District Court (Minnesota), which committed him as a sexually dangerous person.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had been charged and convicted of various sexual offenses and he currently appealed from his commitment as a sexually dangerous person. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that the district court made sufficient findings to sustain its conclusion that he engaged in a course of harmful sexual conduct under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 7a(a) (2006), when it concluded that his 1991 sexual-conduct conviction was based on an act of harmful sexual conduct. The district court specifically found that appellant's three indecent-exposure convictions posed a substantial likelihood of emotional harm. The appellate court agreed with the conclusion that appellant's three convictions of interference with privacy constituted harmful sexual conduct. The record also showed that a doctor applied all six of the Linehan I factors and concluded that there was a high likelihood that appellant would reoffend under § 253B.02, subd. 18c(a)(3) (2006). Further, the Minnesota Supreme Court had determined that civil commitment did not violate a person's right against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1711 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Civ. Commitment of Mosby


A07-755


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1007



September 25, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civil Commitment of Mosby, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 739 (Minn., Nov. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-MH-PR-05-816. Hon. H. Peter Albrecht.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient appealed the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) that ordered his indeterminate commitment as a sexually dangerous person and a sexual psychopathic personality.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued, inter alia, that the district court erred by ordering his commitment because he did not pose a high risk to reoffend. The court of appeals disagreed. In addition to the actuarials and tests, the examiners considered the patient's demographic factors, extensive history of sexual misconduct, diagnoses, and lack of successful treatment. Although the patient's history of sexual misconduct was not directly reflected in his convictions, he admitted to five sexual assaults involving manipulation and violence. The assaults, some under the influence of drugs, some not, were characterized by gratuitous violence and humiliation of the victims. One examiner noted that the patient's "entrenched pattern of sexual deviance most likely continues to date." The patient continued to be an untreated sex offender and his age did not mitigate the high likelihood that he would reoffend due to his history and psychopathy. Therefore, the district court had clear and convincing evidence supporting its determination that the patient was highly likely to reoffend and should be committed as a sexually dangerous person.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1712 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crowell


A06-876


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1010



September 25, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Crowell, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 777 (2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Crowell v. Fabian, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 105944 (D. Minn., Oct. 16, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. K2-05-2092. Hon. Elena L. Ostby.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of two counts of first-degree criminal sexual conduct. The court granted the State's motion to sentence defendant to 302 months in prison, a double upward durational departure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree criminal sexual conduct. The victim was his 10-year-old stepdaughter. On appeal, he claimed that the trial court abused its discretion by precluding his counsel from asking hypothetical questions during voir dire that were intended to determine whether potential jurors gave more credence to police officers than to ordinary citizens. The court found that the trial court acted within its discretion under Minn. R. Crim. P. 26.02, subd. 4(1). The potential jurors, upon counsel's examination, indicated their willingness to decide the case on its merits, giving credence to those witnesses who were believable. Because the content of the victim's statements to an officer was consistent with her trial testimony and the statements bolstered her challenged credibility, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by admitting the statements under Minn. R. Evid. 801(d)(1)(B). The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the victim's videotaped statement given to a nurse at a hospital because the statement was made for the purpose of medical diagnosis and treatment, consistent with the requirements of Minn. R. Evid. 803(4).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Kinley v. Kinley


A06-865


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 963



September 18, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Peck v. Kinley, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 104299 (D. Minn., Sept. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Ramsey County District Court File No. F1-96-163. Hon. Gary W. Bastian.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a child custody dispute between appellant father and respondent mother, the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) granted the mother sole legal custody of the children, prohibited the father from discussing "inappropriate" religious topics with the children, and denied the father's subsequent motions. The father appealed, alleging that the order violated his rights under the First and Fourteenth Amendments.


OVERVIEW: Evidence in the record tended to indicate that the mother was concerned with the father's use of religion as a tool to manipulate her and the children. The district court restrained the father from discussing "inappropriate" religious ideas in the children's presence or telling them stories or teaching lessons from the Bible. The appellate court determined that although the district court had the authority to place restrictions on the father's religious discussions with his children under Minn. Stat. § 518.003, subd. 3(a) (2006), the order impermissibly burdened his right to free exercise of religion because (1) the district court did not make specific findings indicating that he threatened to subvert her choices regarding the children's religious upbringing, and (2) the language of the order was imprecise and not sufficiently limited. Regarding the content-based restriction on the father's free-speech rights, although the order served the compelling state interest of the best interests of the children, the order was constitutionally infirm because it was not narrowly tailored to fulfill that interest. Also, the order was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed, remanded, and ordered the district court to make specific findings before placing limitations on the father's communication with the children.

In re Conservatorship of Hopkins


A06-1818


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 980



September 18, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Conservatorship of Hopkins, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 781 (Minn., Dec. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-P8-97-1381. Hon. H. Peter Albrecht.
In re Conservatorship of Hopkins, 2005 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 16 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, conservatee, challenged the order of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, discharging respondent, conservator.


OVERVIEW: In 1997, the district court appointed the conservator as co-guardian of the conservatee and sole conservator of the conservatee's estate. In May 2004, the district court granted the conservator's petition to sell real estate. In May 2006, the district court filed an order for termination of guardianship and conservatorship, finding that a guardian or conservator would not be of any further assistance. After the conservatee refused to sign the check for the remaining balance issued by the conservator, the conservator placed the remaining $ 473.83 balance in the conservatee's trust account at the center where she resided. The appellate court ruled that the district court did not abuse its discretion. The conservator strictly followed the statutory requirements for terminating the conservatorship under Minn. Stat. § 524.5-431 (2006), and the district court accepted the receipt for discharge filed by the center, even though its termination order requested a receipt from the conservatee. While the conservatee believed she was unjustly deprived of her home, she could not thwart the discharge of the conservator when the statutory requirements for discharge have been fulfilled.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

1715 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Berry


A06-1104


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 901



September 4, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Berry, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 693 (Minn., Nov. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 03061085. Hon. Marilyn Brown Rosenbaum.
State v. Berry, 2005 Minn. App. LEXIS 455 (Minn. Ct. App., May 3, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pleaded guilty to two counts of first-degree burglary, the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, imposed sentences of 120 and 60 months to be served consecutively. On appeal, the case was remanded for resentencing. On remand, the the State's motion to empanel a jury for purposes of the departure issues was granted. The district court found three aggravating factors and reimposed its original sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant raised several issues challenging his sentence. The appellate court found that contrary to defendant's assertion, the 2005 amendments to Minn. Stat. § 244.10, subd. 5(a) (Supp. 2005), and the former version of Minn. Sentencing Guidelines II.D authorized the district court to impanel a sentencing jury on sentencing of a conviction obtained before the act's effective date and to use the jury's findings to impose a new sentence, including, where appropriate, an aggravated sentence. Furthermore, the retrospective application of the 2005 amendments to § 244.10, subd. 5(a) was not prohibited as an ex post facto law, the use of a sentencing jury to consider aggravating factors in the resentencing hearing did not violate double jeopardy, and the district court properly exercised its inherent judicial authority when it empaneled a sentencing jury to apply the dangerous-offender statute in conformity with Blakely. By virtue of defendant's waiver to his right to a sentencing jury and agreement of the existence of aggravating factors, he also granted the district court the authority to make the "severity" finding with respect to aggravating factors.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Stillwater v. Kilbourne


A06-1815


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 907



September 4, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Stillwater v. Kilbourne, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 721 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Kilbourne v. Stillwater, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 3980 (U.S., May 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Washington County District Court File No. C4046764. Hon. John Edward Cass.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, property owner, challenged the judgment of the Washington County District Court, Minnesota, granting summary judgment in favor of respondent, City of Stillwater (the City), in the City's declaratory judgment action, declaring that the owner was in violation of the City's zoning code and granting injunctive relief directing the owner to return the property to the use permitted under the City's zoning code.


OVERVIEW: The owner's property was zoned RB-2, under which a dwelling occupied by not more than two families was permitted, and accessory buildings could not be designed or used for human habitation. After an inspection revealed three separate dwelling units in the house on the property and a fourth dwelling unit above the garage, the City brought a declaratory judgment action for a declaration that the property was not in conformance with the zoning code and for injunctive relief to compel the owner to restore the property to its permitted use. The owner alleged that her use of the property had been permitted by the City, asserting that storm-sewer pipes located on her property had made a portion of the property unbuildable and unusable, as evidenced by the City's refusal to issue building permits to build in the location of the pipes, constituting an unconstitutional taking. The appellate court ruled that the evidence was undisputed that denial of the permit applications did not deprive the owner of residential or rental use of the property, or prevent other remodeling of the dwelling that did not increase the size of the footprint.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hicks v. Dakota County Cmty. Dev. Agency


A06-1302


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 873



August 28, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Hicks v. Dakota County Cmty. Dev. Agency, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 707 (Minn., Nov. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota County Community Development Agency.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Dakota County Community Development Agency (CDA) terminated relator recipient's housing assistance because she failed to report an additional person had moved into her housing unit. The hearing officer upheld the termination of housing assistance. The recipient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The recipient argued that the hearing officer's determination that she violated CDA's policy regarding changes in household size was unsupported by substantial evidence. The appellate court found that the hearing officer failed to make any findings of fact. The record did not support a finding that no request was made prior to February 2006, because there was no testimony about the dates of the recipient's oral requests. Implicit in the decision was a conclusion that the recipient's niece was actually living with the recipient from September 2005, despite the testimony of the recipient and her niece that this was not true and the testimony of the recipient's social worker that she did not see the niece on any of her twice-monthly visits. The hearing officer did not explain why this testimony was rejected. The hearing officer's failure to even consider mitigating circumstances was a failure to consider an important aspect of the case, given the nature of the violation, the degree of the recipient's culpability, or the effects of termination of assistance on the recipient's children, who were not involved in any violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.
