State v. Washington


A06-932


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 889



August 28, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Washington, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 695 (2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Washington v. Benson, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28344 (D. Minn., Apr. 6, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Washington v. State, 2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1288 (Minn. Ct. App., Dec. 15, 2009)
Decision reached on appeal by Washington v. State, 2013 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 283 (Minn. Ct. App., Apr. 1, 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at Washington v. State, 2014 Minn. App. LEXIS 34 (Minn. Ct. App., Apr. 7, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Chisago County District Court File No. CR-04-137. Hon. John R. McBride.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Chisago County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of fourth-degree, third-degree, and second-degree assault and attempted first-degree assault against a peace officer, and sentencing him to an upward durational departure sentenced of 96 months without the possibility of supervised release.


OVERVIEW: Defendant assaulted a correctional officer. Defendant threw hot liquid in the officer's face and struck the officer with his fists. As the officer attempted to flee, defendant chased him and continued to punch him. Defendant returned to his cell and retrieved a knotted sock that contained 24 AA batteries that were taped together. Defendant walked toward the officer holding the sock, but when he saw several officers approaching him, he dropped the knotted sock and placed his hands on the wall, where he was handcuffed by correctional officers. The appellate court ruled that the district court's finding that defendant intended to commit first-degree assault was supported by sufficient evidence. After throwing the scalding water and repeatedly punching the officer, defendant retrieved the battery-filled sock and proceeded toward the officer with it in his hand. Defendant dropped the sock only when numerous correctional officers approached. Also, the district court erred by convicting defendant of third and fourth-degree assault in addition to second-degree assault. Furthermore, the district court did not err in sentencing defendant without the possibility of supervised release.


OUTCOME: The convictions of third-degree and fourth-degree assault were reversed and vacated, and the remaining convictions and sentence were otherwise affirmed.

State v. Bjork


A06-809


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 840



August 21, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Bjork, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 697 (Minn., Nov. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Olmsted County District Court File Nos. K5-03-4098, K7-04-3870. Hon. Robert Birnbaum.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From different files, the Olmsted County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of fleeing a peace officer, obstructing legal process, first-degree test refusal, gross-misdemeanor driving after cancellation, and first-degree driving while impaired. Defendant sought and received downward dispositional and durational departures for some of the convictions, but not others. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that the district court erred in its determination of his sentences for both obstructing legal process and first-degree driving while impaired; Minn. Stat. § 609.035, subd. 5 (2002) was unconstitutional; and the criminal-history score exaggerated the seriousness of the offenses. The appellate court agreed that the district court erred in sentencing defendant for obstructing arrest/legal process as defendant was trying to escape from an officer for a crime for which he was stopped; this was generally considered to be part of the same behavioral incident. Defendant failed to meet the heavy burden of demonstrating beyond a reasonable doubt that the statute was unconstitutional as he argued in generalities and failed to explain why the statute was cruel or unusual in this case. The district court ordered downward durational departures on the sentences for refusal to test and first-degree driving while impaired because it was concerned about not exaggerating the criminality of the offense. The district court did not abuse its discretion here, as these were defendant's fifth and sixth impaired-driving convictions.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence for obstructing arrest/legal process was vacated; otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

 

1720 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walker


A06-470


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 849



August 21, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Walker, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 698 (Minn., Nov. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 05042063. Hon. Stephen C. Aldrich.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of first-degree burglary. Based on the jury's finding of the aggravating factor that defendant acted with particular cruelty, the district court departed upwardly from the presumptive sentence and sentenced defendant to 108 months' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the district court abused its discretion by admitting evidence of a past conviction, the district court was not authorized to impanel a sentencing jury, and the district court erred by not defining "particular cruelty" for the jury. Applying the Jones factors, the appellate court concluded that the district court did not abuse its discretion by admitting the prior-conviction evidence; use of the "whole person" rationale was well established by caselaw, and under that rationale, defendant's prior conviction had impeachment value. Further, the district court had inherent judicial authority to comply with Blakely by seeking a jury finding regarding whether an aggravating factor existed, regardless of the fact that the sentencing guidelines had not yet been modified to provide for such a procedure. However, the appellate court also found that the district court's omission of a definition of "particular cruelty" was plain error, and that error contributed to defendant receiving a sentence that was an upward departure from the presumptive sentence, thereby affecting his substantial rights.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was reversed and remanded for resentencing.

In re Civ. Commitment of Christenson


A07-680


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 864



August 21, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Steele County District Court File No. P6-05-1609. Hon. Lawrence T. Collins.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State filed a petition to commit appellant patient civilly as a sexually dangerous person. The Steele County District Court, Wisconsin, entered an order for indeterminate civil commitment as a sexually dangerous person. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient contended the district court erred by concluding that the State clearly and convincingly proved that he met the statutory criteria for commitment under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18c(a) (2006). The appellate court disagreed, finding that the reports and testimony of the State's witnesses established that the patient's conduct created a substantial likelihood of serious emotional harm to another and was, therefore, harmful sexual conduct within the meaning of the commitment statute. Further, and based on the Linehan factors, both experts concluded that the patient was highly likely to reoffend. The district court credited the experts' testimony, including their opinion that certain tests might underestimate the risk of recidivism. The experts' reports and testimony clearly and convincingly supported the district court's determination that the patient was highly likely to engage in future harmful sexual conduct. The court-appointed examiners' reports and testimony, and the patient's extensive history of sexual offenses, supported the district court's determination that the patient lacked adequate control over his sexual impulses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1722 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Welfare of D.J.M.


A06-1386


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 824



August 14, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
St. Louis County District Court File No. 69VI-JV-05-177, J4-01-150359. Hon. Terrence M. Aronson.
In re Welfare of D.J.M., 2006 Minn. LEXIS 888 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The St. Louis County District Court, Missouri, adjudicated appellant juvenile delinquent on three counts of criminal sexual conduct and consolidated the disposition of these offenses with a probation-violation hearing on a previous sexual offense. Appellant's stay-of-adjudication request was denied, and he was ordered to 120 days of inpatient sex-offender treatment, two years of probation, and to register as a sex offender. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, appellant contended, inter alia, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. The appellate court agreed, finding that appellant's attorney advised the trial court that he had a conflict of interest because of his relationship with the mental health center as a board member; appellant's counsel then proposed a way around the conflict that the trial court permitted. While appellant's counsel's efforts to neutralize the conflict were motivated by his intent to try to help appellant by continuing his representation and not requiring appellant to work with a new attorney, the appellate court found that in attempting to evade the conflict, appellant's counsel "actually affected" the representation. An attorney unaffiliated with the mental health center would have been free to contest the allegation that appellant did not sufficiently participate in treatment at the mental health center; instead, the attorney's conflicting obligations effectively sealed his lips on crucial matters. That appellant's attorney actively avoided the issue due to his conflict resulted in a violation of appellant's U.S. Const. amend. VI rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for a new probation-violation hearing.

 

1723 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Winston v. Minneapolis Pub. Hous. Auth.


A06-1641


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 788



August 7, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Minneapolis Public Housing Authority.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After discovering that relator tenant participated in a check-forgery ring and had a misdemeanor weapons conviction, respondent Minneapolis Public Housing Authority (MPHA) terminated her section-8 rental assistance under 24 C.F.R. pt. 982. A hearing officer determined that the MPHA did not present sufficient evidence to deny rental assistance benefits and reversed, but the MPHA overturned the hearing officer's decision. The tenant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the tenant argued that the MPHA improperly overturned the decision of the hearing officer and that her alleged involvement in criminal activity was an insufficient basis for terminating her assistance. The appellate court agreed, holding that the MPHA's assertion that it was required to prove by a preponderance of the evidence only that the tenant was involved in criminal activity was based on an incorrect interpretation of the federal regulations for terminating rental assistance. To establish grounds for terminating benefits based on the alleged violations of 24 C.F.R. § 982.551, the MPHA needed to show that the criminal activity was either in connection with the housing program or was violent. Here, there was no indication that the check forgery was a crime that was committed in connection with the housing program, or that it was a violent offense. Nor was there evidence that the misdemeanor conviction involved the MPHA. Thus, the MPHA's decision was based on an erroneous theory of law and was not supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1724 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Midwest Oil of Minn., LLC.


A06-1731


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 799



August 1, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Commissioner of Commerce File No. 3-1011-16696-2.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator retail-gasoline-station company appealed from respondent State's imposition of a $ 140,000 civil penalty for violating Minn. Stat. § 325D.71 (2006) that prohibited offering gasoline for sale at a retail price that was lower than a statutory minimum price.


OVERVIEW: The State received complaints that the company was selling gasoline at a price lower than the statutory minimum. On appeal, the company argued that the agency's refusal to consider additional evidence or to grant a rehearing was arbitrary and capricious. The company also argued that the findings were not supported by substantial evidence, and that the statute under which the penalty was imposed was unconstitutional, both facially and as applied to the company. The appellate court agreed with the State that the statute and the applicable rules prohibited the introduction of new evidence after the evidentiary record closed. The documents that company sought to have considered detailed gasoline prices in a metropolitan area, gasoline-terminal prices, and competitors' prices. The documents were evidence, and the parties and the ALJ did not agree to accept this evidence; therefore, it was inadmissible. Consequently, the appellate court concluded that the deputy commissioner's decision not to consider the documents was not arbitrary or capricious. The company did not meet its burden of demonstrating a violation of a constitutional provision.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the decision.

Town of Grey Cloud Island v. Nesvig (In re Petition for Annexation of Land to City of St. Paul Park)


A06-1738


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 776



July 31, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Washington County District Court File No. C2-05-7924. Hon. John Edward Cass.
Minn. Ctr. for Envtl. Advocacy v. City of St. Paul Park, 711 N.W.2d 526, 2006 Minn. App. LEXIS 39 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the real property owner, a developer, and a City, filed a petition seeking annexation of the property by the City. Appellant Town objected to the annexation petition, and a contested agency hearing was held. The administrative law judge (ALJ) issued an order allowing the City's annexation, and The Washington County District Court, Minnesota, affirmed. The Town appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the Town contended the substantial-evidence test for annexation was not satisfied because only about one-quarter of the land in question was buildable and was part of the national park system; and the ALJ's increase in the amount of land to be annexed was contrary to law. The appellate court found that substantial evidence existed to support annexation, including testimony that approximately 116 acres were buildable and that the property was part of a developing community. Furthermore, the Township's board of supervisors admitted that the property was ripe for development and that the urbanization trend was moving south toward the subject property. The City, unlike the Township, was capable of providing the necessary services to the growing population, such as sewer systems, storm-water management and environmental maintenance of the area. However, the appellate court also found that the municipal-boundary procedures under Minn. Stat. § 414.09, subd. 1(e) (2004) for annexing the owner's homestead and "island" lots were not followed in that the hearing was not recessed and notice was not published.


OUTCOME: That portion of the order allowing annexation of the homestead and "island" lots was reversed and remanded for further proceedings; otherwise, the order was affirmed.

Rawlings v. Wash. County Hous. & Redevelopment Auth.


A06-1257


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 710



July 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Washington County Housing and Redevelopment Authority.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After confirming relator tenant's live-in boyfriend's income, respondent Washington County Housing and Redevelopment Authority (Minnesota) terminated the tenant's voucher-program benefits. The tenant requested a hearing, and an informal hearing was administered by a hearing officer. The officer issued a written decision affirming the termination of the tenant's benefits. The tenant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the tenant challenged the Authority's decision to terminate her housing voucher benefits for failure to report her boyfriend's income, arguing that the decision was legally erroneous, was not supported by substantial evidence, and was arbitrary and capricious. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that on more than one occasion the Authority informed the tenant, as the voucher holder, that if her family circumstances changed she was responsible to report that information. Additionally, the tenant was explicitly informed that if her boyfriend began receiving income, the tenant was responsible to report receipt of that income. As such, the officer's legal conclusion that the Authority did not have to establish that the tenant actually knew of the boyfriend's income was correct and was supported by substantial evidence. Further, the officer's written decision sufficiently listed all of the evidence presented at the hearing, which was followed by a decision paragraph explaining why termination of the tenant's rental assistance was warranted, and the tenant did not prove that her disabilities precluded her from complying with reporting requirements.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Cox


A06-555


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 714



July 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 05018105. Hon. Lucy A. Wieland.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which made an aggravated durational departure from the presumptive sentence for second-degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the second-degree assault of his son's mother. Two days after the assault, the mother was admitted to the hospital after a miscarriage. Currently, defendant appealed from the district court's aggravated durational departure from the presumptive sentence. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that the evidence of the miscarriage was relevant to establish the extent of the attack. Defendant told his son's mother that he wanted to kill her baby and directed his blows towards her abdomen, which supported the determination that a shovel, when used in that context, was a dangerous weapon. The application of the revised version of Minn. Stat. § 244.10, subd. 5 (Supp. 2005) did not amount to an ex post fact violation because the jury determination posed no more onerous a sentence than authorized previously when the statute allowed for a judicial finding of aggravating sentencing factors. The nature of the assault, occurring as it did between the son's mother and father, as well as the proximity of the boy, and the fact that it took place in the mother's zone of privacy, justified an upward sentencing departure under Minn. Sentencing Guidelines II.D.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Henderson v. Dep't of Corr.


A06-1326


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 722



July 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Review denied by Henderson v. Dep't of Corr. Faribault Facility, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 596 (Minn., Sept. 18, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Rice County District Court File No. 66-C3-05-001469. Hon. William A. Johnson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prison inmate brought constitutional claims against respondents, the Department of Correction and department employees (Department), challenging their enforcement of a policy prohibiting inmate-to-inmate property transfers via mail. The Rice County District Court, Minnesota, granted the Department's motion for summary judgment. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the inmate challenged the district court's grant of summary judgment on his constitutional claims against the Department's enforcement of a policy prohibiting inmate-to-inmate property transfers via mail. The appellate court found that the policy prohibiting inmate-to-inmate property transfers was rationally connected to the legitimate concern of maintaining a safe and secure institution. Further, he policy did not deprive prisoners of all means of expression, and alternative means of communication between prisoners existed. The Department's assertion that accommodating inmate-to-inmate property transfers would significantly burden prison mailroom staff, require additional resources to implement, and potentially endanger prison inmates, satisfied the reasonableness test. The appellate court concluded that the Department policy prohibiting inmate-to-inmate property transfers had a reasonable relation to the Department's valid interests in maintaining prison security. And as applied here, the policy did not unconstitutionally infringe upon the inmate's U.S. Const. amend. I rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Mower County v. Heimer


A06-1345


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 720



July 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by Mower County v. Heimer, 2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 655 (Minn. Ct. App., June 16, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Mower County District Court File No. 50-CV-06-220. Hon. Donald E. Rysavy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, landowners, challenged the order of the Mower County District Court, Minnesota, granting respondent, county, title and possession of property under Minn. Stat. § 117.042 (2006), the "quick-take" condemnation statute.


OVERVIEW: The county wanted to acquire the landowners' property to construct a portion of a bicycle trail. The landowners argued that taking their land to construct a bicycle trail was unconstitutional since a bicycle trail was not a public purpose and the bicycle trail could be constructed on an existing highway right of way. The appellate court ruled that the district court's finding that a bicycle trail should be deemed a public purpose was not clearly erroneous. The landowners cited no authority for their implied assertion that a recreational purpose was not a public purpose. Also, the district court's finding that taking the landowners' property was reasonably necessary to further a public purpose was not clearly erroneous. The district court found that constructing the trail on the landowners' land was necessary to provide a connection with other planned trails and avoid a gap in the trail. The district court also found that since the existing highway was a curvy road with moderate to heavy traffic and lots of trucks, a bicycle trail placed on the right of way would be too narrow and too dangerous, and would not accomplish the goal of providing safe transportation.


OUTCOME: The order was a affirmed.

 

1730 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Straka


A06-1465


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 702



July 10, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Carver County District Court File No. 10-CR-05-9. Hon. Philip T. Kanning.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Carver County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of second-degree driving while impaired and driving after cancellation, inimical to public safety. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant argued that the trial court erred by determining that the officer's warrantless entry into his garage was justified under the hot-pursuit exception to the warrant requirement. The appellate court disagreed, holding that defendant could not defeat the lawful arrest set in motion in a public place by retreating to a private place. Although the officer did not activate his squad car's emergency lights, when he made eye contact with defendant and turned the squad car around, he made a show of authority. Defendant knew the officer was approaching and attempted to evade him. Once the officer made that show of authority and approached, defendant was not permitted to increase his speed and retreat into his home to avoid a lawful public seizure. Because defendant was aware that an officer was approaching, the hot-pursuit doctrine prevented defendant from increasing his speed, entering his garage, and closing his garage door to defeat a public seizure. As such, the trial court did not err by declining to suppress evidence obtained after the warrantless entry into defendant's garage.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Medley v. Ludeman


A07-97


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 705



July 10, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Judicial Appeal Panel File No. AP069006.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient petitioned respondent Commissioner of Human Services for transfer to the department of corrections and full discharge from his civil commitment, and requested a hearing before the special review board (SRB). Upon the SRB's recommendation, the Commissioner denied the patient's petition. The Judicial Appeal Panel (Minnesota) granted the commissioner's motion to dismiss and affirmed the denial. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient argued that the Judicial Appeal Panel erred in determining that he failed to meet his burden of proving that transfer was appropriate. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the patient failed to meet the criteria stated in Minn. Stat. § 253B.18, subd. 15 (2006); the patient failed to complete sex-offender or chemical-dependency treatment and the state hospital where he was committed was the only facility that could meet the patient's treatment needs. Further, the patient continued to be a danger to the public. Based on the results of tests designed to measure the risk of future violence, the examiners determined that the patient scored in the high range level for psychopathy, was at a higher risk for re-offense than most offenders studied in the normative sample, and was more likely to commit a future violent offense than to refrain from committing such an act if released into the community. As such, Judicial Appeal Panel did not err in concluding that the patient failed to establish a prima facie case for discharge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1732 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lyons


A05-546


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 669



July 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Lyons, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 590 (Minn., Sept. 18, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Itasca County District Court File No. K6-02-1097. Hon. Elizabeth H. Martin.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After pleading guilty to aiding and abetting first-degree assault, appellant inmate was sentenced to an upward durational departure of 172 months. The Itasca County District Court, Minnesota, stayed execution of the sentence as a downward dispositional departure. The stay was vacated when the inmate violated his probation numerous times, and the original sentence was imposed. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the inmate contended he was entitled to relief under Blakely, arguing that his plea agreement impermissibly required him to waive his right to review. He also argued that there was insufficient evidence to support the aggravating factor of particular cruelty, and thus the upward durational departure could not be imposed. The appellate court disagreed, holding that although the inmate's appeal waiver presented a reason why he would not have challenged his sentence duration on direct review, it was not sufficient to justify deviation from the bright-line rule for a Blakely analysis. The inmate's argument would have had merit if his appeal waiver made it impossible for him to challenge his sentence on direct appeal. But such a waiver could have been challenged, even on direct appeal. Furthermore, because the inmate pleaded guilty to aiding and abetting first-degree assault, the acts of the others who had aided were attributable to him for sentencing purposes under Minn. Stat. § 609.05, subd. 1 (2000). And the trial court's finding that the assault was a "savage attack" on the victim that occurred over a long course of time supported a finding of particular cruelty.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1733 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Cooper v. State


A06-907


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 676



July 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 05017030. Hon. Kevin Burke.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his postconviction petition challenging a 2005 sentence for felony first-degree driving while impaired (DWI).


OVERVIEW: Appellant's argument that Minn. Stat. § 169A.276, subd. 1(d), violated the double-jeopardy clause failed because appellant was not sentenced twice (appellant was sentenced once to 42 months in prison with a five-year period of conditional release), and the mandatory imposition of conditional release was not unconstitutional. Because appellant had five prior driving while impaired convictions, the five-year conditional release period was required by statute. Further, appellant's sentence did not exceed the terms of the plea agreement. Also, neither Apprendi nor Blakely prevented the district court from imposing the mandatory five-year period of conditional release. Because the five-year conditional release term was mandated by Minn. Stat. § 169A.276, subd. 1(d) (2004), it did not require the district court to make any additional findings of fact. Finally, the terms "supervised release" and "conditional release" were not interchangeable. Minn. Stat. § 244.05, subd. 1, dealt with supervised release, while Minn. Stat. § 169A.276, subd. 1(d), referred to conditional release. The statutes did not conflict because they covered completely different concepts.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

1734 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re County of Otter Tail Bd. of Adjustment


A06-1696


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 691



July 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by In re Decision of Bd. of Adjustment to Deny a Variance to Stadsvold, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 553 (Minn., Sept. 18, 2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by In re Decision of County of Otter Tail Bd. of Adjustment, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 310 (Minn., June 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Otter Tail County District Court File No. C0-05-1901. Hon. Lisa N. Borgen.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners applied for an after-the-fact variance for a structure setback. Respondent board of adjustment denied the request. The property owners challenged the board's denial, under Minn. Stat. § 394.27, subd. 9 (2006). The Otter Tail County District Court (Minnesota) granted the board's motion for summary judgment. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Because the site permit was issued based on inaccurate setback information provided by the property owners, they were required to apply for a variance, and the district court did not err in interpreting the ordinance to require such. The property owners were afforded adequate time to present their argument. Additionally, the board did not have to describe their physical inspection of the property, even though the board did visit the property, because the reason for the denial was clear from the statement that the property owners' structures were "too close" to the lot lines and the road right-of-way, and the dimensions were provided in the application. The property owners' assertion that a "crucial portion" of the transcript was missing was not supported by a review of the entire record. Further, the property owners had not shown a hardship unique to the land. The reason that the structures went up without compliance with the appropriate setbacks was the property owners' failure to properly stake their property lines, which was their responsibility as landowners. The board's denial was not arbitrary or capricious and was supported by a sufficient factual basis.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

1735 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schwich


A06-783


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 663



June 26, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Schwich, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 571 (Minn., Sept. 18, 2007)
Subsequent civil proceeding at State Farm Fire & Cas. Co. v. Schwich, 749 N.W.2d 108, 2008 Minn. App. LEXIS 294 (2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Remanded by Schwich v. State, 2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 766 (Minn. Ct. App., July 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Scott County District Court File No. CR-05-7048. Hon Mary Theisen.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Scott County District Court (Minnesota) of aiding and abetting third-degree murder. The district court sentenced defendant to 150 months in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that there was insufficient evidence to corroborate the accomplice's testimony or to support his conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. There was independent evidence that defendant possessed methamphetamine on the night of the incident. Defendant and the accomplice injected methamphetamine that evening. The victim had a syringe mark on her body and a lethal level of methamphetamine in her system. Defendant's ex-girlfriend testified that defendant told her that the accomplice injected the victim with methamphetamine, and the accomplice admitted that she did so. Defendant told the ex-girlfriend that he had concealed the syringe the accomplice used. That evidence showed that defendant had an association with the victim, and it linked him to the instrumentalities that contributed to her death. There was expert testimony that acute methamphetamine intoxication was a substantial contributing factor to the victim's death. In light of the record, the jury could have reasonably found that defendant's conduct proximately caused the victim's death. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1736 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Huntsman v. Huntsman


A06-1064


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 650



June 26, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by Huntsman v. Huntsman, 2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 83 (Minn. Ct. App., Jan. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Washington County District Court File No. F7-98-2231. Hon. B. William Ekstrum.
Huntsman v. Huntsman, 2001 Minn. LEXIS 172 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The parties' dissolution judgment awarded respondent mother sole physical custody of their child, and set appellant father's child-support and spousal-maintenance obligations. After much litigation, respondent County sought to collect the father's obligations and arrearages, and the Washington County District Court, Minnesota, entered an administrative income-withholding order, which was sent to the father's employer. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the father argued that the income-withholding order was defective, and that not affording him pre-withholding notice deprived him of due process of law. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that none of the federal authorities the father cited stated that pre-withholding notice was required. Further, the Minnesota statutorily required withholding notice was attached to the dissolution judgment, and stated that when Minn. Stat. § 518.6111 (2004) was satisfied, child support could be withheld from income, with or without notice. Thus, not only did the father receive the statutorily required notice, but lack of the notice would not have precluded withholding. The father's attempt to show that he was deprived of due process of law omitted consideration of the mother's interest in prompt receipt of the amounts he owed her and the state's interest in assuring that the father made those payments. And considering that the father's obligations had been the subject of extensive litigation for over six years, it could not be said that he was unaware of the existence of his obligations, or that his obligations had not been the subject of considerable judicial process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1737 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hutchinson


A07-137, A07-138, A07-178, A07-407


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 623



June 19, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File Nos. 06061875, 06070247, 06066882, 06067082. Hon. Allen Oleisky, Hon. Beryl A. Nord, and Hon. Toddrick S. Barnette.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeals, the State appealed from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed charges against four defendants for third-degree controlled-substance crime, sale or aiding and abetting the sale of cocaine in violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.023, subd. 1(1) (2004).


OVERVIEW: Defendants' criminal conduct fell within the fourth-degree statute. They argued that the third-degree statute was unconstitutional as applied because the State had discretion to arbitrarily charge either the more severe third-degree or the less severe fourth-degree offense for the same conduct. The district court dismissed the charges as violations of the equal-protection clause as applied to defendants. On appeal, the court found that the third-degree controlled-substance offense of § 152.023, subd. 1(1) (2004) was more specific than the fourth-degree offense. The Minnesota legislature intended the sale of less than three grams of cocaine to constitute a third-degree, rather than a fourth-degree, controlled-substance crime. Thus, the district court erred in ordering the dismissals and the State properly charged defendants for their conduct under the third-degree controlled-substance statute. Defendants failed to show that their third-degree controlled-substance-crime charges constituted as-applied violations of the federal or state equal-protection clauses.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the action.

 

1738 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schmidt


A06-1042


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 633



June 19, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Scott County District Court File No. 70-2005-00998. Hon. Mary Jean Theisen.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Scott County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of third-degree driving while impaired (DWI).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for DWI. After defendant was read the implied consent advisory, defendant agreed to take the intoxilyzer test. The test result indicated an alcohol concentration of 0.12. Defendant moved to suppress the alcohol test results, and the district court denied the motion. Defendant argued that the district court erred by not suppressing evidence obtained after he was read the implied-consent advisory. Defendant argued that the ruling by the Minnesota Supreme Court in Fedziuk required that any evidence obtained under the implied-consent statute between the purported effective date of the 2003 amendments and the decision was inadmissible in a criminal proceeding. The appellate court disagreed on the phrase "any evidence." The portion of the implied-consent law that was declared unconstitutional by the Fedziuk decision did not have an effect on evidence obtained for a criminal DWI proceeding. The Minnesota Supreme Court was careful to sever only the portion of the statute purporting to delete prompt judicial review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1739 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Halliburton


A06-471


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 596



June 12, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Halliburton, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 525 (Minn., Aug. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Dakota County District Court File No. K7-05-643. Hon. Joseph T. Carter.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by a jury of car theft, fleeing a peace officer in a motor vehicle, giving a false name to a peace officer, and obstructing legal process. The Dakota County District Court (Minnesota) imposed an aggravated durational departure in sentencing, after the jury found the requisite departure factors beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The record supported the determination that defendant was the one who crashed the stolen car. A police officer provided direct eyewitness testimony that she saw defendant leave the stolen car after it crashed and go into a shopping area, and she was later able to identify defendant as the driver of the vehicle. Further, several witnesses said that they saw defendant approach the shopping area from the direction of the accident, and that he was injured, holding a dark coat even though it was cold outside, and acting strangely. Also, because the police officer's testimony established that defendant drove the stolen vehicle, and the owner of the vehicle testified that she did not know or recognize defendant and that she had not given anyone permission to use the vehicle, the evidence was sufficient to support his motor-vehicle theft conviction. Also, defendant's conduct, shown by his prior convictions for financial-transaction fraud, possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, third-degree burglary, theft, fifth-degree controlled-substance crime, motor vehicle theft, and fleeing a peace officer in a motor vehicle, was sufficient to satisfy Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 4.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.

 

1740 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Meridian Servs.


A06-1112


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 595



June 12, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Department of Employment and Economic Development File No. 3370 06.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Minnesota Department of Employment and Economic Development denied relator employee unemployment benefits; an unemployment law judge (ULJ) subsequently determined that the employee voluntarily quit when she failed to report to work for respondent employer and was thus disqualified from receiving unemployment benefits. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the employee challenged the ULJ's denial of unemployment benefits, contending that she had a daily chiropractor's appointment because of her injury, that her appointments explained her absences, that the employer knew about the appointments and refused to accommodate her, and that employer discharged her to end her workers' compensation benefits. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the record supported the ULJ's determination that the employee quit her employment, and that others at the company did not know of the employee's ongoing chiropractor appointments. The employee was told to inform the employer of any appointments, but she did not. The record did support the determination that four people expressly told the employee to report to work as scheduled, and that letters provided to the employee stated that she was scheduled to work. The record supported the ULJ's finding that the employee was stubborn and unjustified in her refusal to return to work; she defiantly refused to leave when she was not to be at work, and defiantly refused to return when she was to be at work. Further, the record established that the ULJ conducted a fair and unbiased hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Thompson


A06-729


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 597



June 12, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Roseau County District Court File No. K9-05-000411. Hon. Donna K. Dixon.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motion to suppress statements or test results, the Roseau County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of third-degree test refusal and fourth degree misdemeanor driving while impaired. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant argued that his conviction of third-degree test refusal under Minn. Stat. § 169A.20, subd. 2 (2004) had to be reversed because the deputy's reading of the implied-consent advisory misled him about the legal consequences of test refusal. The appellate court found that defendant did not raise this issue before the trial court. Because this issue was not raised before the trial court, the factual record regarding the deputy's reading of the implied-consent advisory was insufficient to facilitate review, even if the appellate court was so inclined. Facts critical to an analysis of the implied-consent advisory were not developed, and therefore, it was not in the interests of justice to consider this claim on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1742 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ybarra


A06-1753, A06-1766


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 610



June 12, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Motion denied by State v. Ybarra, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 431 (Minn., July 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Clay County District Court File No. K6051335. Hon. Steven J. Cahill.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized as a result of a search of his apartment was denied, the case was submitted on stipulated facts. The Clay County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of felon in possession of a firearm and imposed a downward durational departure sentence. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the warrant to search his apartment was not supported by probable cause because the application failed to establish a connection between an alleged crime and his apartment. The appellate court agreed, finding that knowledge that a relative of the wife of the suspect (the target of the investigation) lived in defendant's apartment and that the suspect had recently carried bags into the apartment did not give rise to "a fair probability" that drugs would be located in the apartment. The affidavit contained no description of the bags and no basis for suspecting that they contained drugs, and the relative was not alleged to have been connected with drugs. Even when the facts in the affidavit were considered as a whole, there was still no nexus between the suspect's drug activities and the apartment. As such, the warrant was not supported by probable cause and the trial erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress the gun found in his apartment. However, the appellate court agreed with the State that the trial court erred by imposing the downward durational departure sentence as it failed to articulate substantial and compelling reasons to do so.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed.

 

1743 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Enger


A05-2117


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 529



June 5, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 04080840. Hon. Thorwald H. Anderson.
State v. Enger, 2006 Minn. LEXIS 855 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to second-degree arson. The Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) sentenced defendant to the statutory maximum, after finding that he met the criteria set forth in Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 2. The court reversed and remanded the sentence, finding that the dangerous-offender statute was unconstitutional. The Minnesota Supreme Court granted further review, vacated the court's opinion, and remanded for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: The district court's inherent authority to impanel a sentencing jury existed even after the 2005 amendments to Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 2, the dangerous offender statute were passed, as those amendments did not apply to defendant's offense. The district therefore had inherent judicial authority to impanel a sentencing jury, and it could have exercised that authority if defendant had not waived his right to a jury. Also, defendant cited no legal authority holding that due process required that he be informed of the permissibility of sentencing departures at the time he committed the offense. Additionally, the notion that jury sentencing factfinding would have violated the Ex Post Facto Clause was without merit. By its terms, the Ex Post Facto Clause applied to legislation, not to court decisions. Finally, defendant's criminal behavior supported the finding that he was a danger to public safety. Because defendant had four violent crimes, which was twice the minimum required, and because they occurred over a 23-year period, the 120-month sentence was not disproportional to the seriousness of his conduct.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

 

1744 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Warmbold


A06-921


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 556



June 5, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Warmbold, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 530 (Minn., Aug. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Itasca County District Court File No. KX-02-2401. Hon. Daniel A. Tollefson.
Warmbold v. State, 2005 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 347 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree criminal sexual conduct. The Itasca County District Court, Minnesota, imposed a 240-month sentence under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 2 (2002), the dangerous-offender statute, which was a departure from the presumptive 161-month sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that although certain findings established a basis upon which the district court could have found that defendant was a danger to public safety, the district court did not actually find that defendant was a danger to public safety. Defendant asserted that because this finding was not articulated on the record at the time of sentencing, the departure under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 2, must be disallowed and defendant was entitled to be sentenced to the 161-month presumptive sentence. The appellate court disagreed with defendant's argument. The failure to specifically find that defendant was a danger to public safety did not invalidate his sentence under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 2. When sentencing under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 2, it was important to make specific findings that complied with the requirements of the statute, but there was nothing to suggest that Minnesota Supreme Court precedent intended to impose a mandatory requirement for findings that involved a sentence imposed under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 2.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hibbs


A06-986


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 560



June 5, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 06003905. Hon. Mark S. Wernick.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of violating a city traffic ordinance. Defendant appealed the decision from the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota.


OVERVIEW: A police officer testified that, using a radar device, he measured defendant's speed at 66 miles per hour, six miles over the posted speed limit on the portion of interstate highway where defendant was traveling. A second radar test measured defendant's speed at 63 miles per hour. The police officer issued a citation to defendant for violating a traffic ordinance. The district court ruled that defendant was driving his vehicle faster than the posted speed limit. Defendant argued that the evidence did not support the verdict, that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague, and that the district court abused its discretion by admitting into evidence documents that were not produced during discovery. The elements of a violation of Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 474.30, were that the driver (1) started or accelerated a vehicle (2) with an unnecessary exhibition of speed (3) on a public or private way (4) within the city limits. The record was entirely devoid of any evidence that defendant started or accelerated the vehicle with an unnecessary exhibition of speed. To the contrary, the evidence established that defendant decelerated the vehicle from 66 to 63 miles per hour.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1746 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Welfare of H.V.


A06-1214


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 564



June 5, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Winona County District Court File No. J70550309. Hon. Jeffrey D. Thompson.
In re H.V., 2006 Minn. LEXIS 836 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile was adjudicated delinquent in the Winona County District Court (Minnesota), by reason of having committed third-degree criminal sexual conduct. The juvenile appealed, arguing that, as applied to juveniles, the mandatory registration requirement in Minn. Stat. § 243.166, subd. 1(a)(1)(iii) violated the Sixth Amendment, the Due Process Clause, and the separation-of-powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: The court declined the juvenile's invitation to reexamine its prior holding that the registration statute, as applied to juveniles who were adjudicated delinquent for listed offenses without jury trials, did not violate due-process rights. The registration statute was civil/regulatory in nature and did not trigger the constitutional due process and Sixth Amendment rights. Also, because registration was not punitive, it was not a sentence enhancement, and the juvenile's constitutional challenges to the registration statute based on Apprendi and Blakely were without merit. Finally, even if the requirement could have been considered to be a part of the sentence, the registration statute did not violate the separation-of-powers doctrine because the legislature could limit the exercise of judicial discretion in sentencing. The court reissued its invitation to the legislature to reexamine the wisdom of imposing predatory offender registration on all juveniles adjudicated of predicate offenses, particularly in the context of cases in which there was record evidence that the juvenile delinquent was not a sexual predator.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

In re Welfare Of: P. Q. C.


A06-829


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 568



June 5, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Welfare of P.Q.C., 2007 Minn. LEXIS 520 (Minn., Aug. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-JV-06-2746. Hon. Pamela G. Alexander.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile, challenged his delinquency adjudication for attempted simple robbery under Minn. Stat. §§ 609.17, subd. 1 and 609.24 (2004), and the Hennepin County District Court's (Minnesota) subsequent decision to place him on supervised probation.


OVERVIEW: With respect to the six issues raised by the juvenile on appeal, the appellate court found that, although the district court should have held an omnibus hearing, the juvenile failed to object or raise the issue, which created a presumption of waiver, Minn. R. Juv. P. 10.02, 11.02, 12.01. Because the juvenile did not raise his right to testify on the record, there was a presumption that his decision not to testify was made voluntarily and intelligently, Minn. Stat. § 260B.163, subd. 10(a) (2006). Although a photographic lineup was unnecessarily suggestive, the identifications were reliable under the totality of the circumstances. The evidence was sufficient to support the juvenile's conviction. The district court did not violate Minn. R. Juv. P. 15.04(5). However, the district court's order for out-of-home, residential treatment was not supported by sufficient findings, as required under Minn. R. Juv. P. 15.05 and Minn. Stat. § 260B.198, subd. 1(m)(2) (2006), because the findings did not indicate why the placement was in the juvenile's best interests, why his current custodial arrangement was not appropriate, and why the particular placement was appropriate and beneficial.


OUTCOME: The district court's order was reversed and remanded for more detailed findings of fact to comport with § 260B.198(m)(2) and Minn. R. Juv. P. 15.05. Otherwise, the order was affirmed.

 

1748 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thole


A06-973


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 504



May 29, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Vacated by, Remanded by State v. Thole, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 510 (Minn., Aug. 21, 2007)
Review denied by State v. Thole, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 52 (Minn., Jan. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Carver County District Court File No. CR-05-83. Hon. Thomas G. McCarthy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Carver County District Court (Minnesota) denied defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant was convicted of a fifth-degree controlled-substance offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: While on patrol, an officer observed a vehicle with a headlight out. The officer conducted a traffic stop and identified the driver as defendant. After the officer detected the odors of marijuana and burnt methamphetamine coming from inside the vehicle, the officer asked defendant and his passenger to exit the vehicle, and informed them that he was going to conduct pat-down searches for officer safety. Thus, the initial pat search of defendant did not violate his constitutional rights under the Fourth Amendment and Minn. Const. art. I, § 10. Also, probable cause for an arrest existed before the second search. Also, there was probable cause to believe that defendant had committed a criminal activity unrelated to the traffic stop because (1) the officer, who was trained and experienced in detecting drugs by sight and odor, detected the smells of marijuana and burnt methamphetamine coming from inside the vehicle; (2) the officer had personal knowledge of defendant's past narcotics violations; and (3) the pat-down search of the passenger yielded drugs and paraphernalia. Thus, the second search of defendant and the vehicle were valid searches incident to a lawful arrest.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1749 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cregg


A06-1158


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 506



May 29, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Cregg, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 474 (Minn., Aug. 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. 05028880. Hon. Marilyn Brown Rosenbaum.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) of fifth-degree controlled substance offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the probable cause to search his residence had grown stale when the search was executed five days after the warrant was signed. The court of appeals disagreed. On May 4, 2005, a police officer applied for a warrant to search defendant's residence. The district court signed the search warrant on May 5, 2005. On May 10, 2005, police officers executed the search warrant. During execution of the search warrant, defendant arrived home and was searched. Officers found a substance in his pocket that tested positive for cocaine. In his search-warrant application, the officer indicated that he received numerous complaints from anonymous citizens who suspected narcotics trafficking occurring at defendant's residence. A controlled buy was set up within 72 hours of the officer applying for the search warrant and the informant purchased cocaine from defendant. The search-warrant application supported probable cause existing five days after the search warrant was issued because the affidavit showed that defendant was in an ongoing business of selling drugs from his residence. Therefore, the district court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Civ. Commitment of Hilton


A06-2261


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 518



May 29, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Olmsted County District Court File No. P8-04-4347. Hon. Robert Birnbaum.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, Olmsted County, petitioned the Olmsted County District Court, Minnesota, for the civil commitment of appellant, a known sexual offender. The district court granted the petition and committed appellant as a sexual psychopathic personality (SPP) and a sexually dangerous person (SDP) for an indeterminate period pursuant to the Minnesota Commitment Treatment Act (MCTA). This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Sufficient evidence supported appellant's commitment as an SPP, Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18b (2006), and an SDP, Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18c(a), (b) (2006). His commitment as an SPP was supported by clear and convincing evidence. Appellant's past conduct involving sexual assault, kidnapping and rape, and attempted sexual assault established a habitual course of sexual misconduct. Appellant had a demonstrated inability to control his sexual impulses, and expert testimony confirmed that he was unchanged from the time he committed the assaults and thus was dangerous to other persons. Likewise, clear and convincing evidence established that appellant met the criteria for SDP commitment. Appellant did not rebut the statutory presumption that his past conduct, including attempted sexual assault, constituted a course of harmful sexual conduct, Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 7a(b). Experts testified that appellant suffered from a personality disorder, and the record supported a finding that he was likely to engage in future acts of sexual misconduct. Also, appellant did not establish the availability of a suitable, less restrictive treatment program, Minn. Stat. § 253B.185, subd. 1.


OUTCOME: The decision to commit appellant as an SPP and an SDP pursuant to the MCTA was affirmed.

In re Civ. Commitment of Green


A06-2272


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 519



May 29, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Olmsted County District Court File No. 55-P5-05-000119. Hon. Joseph F. Wieners.
State v. Green, 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 814 (Minn. Ct. App., July 25, 1989)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, Olmsted County, petitioned the Olmsted County District Court, Minnesota, for the civil commitment of appellant, a known sexual offender. The district court granted the petition and committed appellant as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) and a sexual psychopathic personality (SPP) for an indeterminate period pursuant to the Minnesota Commitment Treatment Act (MCTA). This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Sufficient evidence supported appellant's commitment as an SDP, Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18c(a), (b) (2006), and as an SPP, Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18b (2006). The record, including expert testimony, established that appellant satisfied the criteria for SDP commitment. Appellant's past actions, including an assault and a sexual assault for which he was imprisoned, as well as 13 sexually related disciplinary infractions he committed while in prison, constituted a course of harmful sexual conduct. Experts testified that appellant suffered from an antisocial-personality disorder, and the record supported a finding that he was likely to engage in future acts of sexual misconduct. There was also strong evidentiary support for appellant's commitment as an SPP. Experts testified that appellant's assault, sexual assault, and numerous sexually related disciplinary infractions constituted repetitive behavior that established a habitual course of sexual misconduct. His recidivism pattern and lack of regard for sanctions showed his inability to control his sexual impulses. Also, appellant did not have a relapse-prevention plan in place, and he did not know what triggered his behavior.


OUTCOME: The decision to commit appellant as an SDP and an SPP pursuant to the MCTA was affirmed.

 

1752 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lewandowski


A06-537


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 471



May 22, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mille Lacs County District Court File No. K6-04-906. Hon. Lawrence R. Johnson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Mille Lacs County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant on four counts of first-degree criminal sexual conduct, and on lesser-included offenses of third- and fourth-degree criminal sexual conduct. Defendant's motions for a new trial and for a downward durational departure were denied, and he was sentenced to 144 months. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the definition of "position of authority" under Minn. Stat. § 609.341, subd. 10 (2004) was unconstitutionally vague, and the trial court erred in instructing the jury on lesser-included offenses. The appellate court found that "position of authority" had previously been determined not to be unconstitutionally vague. Further, defendant was the victim's horseback-riding instructor, fed her and provided her with transportation when she stayed at his farm, and effectively acted as her guardian. For these reasons, and based on the plain language of the statute, defendant held a "position of authority" over the victim within the meaning of the statute. However, the appellate court agreed that the jury instructions and verdict forms confused the jury and deprived defendant of a fair trial, and that this confusion may have resulted in a harsher verdict than might otherwise have been rendered, entitling defendant to a new trial. If the jury had truly understood the relationship between the greater- and lesser-included offenses, it would have found defendant guilty of first-degree criminal sexual conduct or third-degree criminal sexual conduct, but not both.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Mortensen


A06-590


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 472



May 22, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Nobles County District Court File No. K905526. Hon. Jeffrey L. Flynn.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Nobles County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of driving while impaired (DWI) and an open-bottle violation. Defendant was sentenced to 42 months in prison, but execution of the sentence was stayed; he was ordered to serve one year in the county jail and placed on probation for five years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction and the use of his civil license revocation to enhance his conviction violated his due-process and equal-protection rights. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that the testimony of the officers that they observed defendant behind the wheel of the tractor with the keys in the ignition, and that his companion would not have been able to drive or control the tractor from her position in the tractor, supported a finding that defendant was in physical control of the tractor while he was intoxicated. The appellate court also found that defendant was not entitled to have a court-appointed attorney for the civil revocation proceeding because he was not facing any confinement. And contrary to defendant's assertion, Blakely did not apply as it related only to sentencing issues and had no application to the distinction between civil and criminal proceedings or the effect a civil finding might have had on potential criminal sentences. And because Minn. Stat. § 169A.24, subd. 1(1) (2004) did not create any classifications on its face or by inference, defendant's equal protection challenge failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
