State v. Veal


A06-1161


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 487



May 22, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Veal, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 492 (Minn., Aug. 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. 06-009422. Hon. Thomas W. Wexler.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of third-degree driving while impaired.


OVERVIEW: The officer was responding to a citizen's request to investigate loud banging on a locked service door of a saloon in the early morning hours after the saloon was closed for the night, which the citizen, an employee still inside the saloon, considered an unusual and suspicious occurrence. The officer stopped a vehicle to talk with the people to see if they knew what was going on at the saloon. Defendant was the driver of the vehicle. The officer observed signs of intoxication and arrested defendant. The appellate court ruled that the stop did not violate defendant's right to be free from unreasonable government intrusion, and the district court did not err in denying his motion to suppress. The officer stopped defendant on the reasonable suspicion that defendant or his passenger were involved in or had knowledge of reported suspicious activity or were in need of assistance. The office testified that although he had not observed any traffic violations or criminal behavior, he wanted to see if the occupants of the vehicle knew or observed anyone knocking on the back door of the saloon.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1755 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


A06-1891


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 495



May 22, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Thompson, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 476 (Minn., Aug. 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. 06046385. Hon. John Q. McShane.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, suppressing evidence on the ground that the police officers lacked the reasonable, articulable suspicion necessary to stop the vehicle operated by defendant because he did not violate a Minneapolis ordinance that prohibited the needless obstruction of traffic.


OVERVIEW: The officer stopped defendant for obstructing traffic, and later arrested him for driving while impaired. The State argued that defendant violated a Minneapolis ordinance when he entered an intersection even though he could not clear the intersection because the traffic ahead of him was stopped. The district court determined that because defendant entered the intersection legally, he did not needlessly, unnecessarily, or unwarrantedly obstruct traffic. The appellate court ruled that regardless of whether defendant entered the intersection on a green light, it was uncontested that his vehicle obstructed traffic, and the ordinance applied in all circumstances in which a vehicle obstructed traffic needlessly. The officers had a reasonable, articulable suspicion that defendant violated Minneapolis, Minn., Code Ordinances § 466.230 (1991). The ordinance prohibited obstructing traffic needlessly, and it was uncontested that defendant obstructed traffic by entering the intersection when he could not clear it. Defendant's obstruction of traffic was needless, unnecessary, and unwarranted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

1756 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Civ. Commitment Of: Black


A06-2262


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 499



May 22, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Olmsted County District Court File No. 55-P4-05-4534. Hon. Joseph F. Wieners.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State filed a petition for judicial commitment, alleging that appellant patient was a sexual psychopathic personality and a sexually dangerous person (SDP). The Olmsted County District Court, Minnesota, found the patient to be a sexually dangerous person and committed him to the Minnesota Sex Offender Program for an indeterminate period. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient contended there was insufficient evidence to support a finding that he was a SDP, that his civil commitment violated his constitutional right to adequate treatment, and that his civil commitment constituted double jeopardy. The appellate court disagreed, finding that civil commitment was proper even though the patient's harmful sexual conduct took place while he was a juvenile. And contrary to his assertion, the possibility that the patient did not know that his conduct was wrong did not controvert, but in fact supported, his need for treatment. Because the evidence sufficiently supported the conclusion that the inmate had engaged in a course of harmful sexual conduct, had manifested a sexual or mental disorder or dysfunction, and was likely to engage in acts of harmful sexual conduct, the trial court did not improperly determine that there was clear and convincing evidence that he satisfied the criteria for commitment as an SDP. Further, the patient failed to establish that a less-restrictive treatment program would meet his needs. And because civil commitment was rehabilitative, not punitive, it did not violate the double-jeopardy clauses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1757 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Rubey v. Vannett


A05-310


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 447



May 15, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Motion denied by Rubey v. Vannett, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 496 (Minn., Aug. 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Washington County District Court File No. F9-02-4611. Hon. Stephen L. Muehlberg.
Rubey v. Vannett, 714 N.W.2d 417, 2006 Minn. LEXIS 276 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a decision of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota), adopting respondent mother's proposed findings verbatim, granting the mother sole legal and physical custody, awarding the mother attorney fees, excluding the father's expert testimony, accepting the custody evaluator's report, and allocating to the father dependent medical costs. The father also challenged the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 518.17.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother stipulated that they would share joint legal custody. Despite the stipulation, the district court denied joint legal custody without giving any indication that it was not accepting the joint legal custody stipulation until it issued its order. The court held that the district court abused its discretion because the father did not have proper notice that legal custody was at issue. The court also held that the district court erred in awarding conduct-based attorney fees under Minn. Stat. § 518.14, subd. 1 (2004), to the mother because, although the father's attempts to protect his interests were, at times, lengthy and involved, they did not rise to the level of an unreasonable delay. The court further held that the district court erred in awarding need-based attorney fees under § 518.14, subd. 1, because the mother failed to show that she lacked the ability to pay her own fees or that the father had the ability to contribute to the mother's fees. The court held that the district court also erred in excluding the testimony of the father's expert witness because it failed to conclude that the mother would have been prejudiced by the father's late disclosure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded on the issues of custody, attorney fees, exclusion of expert testimony, and the allocation of dependent medical costs. The court affirmed on the issues of the proposed findings and the custody evaluator's report. The court held that Minn. Stat. § 518.17 was not unconstitutional.

State v. Love


A06-7


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 449



May 15, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Love, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 461 (Minn., Aug. 7, 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Love v. Dingle, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 87249 (D. Minn., Oct. 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County District Court File No. K5-05-823. Hon. Paulette K. Flynn.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, sentencing him to 120 months for one count of burglary in the second degree, and 60 months for each of the other four counts of burglary in the third degree, each sentence to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated that defendant had at least five prior felony convictions for purposes of career-offender sentencing under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095 (2004). During the sentencing phase, after hearing evidence regarding defendant's prior robbery and theft-related convictions, the jury found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant committed each of the five instant offenses as part of a pattern of criminal conduct. Defendant challenged his sentence, which was an upward durational departure, arguing that the district court lacked inherent authority to submit aggravating factors to a jury during the sentencing phase of the trial. The appellate court ruled that the district court possessed inherent authority to empanel a sentencing jury to find sentencing factors. The district court bifurcated the trial. After phase one of the trial in which the jury found defendant guilty of five of the six counts with which he was charged, the district court submitted aggravating sentencing issues to the jury during phase two of the trial. The jury found beyond a reasonable doubt that each of these offenses were committed as part of a pattern of criminal conduct.


OUTCOME: The sentences were affirmed.

In re Civ. Commitment of Tallman


A07-58


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 468



May 15, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civ. Commitment of Tallman, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 430 (Minn., July 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. 27-MH-PR-05-1183. Hon. H. Peter Albrecht.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a petition was filed to commit appellant, a sexual offender, as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) and a sexual psychopathic personality, the Hennepin County District Court, Missouri, filed findings of fact, conclusions of law, and an order committing him to the Minnesota Sex Offender Program as a SDP. The district court ultimately issued an order committing the offender for an indeterminate period. The offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that competent evidence, including expert testimony and evidence on the Linehan factors, supported the offender's indeterminate commitment as an SDP because the offender was highly likely to reoffend. Also, the Minnesota SDP Act, Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18c (2004), was not unconstitutional as applied to the offender. Although the act did not distinguish between a recidivist, like the offender, and sexually dangerous offenders, as the act was narrowed by Linehan, it adequately distinguished between the typical recidivist and the dangerous sexual offender and thus complied with substantive due process requirements. The act was not void for vagueness because, taken in context, the act's "adequate control" language related to the offender's history of harmful sexual conduct, his high likelihood of future dangerousness, chemical dependency, and antisocial personality disorder. The offender's civil commitment did not constitute double jeopardy because the act was predominantly remedial, not punitive. Moreover, it was facially civil, and it was not so punitive in purpose or effect to trigger the federal constitutional prohibitions against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment for the indeterminate commitment of appellant was affirmed.

In re Welfare of S.A.W.


A06-914


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 433



May 8, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Goodhue County District Court File No. J3-05-50615. Hon. Karen Asphaug.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged the judgment of the Goodhue County District Court, Minnesota, adjudicating him delinquent for second-degree criminal sexual conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.343, subd. 1(a) (2004).


OVERVIEW: On numerous occasions in 2005, appellant, then fifteen years old, babysat the six-year-old victim. In September 2005, the victim disclosed to her mother that appellant had inappropriately touched her. Viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the State, the appellate court found that there was sufficient evidence to support appellant's adjudication of delinquency for second-degree criminal sexual conduct. The victim offered graphic and disturbing testimony regarding appellant's sexual conduct. Although the district court did not find the victim's testimony credible enough to establish penetration, the testimony was sufficient to support the district court's adjudication. Appellant's proposition that a failure to establish penetration precluded a finding of sexual contact defied logic, as not all sexual contact required penetration. Also, adjudication of delinquency was not a criminal proceeding, nor was predatory-offender registration a punitive sanction. The appellate court has previously rejected challenges to the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 243.166 (2006), the predatory-offender registration statute as applied to juveniles.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Nathan v. Ritchie


A06-1092


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 438



May 8, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County District Court File No. C5-05-010879. Hon. Steven D. Wheeler.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen brought a taxpayer's lawsuit seeking a declaration that respondents, the State and state officials (the State), acted unlawfully in cancelling a service contract for the state's voter registration system. The Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, granted the State's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the action for lack of standing. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The underlying action arose when the State, through its then secretary of state, entered into and later cancelled a service contract with a company to maintain the statewide voter registration system. On review, the citizen argued that he had standing to bring his action as a taxpayer whose tax burden could be increased by illegal spending. The appellate court disagreed, holding that the citizen failed to show that he was the proper party to bring this lawsuit because (1) he failed to show a direct injury distinct from the public's injury; (2) he failed to identify express statutory authority to bring the action; and (3) he failed to show that the State, by its letter of agreement to cancel the original service contract, unlawfully disbursed public money or acted illegally. Neither the citizen nor the legislative auditor report identified "illegal" action. Moreover, the citizen did not challenge the legality of the original contract, which gave the secretary of state's office sole discretion and authority to cancel. The citizen's mere disagreement with that office's cancellation of the contract was insufficient to confer standing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1762 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gillen


A06-26


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 394



May 1, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Meeker County District Court File No. K6-05-163. Hon. Steven E. Drange.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motion to suppress his confession, the Meeker County District Court, Minnesota, convicted him of first-degree burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested when information was obtained from defendant's roommate; the roommate had been arrested on an unrelated outstanding warrant when an informant reported seeing defendant unloading stolen items at the roommate's trailer home. On review, defendant argued that police lacked probable cause to arrest him and used coercive tactics to obtain his confession. The appellate court disagreed, finding that information obtained from various sources directly linked defendant to items taken during that burglary, including a gun that the informant claimed defendant was trying to sell and a boat motor that was found in the defendant's bedroom. Furthermore, information obtained from the roommate was corroborated by other information already held by police. The appellate court concluded that the police had probable cause to arrest defendant because they had facts and circumstances that would have warranted a prudent person to reasonably conclude that defendant had committed a crime. While the investigator's methods were designed to obtain information from defendant, they were not so oppressive as to overcome defendant's will and produce an involuntary admission of guilt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Chan


A06-121


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 402



May 1, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. 05-039767. Hon. Susan N. Burke.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicting her for driving while impaired.


OVERVIEW: At 12:24 a.m., an officer noticed a car parked in front of a convenience store which closed at 9:00 p.m. The officer parked the police car two car-lengths away from the car in the parking lot. Defendant was in the driver's seat of the car and opened her door. He saw orange paint on the car and a dent in the bumper, which looked like fresh damage. Defendant smelled of alcohol, and admitted that she had been drinking. Defendant agreed to take a breath test; based on the results, the officer arrested her. She moved the district court to suppress the evidence of her intoxication, because she was unconstitutionally seized. The appellate court held that defendant was not seized when the officer parked his police car two car-lengths away from her car. Defendant could have backed up and driven out of the parking lot. The district court did not err by denying her motion to suppress the evidence of her intoxication.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1764 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bjergum


A06-139


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 405



May 1, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Lake County District Court File No. KX-03-445. Hon. Kenneth A. Sandvik.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Lake County District Court (Minnesota) of second-degree possession of a controlled substance. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the district court erred by granting the search warrant for his residence because the affidavit in support of the warrant did not provide probable cause. The court of appeals agreed. The affidavit in support of the search warrant did not provide any nexus between the alleged crime and defendant's residence. The affidavit's only mention of defendant's residence was the statement that "during the interview with defendant, deputies learned that he had been living at his mother's residence." The affidavit stated that nine bags of a crystal-like substance were found in defendant's car near where he was sitting and that defendant lived at his mother's home. The affidavit contained no allegations or facts linking the drugs in the vehicle to defendant's residence. Because the affidavit failed to allege any connection between the residence and drug activity, the district court erred by issuing the search warrant. In addition, the prosecutor committed misconduct because opening argument included not only the facts obtained through the suppressed interrogation, but also that defendant had admitted those facts.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed.

State v. Bane


A06-313


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 406



May 1, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Bane, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 401 (Minn., July 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. 05019163. Hon. John L. Holahan.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of a fifth-degree controlled substance offense and felon in possession of a weapon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that the search warrant was issued without probable cause, and statements an unavailable witness made should have been allowed. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that the facts enumerated in the search warrant application supported the issuance of the warrant because recent events associated with the apartment, including the connection of those arrested for drug use and the observance of drug paraphernalia there, established a fair probability that other evidence of drug activity would be found in the apartment. Knowledge that defendant had an extensive criminal history also supported issuance of the warrant. Allowing the unannounced nighttime entry was proper as defendant had a criminal history that included convictions for second-degree murder and drug possession, so officers were reasonably concerned for their safety. Discrepancies in the witness's descriptions of the gun and inconsistencies in identification of the gun's owner justified exclusion of this testimony. Because defendant's sentencing hearing occurred after the effective date of Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 2 (2004), his sentence was authorized by law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1766 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vierling


A06-878


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 370



April 24, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Scott County District Court File No. 2004-15280. Hon. William E. Macklin.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Scott County District Court, Minnesota, convicting her for second-degree driving while impaired (DWI).


OVERVIEW: Police officers arrested defendant on suspicion of DWI. After being read the Minnesota Implied Consent Advisory and afforded an opportunity to consult an attorney, defendant took the Intoxilyzer test, which indicated an alcohol concentration of .18. Defendant moved to suppress the test result. The district court correctly denied defendant's motion. The implied-consent advisory read to defendant did not violate defendant's right to due process. While defendant argued the implied-consent statute was declared unconstitutional in Fedziuk, defendant's reliance on Fedziuk was misplaced. Fedziuk did not render unconstitutional the entire implied-consent advisory; it only struck down the 2003 amendment to the implied-consent statute which dispensed with the judicial-review requirement. The legitimacy of the advisory was never at issue. Defendant did not claim that the lack of judicial review coerced her into submitting to a breath test or otherwise prejudiced her interests.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1767 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Jennings v. State


A06-1185


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 371



April 24, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Jennings v. State, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 419 (Minn., July 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: McLeod County District Court File No. K4-03-1028. Hon. Terrence E. Conkel.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the McLeod County District Court, Minnesota, denying his postconviction motion for correction of his 2003 sentence for kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with kidnapping -- safe release, false imprisonment, third-degree assault, and fleeing a peace officer, after he allegedly kidnapped his wife and her two children. He waived his right to a jury trial and entered an Alford plea to kidnapping -- safe release. The plea agreement called for a 63-month sentence, which was a 12-month upward durational departure from the presumptive guidelines sentence of 51 months. Appellant filed a pro se motion to correct his sentence on the basis that the sentencing departure was unconstitutional pursuant to Blakely. The district court correctly denied the motion, holding that Blakely did not apply because appellant's case was final at the time Blakely was decided. He was not entitled to postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Welfare of: M.T.L.


A06-650


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 375



April 24, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Stearns County District Court File No. J9-05-50777. Hon. Paul E. Widick.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Stearns County District Court, Minnesota, adjudicated juvenile defendant delinquent and ordered him to pay restitution after he pleaded guilty to third-degree burglary. Defendant's request for a hearing to challenge the restitution amount was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant challenged the trial court's acceptance of his guilty plea, and argued that the trial court erred by denying his challenge to the restitution request because he failed to timely comply with the requirements for submitting his challenging affidavit. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that defendant intelligently pleaded guilty and that he never moved the trial court to withdraw his guilty plea. Defendant, his counsel, and one of his parents signed the statement of rights form, the form explained the trial rights afforded to him and that the consequence of pleading guilty included waiving these rights, and defendant confirmed that he had sufficient time to speak with his attorney before pleading guilty. And contrary to defendant's assertion, the victim timely filed the affidavit requesting restitution with the court administrator pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 611A.045, subd. 1(a) (2004). Because defendant failed to comply with the requirements of the statute by not timely filing his affidavit, the trial court properly denied his request for a hearing on that basis.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1769 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gibbs


A06-17


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 383



April 24, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Gibbs, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 404 (Minn., July 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Olmsted County District Court File No. K2-03-3958.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Olmsted County District Court, Minnesota, convicted defendant of first-degree criminal sexual conduct with a child under 13. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the child victim's uncorroborated testimony that defendant sexually abused her was insufficient to support his conviction; and the trial court abused its discretion by declining to conduct in camera review of statements the victim made to victim services and by admitting the victm's videotaped statement to police. The appellate court disagreed, finding that a rational jury could have determined that the victim's testimony regarding it raining on the day of the incident to be credible based on the reasonable possibility that it might rain in March in Minnesota. Although the victim also testified that she did not remember the exact time of year the abuse occurred, her testimony on the details of the abuse was consistent with her videotaped statement to police and her statement to her treating psychologist. The appellate court deferred to the jury's determination of credibility and concluded the evidence sufficiently supported defendant's conviction. Further, the trial court properly exercised its discretion by determining that no victim statements existed in the victim-services records based on the director's testimony and by declining in camera review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1770 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martinelli


A06-564


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 377



April 24, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Martinelli, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 405 (July 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Nicollet County District Court File No. 52CR0573. Hon. Allison Krehbiel-Baskfield.
In re Martinelli, 1998 Minn. App. LEXIS 1060 (Minn. Ct. App., Sept. 15, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Nicollet County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of escape from custody under Minn. Stat. § 609.485 (2004).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was civilly committed to the Minnesota Sex Offender Program as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) in 1998. He was later charged with escape from custody under Minn. Stat. § 609.485, subd. 2(5) (2004). After he was convicted, defendant sought review. In affirming, the appellate court held that § 609.485 did not violate equal protection based on the fact that it allowed persons that had been found not guilty by reason of mental illness or mental deficiency to avoid a felony charge if they returned within 30 days, but did not have a similar provision for a SDP. These two classes were not similarly situated since the commitment criteria were not the same, the treatment was not the same, and the Minnesota Legislature clearly provided that they were dissimilar in certain circumstances. The rational basis test would have been applicable if defendant had been able to show a similar situation. Finally, the use of the necessity defense was properly denied because defendant had not exhausted all available legal remedies, there was no emergency or imminent harm, and the escape did not prevent a harm that would have significantly exceeded the harm resulting from the escape.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Winkelman v. County of Stearns


A06-999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 347



April 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Stearns County District Court File No. C4-05-4483. Hon. Sally Ireland Robertson.
Winkelman v. Stearns County Planning Comm'n, 2006 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 979 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owners, challenged the judgment of the Stearns County District Court, Minnesota, granting summary judgment in favor of respondent, Sterns County (the County), Minnesota, in a declaratory judgment action in which the owners requested certain provisions of the county's amended zoning ordinance be found unconstitutionally vague and subjective, and lacking a rational basis.


OVERVIEW: The owners owned approximately 37 acres of real property located in Agricultural District A-40 in Stearns County. The land was subject to the County zoning ordinance. The owners applied for a construction permit to build a single-family dwelling but were denied by the Stearns County Environmental Services Department. The property was found to have a Land Evaluation Site Assessment (LESA) score of 77.91, thereby requiring a conditional use permit (CUP). The Stearns County Environmental Services informed the owners of the need for a CUP. The owners submitted an application for a CUP to build a single-family residence on the northwest corner of the property. The County denied the CUP as requested but granted a permit on the condition that the owners build the house on the property's northeast corner. The appellate court ruled that when all relevant provisions were read together, the County ordinance was not vague. The ordinance cross referenced and directed a reader to and through the relevant sections and subsections. Contrary to the owners' belief, the LESA system was objective, organized, and clearly identified the criteria considered in reaching a property's LESA score.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1772 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reese


A06-321


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 353



April 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Lyon County District Court File No. K8-05-41. Hon. George I. Harrelson.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Lyon County District Court (Minnesota) convicting him of second-degree controlled substance offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after drugs were found in a vehicle he was driving, which had been towed and impounded because defendant could not show proof of insurance. On appeal, the court held that while the police officer did not impermissibly expand the scope of the initial stop of the vehicle, the impoundment and subsequent inventory search of the vehicle were illegal, and therefore defendant's motion to suppress should have been granted, because the tow of the vehicle was purely pretextual and the police had no legitimate reason to tow the car. Minn. Stat. § 169.791, subd. 2 (2004) was incompatible with the claim by law enforcement that, absent any other circumstances, their departmental policy mandated towing away all cars immediately upon the driver's failure to have his proof of insurance card in his possession. The issuance to defendant of a citation was in line with the statute but not the immediate towing of the vehicle. The officer's claim that the vehicle needed to be towed because it presented a traffic hazard was not supported by the record, and the State failed to provide any documents that it was the department's policy to tow all uninsured vehicles.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed.

 

1773 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mueller


A06-73


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 358



April 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hubbard County District Court File No. K4-04-783. Hon. Paul Rasmussen.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hubbard County District Court (Minnesota) convicted defendant of a third-degree controlled-substance crime. Defendant appealed, arguing that law-enforcement officers, who received a tip from a confidential informant, did not have probable cause to arrest and search him and his car after initiating a stop.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant called the drug task force and told them that defendant would be leaving a bowling alley and driving west with methamphetamine and marijuana in his possession. Presumably a special agent for the task force knew the confidential informant's name because the special agent testified that he had worked with the confidential informant in the past. But there was no indication that the confidential informant had provided reliable information in the past, was making statements against his interest, was voluntarily cooperating with law enforcement, or met with police face to face, any of which could be cited as reasons to credit the confidential informant's tip. Also, defendant's acts of leaving a bowling alley and driving west were innocent activities that became no more suspicious because of the confidential informant's tip. Although the confidential informant's tip was sufficient to establish reasonable suspicion to justify the stop of defendant's vehicle, it was insufficient to establish probable cause to arrest or search defendant and his car under the Fourth Amendment and Minn. Const. art. I, § 10. Thus, defendant's motion to suppress was improperly denied.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1774 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Campbell


A06-539


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 363



April 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County District Court File No. K0-05-566. Hon. Joanne M. Smith.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of first-degree criminal sexual conduct. He also challenged the sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of having sexual contact with his girlfriend's 10-year-old son. During the trial, defendant consented to the State's request to close the courtroom. The district court imposed a sentence of 216 months, which was an upward durational departure. This appeal followed. In partially affirming, the appellate court determined that defendant waived his challenge to the decision to close the courtroom due to his consent given through his attorney. Even so, the constitutional right to a public trial was not absolute, and safeguarding the well-being of a minor victim of sexual assault was an overriding interest that justified the limited closure of a courtroom under Minn. Stat. § 631.045 (2004). As to the sentence imposed, the district court had the authority to submit the aggravating factors to the jury under Minn. Sentencing Guidelines II.D (2004). However, it was error to make an upward departure based on multiple acts or forms of penetration because only a single act of sexual abuse with one form of penetration occurred on the date of the charged offense; other incidents did not arise out of a continuous and uninterrupted course of conduct.


OUTCOME: The sentence was reversed, and the case was remanded for the imposition of the presumptive guidelines sentence. The rest of the decision was affirmed.

 

1775 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bailey


A05-2107


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 306



April 10, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Bailey, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 300 (2007)
Related proceeding at Bailey v. County of Kittson, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 26388 (D. Minn., Mar. 31, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Kittson County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of terroristic threats and fifth-degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from statements he allegedly made to a county court administrator. According to the administrator, defendant was extremely angry and stated "the Judge was driving him crazy," and "Do I have to be another Timothy McVeigh?" The administrator composed a summary of her conversation with defendant and brought it to the sheriff's office. The appellate court disagreed with defendant's assertion that his conviction for terroristic threats must be reversed because the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that his statement was intended to terrorize and was anything more than an expression of transitory anger. There was circumstantial evidence from which a jury could reasonably infer intent to terrorize. The reference to Timothy McVeigh would carry more weight in light of the fact that Timothy McVeigh was convicted of bombing a government building. Considering the context in which the statement was made, the statement, at the least, was made with reckless disregard of the risk of causing terror. However, the conviction for fifth-degree assault was vacated because it was a lesser-included offense of terroristic threats.


OUTCOME: The conviction for fifth-degree assault was vacated, and the judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Aron v. State


A06-389


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 321



April 10, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Aron v. State, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 351 (Minn., June 19, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Aron v. Minn., 2008 U.S. LEXIS 905 (U.S., Jan. 14, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pleaded guilty to aiding and abetting and second-degree assault with a dangerous weapon, the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, accepted his plea and later imposed the negotiated aggregate sentence of 190 months. Defendant's subsequent motion for postconviction relief was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the record was insufficient to support the trial court's determination that his guilty plea to an assault count did not result in manifest injustice. He also argued that the 10-month upward departure based on aggravated factors was unconstitutional because the facts underlying the departure were not determined by a jury beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that the complaint against defendant alleged that his accomplice pointed his pistol at a victim. At his plea hearing, defendant admitted more than once that he participated in the shooting with his accomplice. He also stated that he understood the legal principle of aiding and abetting. The combination of the allegations in the complaint and defendant's testimony provided the necessary link for finding a sufficient factual basis for the charge that he aided and abetted the assault on the victim. The confusion at the plea hearing did not undermine the factual basis for defendant's plea and it did not result in his pleading guilty to a more serious charge. And under current law, defendant's upward departure did not violate his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Royster


A05-2325


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 281



April 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Royster, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 304 (Minn., May 30, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, sentencing him under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 4 (2004), the career-offender statute, to an executed term of 108 months for second-degree burglary.


OVERVIEW: The district court determined that it would submit to the jury the issue of whether defendant's current offense was part of a pattern of criminal conduct within the purview of the career-offender statute. Defendant objected on the ground that the law did not permit a jury to make this determination. The district court overruled the objection. Defendant then moved to impanel a new jury for this proceeding, but the district court denied the motion. Defendant stipulated that his current offense was a felony and that he had five or more prior felony convictions, as required by the career-offender statute. The State then presented evidence of the circumstances of defendant's prior convictions which consisted of two burglaries, one attempted burglary, two receiving stolen goods, and one attempt to offer forged checks, all between 1995 and 2002. The appellate court ruled that the district court had authority to impanel a sentencing jury to determine the aggravating factor of a pattern of criminal conduct under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095, subd. 4 (2004). Also, the record provided no indication that the performance of defense counsel was objectively unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1778 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Loprete


A06-773


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 282



April 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County District Court File No. K9-04-293. Hon. Michael Sovis.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Dakota County District Court, Minnesota, revoking his probation imposed for felony theft.


OVERVIEW: In the instant case, the district court did not expressly recite either the second or third Austin factor. Rather the district court stated it was basing revocation on defendant's admission that he failed to remain law abiding as required by the terms of his probation. Defendant, represented by counsel, actively negotiated and agreed that the district court could revoke his probation and execute his stayed sentence in exchange for lenient sentences on two pending criminal charges and the dismissal of a third charge. The appellate court ruled that because defendant voluntarily admitted to probation violations and agreed to the execution of a stayed sentence in exchange for prosecutorial leniency, the underlying policy reasons for the district court to convey its substantive reasons for revocation and the evidence relied upon did not apply. Also, defendant had the right to have a jury determine any aggravating sentencing factors at the time he made a valid waiver of such rights. Defendant could waive his constitutional right to a jury trial as long as the waiver was knowing, voluntary and intelligent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: The father was convicted of two counts of criminal sexual conduct in May 2001. Jensen v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety


A06-544


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 288



April 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Washington County District Court File No. C7-05-8101. Hon. Judge Gary J. Meyer.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Minnesota Commissioner of Public Safety (the Commissioner), challenged the order of the Washington County District Court, Minnesota, granting the petition for reinstatement of an operating license filed by respondent, driver.


OVERVIEW: The driver was convicted in Wisconsin of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated in June 2004. The driver's operating license was revoked for 30 days beginning June 21, 2005. The driver was later arrested in Minnesota for driving while impaired (DWI). The June 2005 license revocation was used to enhance the DWI charge brought against the driver. In October 2005, the driver filed a petition for a hearing under Minn. Stat. § 171.19 (2004) to determine whether she was subject to license revocation based on the June 2004 Wisconsin conviction. The district court ordered the Commissioner to remove all references to the June 2005 license revocation from the driver's operating record. The appellate court ruled that the driver's petition was untimely, and the district court should not have exercised its jurisdiction to hear the petition. Also, because the driver had an opportunity to assert the claim she was not afforded the right to consult with an attorney prior to testing following her Wisconsin arrest in a timely petition for judicial review, but failed to do so, it was not fundamentally unfair and a denial of due process to not allow her to assert the claim in an untimely petition.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed.

In re Civil Commitment of Semler


A06-2213


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 298



April 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civ. Commitment Of: Raymond Leon Semler, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 285 (2007)
Related proceeding at Semler v. Finch, 2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 696 (2007)
Related proceeding at Semler v. Klang, 743 N.W.2d 273, 2007 Minn. App. LEXIS 163 (2007)
Related proceeding at In re Civ. Commitment of Semler, 2011 Minn. LEXIS 300 (2011)
Related proceeding at In re Civil Commitment of Semler, 2012 Minn. LEXIS 234 (Minn., May 15, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Crow Wing County District Court File No. P5-05-1006. Hon. David J. TenEyck.
State v. Semler, 1998 Minn. App. LEXIS 864 (Minn. Ct. App., July 28, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon respondent County's request to have appellant patient committed as a sexually dangerous person (SDP), the Crow Wing County District Court, Minnesota, found that the patient engaged in a course of harmful sexual. The patient was committed to a secure treatment facility for an indeterminate commitment as an SDP. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient challenged his commitment. The appellate court found that the testimony of several victims, including minors, and two court-appointed experts constituted clear and convincing evidence that the patient engaged in a course of harmful sexual conduct that caused serious physical and emotional harm to the victims. Although the patient had not been convicted of a criminal sexual offense for over 10 years, he had been either incarcerated, on probation, or on intensive supervised release since his the offense. During that time, despite supervision, he had new criminal convictions, developed a chemical dependency problem, and continued to engage in high-risk behavior including accessing pornography, keeping weapons, and drinking. The patient also failed five sexual offender treatment programs. These facts, as well as the experts' opinions, supported the trial court's finding that the patient was highly likely to reoffend sexually. Because the patient failed to sustain his burden of proving that a less-restrictive appropriate treatment program was available, the trial court did not err by ordering his commitment to a secure treatment facility.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lopez


A06-1781


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 300



April 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Douglas County District Court File No. K6-06-198. Hon. Peter Irvine.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the Douglas County District Court, Minnesota, suppressing the cocaine discovered in the trunk of defendant's vehicle and dismissing the complaint against her for first-degree possession of a controlled substance and sale of a controlled substance in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding. Defendant consented to a search of the vehicle, and a search of the trunk revealed a detergent box that contained approximately one pound of a white powder that was later determined to be cocaine. Defendant moved to suppress the cocaine, arguing that the traffic stop was unconstitutionally extended. The district court determined that the facts did not amount to grounds for the reasonable, articulable suspicion necessary to extend the traffic stop, noting that the air freshener and the religious icon depicting the patron saint of narcotics smugglers was not sufficient to indicate contraband, that a messy car was not unusual after a long trip, and that defendant's nervousness was reasonable. The appellate court ruled that the State failed to show that the district court clearly and unequivocally erred. The discrepancies in the statements made by defendant and the passenger were not sufficient to justify a reversal. Also, the religious icon was of limited value in establishing a reasonable suspicion.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

1783 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Fiedler v. City of Osakis


A06-838


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 303



April 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Fiedler v. City of Osakis, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 337 (Minn., June 19, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, claimant, challenged the judgment of the Douglas County District Court, Minnesota, dismissing the claimant's personal-injury action against respondents, city and its employee.


OVERVIEW: The claimant's vehicle collided with a city ambulance. The parties reached a settlement agreement under which the claimant and his wife were each paid $ 300,000. The claimant did not dispute that the plain language of Minn. Stat. § 466.04, subd. 1 and 1a (2006), limited the amount that he could recover from respondents at $ 300,00. The claimant challenged the provision in Minn. Stat. § 466.04, subd. 1a, that excluded professional employees from the limitation. The claimant argued that applying Minn. Stat. § 466.04 to the employee when he had valid private insurance violated equal-protection and due-process. The appellate court ruled that the claimant did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statutory exception, because he had not shown direct, personal harm from the alleged constitutional violation. If the exception were severed from the remainder of the statute, the claimant would be left with a statute that limited respondents' liability at $ 300,000, and respondents had already paid that amount. The claimant would be in the same position whether or not the statutory exception for the liability of professional employees was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Nicolaison v. Ludeman


A06-1969


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 299



April 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Motion denied by, Review denied by Nicolaison v. Ludeman, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 303 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Carlton County District Court File No. 09-CV-06-1087. Hon. Robert E. Macaulay, Jr.
In re Nicolaison, 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 632 (Minn. Ct. App., July 8, 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, patient, challenged the judgment of the Carlton County District Court, Minnesota, denying his petition for writ of habeas corpus requesting discharge from his commitment as a psychopathic personality.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued that the conditions of his confinement were unconstitutional. The district court found that the patient challenged the conditions of his confinement in the Minnesota Sex Offender Program's behavior therapy unit, complaining about the unit's rules, expectations, privileges, restrictions and disciplinary procedures. The appellate court ruled that the district court did not err in concluding that none of the patient's claims were appropriate for habeas corpus review, and that the patient did not allege facts implicating the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. The patient was placed in the behavior therapy unit because of his disruptive behavior, which had to be dealt with to ensure a safe environment for other patients. The restrictions that the patient complained of fall well within Minn. Stat. § 253B.185, subd. 7(b) (2004). The most dangerous and aggressive patients resided in the behavior therapy unit, and its restrictions were related to the legitimate purpose of maintaining a secure and therapeutic environment that adequately protected the patients, the staff members, the public, and the facility.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1785 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grady


A06-228


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 271



March 27, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Grady, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 331 (Minn., June 19, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Grady v. State, 2009 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1260 (Minn. Ct. App., Dec. 8, 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Grady v. Zanders, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 74467 (D. Minn., Apr. 7, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Sherburne County District Court (Minnesota), which sentenced him to 96 months in prison after he was convicted of criminal vehicular homicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his aggravated sentence for criminal vehicular homicide, arguing that the district court relied on improper aggravating factors, ignored significant mitigating factors, and imposed a sentence that is disproportionate to the severity of the crime. Because the district court acted within its discretion by imposing the double durational departure and because the constitutional arguments in his se brief did not present a basis for reversal, the appellate court affirmed. Defendant's alcohol concentration of .26 was an appropriate aggravating favor in Minn. Stat. § 609.21, subd. 1(4) (2004). The district court also did not abuse its discretion in considering defendant's decayed DWIs. Defendant's argument that his conduct was no more serious than the "normal" criminal-vehicular-homicide case was not supported by the facts. The district court did consider the Trog factors in determining that defendant was not amenable to probation and the district court did not abuse its discretion by declining to apply the Trog factors when addressing the duration of defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1786 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bellanger


A04-1790


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 258



March 20, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Bellanger, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 286 (Minn., May 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Itasca County District Court File No. K0-02-1094. Hon. John Hawkinson.
State v. Bellanger, 2006 Minn. LEXIS 742 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Itasca County District Court, Minnesota, revoking his probation for first-degree assault, and executing his 172-month sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to three misdemeanor offenses, and the district court revoked his probation and executed his sentence. Defendant asserted that he was precluded from challenging his sentence duration because his plea agreement barred him from doing so. The appellate court ruled that there was a difference between having no sentence duration to challenge and having a reason not to do so, even a reason as strong as an agreement not to do so. Defendant's appeal waiver constituted only a reason not to challenge the sentence duration on direct review. Defendant received a significant benefit for the waiver, in the form of a dispositional departure. If the appellate court were to recognize the appeal waiver as justifiable grounds for applying the U.S. Supreme Court Blakely decision retroactively, other grounds would inevitably be advanced and the Blakely retroactivity analysis would evolve from a bright-line rule into a fairness argument dependent on the facts of each individual case. The appellate court declined to open the door to a wide variety of fact-specific exceptions to the bright-line rule distinguishing between direct review and collateral review.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

1787 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ocampo-Perez


A06-1289


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 263



March 20, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Scott County District Court File No. 2004-08608. Hon. William E. Macklin.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Scott County District Court (Minnesota), which imposed a durational departure sentence after he was convicted of aiding and abetting second-degree felony murder.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from a sentence imposed for aiding and abetting second-degree felony murder, the appellate court affirmed, stating that the plea and sentencing occurred at the same hearing, with no break between the plea and sentencing. The record contained significant discussion regarding defendant's stipulation to the aggravating factor of victim vulnerability and how that agreement impacted his sentencing. Further, the district court did make findings that defendant understood his rights and waived them knowingly and voluntarily, and there was a factual basis for his guilty plea. Because there was one continuous plea and sentencing hearing and the record contained significant discussion of defendant's agreement to the upward departure and stipulation to the aggravating factor of victim vulnerability, the district court did not abuse its discretion in imposing an upward departure. Additionally, defendant entered a valid waiver of his right to a hearing on aggravating factors under Blakely.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1788 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Knaffla


A06-1512, A06-1513


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 264



March 20, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Lake County District Court File Nos. 38-CR-05-505, 38-CR-05-504. Hon. Kenneth A. Sandvik.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged in the Lake County District Court (Minnesota) with possession of a stolen firearm, fifth-degree possession of methamphetamine, and possession of marijuana. The trial court granted defendants' motion to suppress and dismissed the charges. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued, inter alia, that based on an officer's testimony that his reason for stopping the vehicle was an ongoing investigation of one defendant he had a lawful basis for the stop. The court of appeals disagreed. The State conceded that there was nothing in the record to indicate that the person driving the vehicle had committed any traffic violation or other criminal activity. The officer admitted that the vehicle had not been seen in the area for a month and that the stop took place in the afternoon, not in the early morning hours when defendant was believed to deliver drugs. The State nonetheless argued that the stop was valid under the totality of the circumstances. The State failed to cite anything indicating that a suspicion that stemmed from an ongoing investigation could constitute a particularized objective basis for an investigatory stop. Even if the ongoing investigation were part of a valid, particularized, and objective basis for the stop, that basis evaporated as soon as officers discovered that the person for whom they were looking was not in the vehicle. Because there was no particularized, objective basis for stopping the vehicle, the stop was illegal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1789 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nace


A06-216


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 239



March 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Nace, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 289 (Minn., May 30, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the St. Louis County District Court, Minnesota, convicting him of fourth-degree assault of a peace officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant scuffled with a police officer who was attempting to question defendant near the scene of a sounding burglar alarm at a downtown business. Defendant argued that the district court abused its discretion by denying his request for a different public defender. The appellate court ruled that the district court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's request for substitute counsel or in any other manner with regard to defendant's representation. Defendant did not argue that exceptional circumstances existed nor had he challenged his attorney's ability or competence to represent him. Defendant never expressed an interest in representing himself and did not discharge his appointed attorney. Also, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of the charged offense. Defendant turned and tried to punch the officer, but the officer backed away from the punch and used a takedown technique to bring defendant to the ground. Defendant resisted and grabbed the officer's legs causing him to fall and scrape his hands and right knee. Defendant did not release the officer's legs until the officer maced him twice, and the altercation lasted 15-20 seconds.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1790 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re N. D. J.


A05-2200


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 231



March 6, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. JX-04-053129. Hon. Philip D. Bush.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile, sought review of the decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which adjudicated him delinquent, imposed disposition, and denied his motion to withdraw his guilty plea. He had pled guilty in Ramsey County and the case was transferred to Hennepin County for disposition.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of an order adjudicating him delinquent, imposing disposition, and denying his motion to withdraw his guilty plea. He argued that his guilty plea was not accurate or intelligent, but the appellate court affirmed, stating that when appellant pled guilty, his competency was not an issue under Minn. R. Juv. P. 20.01, subd. 3. Appellant failed to provide any evidence of his incompetence at the time that he entered his initial plea of guilty. Through defense counsel's questioning, appellant admitted sufficient facts to support his guilty plea. Defense counsel inquired about the amount of time appellant had spent with the public defender discussing the charges, the plea options and meaning of the options, and the consequences of a guilty plea. Based on the totality of the circumstances under Minn. R. Juv. P. 8.04, subd. 1, appellant's guilty plea was voluntary and intelligent. He was not denied due process with the refusal to conduct a second competency hearing because he effectively waived his right to be present since he was in treatment and his public defender made a record of that absence and appellant's location during the hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1791 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Hebert v. City of Fifty Lakes


A06-215


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 207



February 27, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Motion granted by Hebert v. City of Fifty Lakes, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 257 (2007)
Affirmed by Hebert v. City of Fifty Lakes, 2008 Minn. LEXIS 9 (Minn., Jan. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Crow Wing County District Court File No. C2-05-1223. Hon. Richard Zimmerman.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sued respondent city, seeking a declaratory judgment, damages for trespass, and ejectment of the city from a portion of their registered Torrens property. The Crow Wing County District Court found that the city's encroachment constituted a de facto taking and granted the city's motion to dismiss the landowners' claims. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city encroached on the landowners' property when it laid a gravel road in 1971 that deviated from the platted road. The appellate court determined that the district court erred in granting the city's motion to dismiss. Although the landowners' Torrens property was subject to taking by eminent domain under Minn. Stat. § 508.02 (2006), the nature of the damages caused by the city's action more readily constituted a trespass than a de facto taking because the degree of interference by the gravel road at the wrong location was not so substantial as to constitute a taking in the constitutional sense under Minn. Const. art. I, § 13. Thus, the 15-year statute of limitations for recovery of real estate did not apply under Minn. Stat. § 541.02 (2006). The landowners sufficiently stated a claim because (1) the city's failure to abide by the landowners' demand to remove the road supported the continuing trespass and ejectment claims, (2) the six-year statute of limitations for actions in trespass did not run from the initial trespass and therefore was inapplicable to the claims, and (3) even if the trespass claim was untimely, the landowners stated an ejectment claim.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

 

1792 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pahkala


A06-304


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 194



February 20, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County District Court File No. T9-05-10755. Hon. Stephen M. Halsey



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was charged with fourth-degree DWI, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 169A.20, subd. 1(1) (2004). He moved to suppress the test results in the criminal proceedings, arguing that his due-process rights were violated when he was read the implied-consent advisory that the Supreme Court of Minnesota had declared unconstitutional in Fedziuk. The Anoka County District Court (Minnesota) denied the motion, found appellant guilty, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that the court erred in not suppressing evidence obtained under an implied-consent statute that was declared partially unconstitutional for not providing prompt judicial review of a driver's-license revocation. In Fedziuk, the Supreme Court of Minnesota held that the 2003 amendments to the implied-consent statute were unconstitutional as violating due process because they removed the requirement for prompt judicial review of a prehearing revocation. The court severed the unconstitutional provision and revived the version of the implied-consent law existing prior to the 2003 amendments. Accordingly, the implied-consent statute remained in effect. Thus, although appellant was read the implied-consent advisory at a time when the process was governed by a statute that was later declared unconstitutional in part, the portion that was declared unconstitutional did not relate to anything to do with appellant's decision to submit to an Intoxilyzer test. Appellant voluntarily submitted to testing after he consulted with an attorney and the implied-consent advisory did not include misleading language that would have made appellant feel coerced into submitting to a test.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
