State v. Boswell


A05-2377


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 198



February 20, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Boswell, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 244 (2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Boswell v. Symmes, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 126809 (D. Minn., Feb. 6, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Boswell v. State, 2016 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 703 (Minn. Ct. App., July 18, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. 05018292. Hon. Marilyn Brown Rosenbaum.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motion to suppress a handgun found in the basement of the duplex where his mother lived, the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, convicted him of second-degree intentional murder and second-degree assault, and an upward departure sentence was imposed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in finding that he did not have standing to challenge the search of his mother's duplex, the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions, his Blakely waiver was inadequate, and the sentence imposed was unconstitutional. The appellate court disagreed as to all of defendant's points, finding first that the evidence that the trial court found credible supported the finding that defendant did not live with his mother and did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy in the basement. Thus, the trial court did not err in not suppressing the handgun. The evidence was sufficient to support the convictions based on the testimony of several witnesses who identified defendant and saw the shooting, photos of the coat defendant was wearing, the handgun found in the basement, and shell casings found at the scene that matched the gun. Defendant validly waived the jury determination and agreed that the trial court would determine the existence of aggravating factors. Some factors included that defendant put the public at risk, and treated the victim with particular cruelty in that the shooting was unprovoked and done at close range.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1794 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Goetzmann v. Domestic Dev., Inc.


A06-645


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 151



February 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County District Court File No. C3-05-6617. Hon. Leslie May Metzen.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant general contractor appealed from the judgment of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondents on the grounds that the district court erred in its determination that the contractor's settlement agreement with the homeowners was a Pierringer release, and that the contractor's claims were time-barred.


OVERVIEW: The district court did not err by finding that the first settlement agreement controlled. While the contractor had not yet signed it, the homeowners had signed it and received the settlement proceeds a few months before the summary-judgment hearing. Even if the district court was in error and the revised settlement agreement was the appropriate one to consider, the result was the same because both agreements were modified Pierringer releases. Because the agreements were modified Pierringer releases, the contractor had paid no more than its fair share of the common liability to the homeowners. Therefore, the contractor had no remaining third-party claims. The district court did not err in its ruling. Also, the district court did not err by determining that its claims for contribution and indemnity were time-barred by Minn. Stat. § 541.051 (2002) because the claims had not accrued and were not brought within 10 years of the completion of the home's construction. Finally, because the issue had been resolved by the Minnesota Supreme Court in another case, the court concluded that the contractor's due-process rights had not been violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

1795 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


A06-541


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 153



February 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Smith, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 215 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Smith v. Minn., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 10512 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. 03033288. Hon. Francis J. Connolly.
State v. Smith, 2004 Minn. App. LEXIS 1337 (Minn. Ct. App., Nov. 30, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand, the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, resentenced appellant to 240 months in prison for aggravated first-degree robbery, an upward durational departure from the presumptive guidelines sentence, after impaneling a second jury to determine whether he met the criteria for sentencing as a dangerous or career offender under Minn. Stat. § 609.1095 (2002). This appeal, which challenged the court's resentencing procedures, followed.


OVERVIEW: When resentencing defendant, the district court had inherent authority to impanel a second jury to consider whether aggravating factors existed under § 609.1095, subd. 2, even though it lacked legislative authority to do so, and the use of a sentencing jury to consider aggravating factors at the resentencing hearing did not violate the Double Jeopardy Clause of the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments. Because the complaint charging appellant with aggravated first-degree robbery informed him of the nature of the charges and the maximum sentence, failure to include aggravating factors in the complaint did not violate constitutional due-process or notice requirements. Retroactive application of the 2005 amendments to Minn. Stat. § 244.10, subd. 5(a) (2004), and the former version of Minn. Sentencing Guidelines II.D, authorized the district court to impanel a sentencing jury on resentencing of appellant's 2003 conviction and to use the jury's findings to impose a new sentence. The retroactive application of the 2005 amendments did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause of the U.S. and Minnesota constitutions. Appellant's sentence was not unreasonable in light of his criminal history.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1796 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Civil Commitment of Alverson


A06-1567


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 158



February 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Olmsted County District Court File No. 55-P3-05-000409. Hon. Robert Birnbaum.
State v. Alverson, 2002 Minn. App. LEXIS 1372 (Minn. Ct. App., Dec. 17, 2002).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient appealed the judgment of the Olmsted County District Court (Minnesota) that committed him as a sexually dangerous person and a sexual psychopathic personality. The court of appeals disagreed.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to support a finding that he was a sexually dangerous person. The court of appeals disagreed. Although the patient participated in several sex-offender treatment programs he was terminated from each of the programs after violating probation, supervised-release provisions, or program rules. During periods of supervised release and even after the first petition for civil commitment was dismissed, the patient's actions were consistent with his cycle of sexual offending. He maintained contact with minors both in person and on the Internet, viewed pornography, used alcohol, and continually used computers and the Internet to facilitate his sexual behaviors. The district court's determination that the patient was likely to engage in further acts of harmful sexual conduct was supported by the opinions of two experts, and tests indicated that the patient was at a high risk for sexual reoffense. Therefore, clear and convincing evidence supported the district court's determination that the patient was highly likely to engage in future harmful sexual conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1797 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


State v. Simons


A05-2121


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 119



February 6, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Simons, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 242 (Minn., Apr. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Clay County District Court File No. K7-04-1401. Hon. Galen J. Vaa.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Clay County District Court (Minnesota) convicted defendant of two counts of possession of pornographic work involving minors in violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.247, subd. 4 (2004). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the trial court might not have identified the precise ages of the persons depicted in the pornographic videos, it did find that the videos depicted minors, which satisfied Minn. Stat. §§ 617.247, subd. 4 and 617.246, subd. 1(b) (2004). Additionally, nothing in Minn. Stat. § 617.247 required the State to present expert testimony or evidence of the identity of the person depicted. Therefore, the appellate court concluded that it was not necessary that the trial court's finding that the videos depicted minors be supported by expert testimony or evidence of the identities of the persons depicted. In addition, based on the videos, a reasonable fact-finder could have concluded that the persons depicted were, in fact, minors. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to show that the videos depicted minors. In addition, the evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's finding that defendant possessed the two videos with knowledge of their content as he described their content and stated that he watched one more than once. Finally, because there were multiple victims, the trial court did not err in sentencing defendant to concurrent sentences.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1798 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


Hous. & Redevelopment Auth. v. Bloomington Prof'l Bldg., LLC


A06-159


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 105



January 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Hous. & Redevelopment Auth. v. Bloomington Prof'l Bldg., LLC, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 213 (Minn., Apr. 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court File No. CD 2783. Hon. Lloyd B. Zimmerman.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee housing redevelopment authority (HRA) sought to take title and possession of appellant owner's commercial property pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 117.042 (2004), the "quick-take" statute. The Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) found that the taking was for a public purpose, was reasonably necessary to that purpose, was not arbitrary or capricious, and granted the motion to acquire title pursuant to the statute. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner argued that the HRA exceeded its power to take private property, took private property that was not "blighted" for a nonpublic purpose, and took property that was not necessary. The Court of Appeals of Minnesota found that the HRA acted within its authority and the district court properly exercised its discretion. The district court found that the HRA plainly had statutory authority in the instant case based on Minn. Stat. § 469.012, subd. 1g, since the HRA acted for a public purpose and in a public way. The statutory definition of blighted area included both the condition of a service station and retail mall as well as the layout issues confronting the city. It was irrelevant that the owner's property failed to meet the definition of blight because cities acted within their power by eliminating blight on an area basis rather than a structure-by-structure basis. Therefore, the HRA did not exceed its authority in condemning the owner's property. Nor was the HRA's condemnation of the property for an unconstitutional private purpose because transferring it to another private entity for redevelopment did not constitute a private purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1799 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Truck Rental Rate


A06-638


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 113



January 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Department of Labor and Industry File No. 12-1900-16601-2.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator trucking firms filed a petition challenging respondent Minnesota Department of Labor and Industry's (DOLI) decision upholding the certification of truck rental rates, operating costs, and broker fees under the Minnesota Prevailing Wage Law, Minn. Stat. §§ 177.41-.44 (2004). The DOLI Commissioner (Commissioner) adopted an administrative law judge's recommendation to deny the petition. The trucking firms appealed.


OVERVIEW: The DOLI conducted a survey of over 10,000 firms and individuals, received 139 responses, and certified the truck rental rates, operating costs, and broker fees. The court rejected the trucking firms' challenges to the DOLI's order. The Commissioner's decision to conduct a survey to determine operating costs was a reasonable interpretation of Minn. R. 5200.1105 (2005) because the rule was silent on how operating costs were to be gathered and the Commissioner had historically used surveys to determine operating costs. The Commissioner's interpretation that the definition of "trucking firms" under Minn. R. 5200.1106, subpt. 7B (2005) included prime contractors was reasonable. The Commissioner did not err in refusing to disclose the names of the survey respondents because Minn. Stat. §§ 175.24-.27 (2004) clearly prohibited the DOLI from releasing such information. The Commissioner did not unconstitutionally impair existing contracts under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1 and Minn. Const. art. I, § 11, because the certified rates were not retroactive, and the trucking firms could have negotiated terms in their contracts to resolve any conflict.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the DOLI's order.

 

1800 of 1980 DOCUMENTS


In re Civil Commitment of Peria


A06-1452


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


2007 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 114



January 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Civ. Commitment Of: Peria, 2007 Minn. LEXIS 178 (Minn., Mar. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County District Court File No. P9-03-738. Hon. Thomas D. Hayes.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a committed individual (appellant), sought review of the decision of the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), which ordered indeterminate civil commitment after it determined that appellant was a sexually dangerous person (SDP) under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18c(a) (2004) and that he had a sexual psychopathic personality (SPP) as defined by § 253B.02, subd. 18b.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from the district court's order for indeterminate civil commitment, appellant claimed that the district court erred in determining that he was a SPP and a SDP. He was also denied intensive supervised release as a less-restrictive alternative. The appellate court affirmed, stating that appellant's pattern of behavior demonstrated an inability to control sexual urges. The district court's findings were well supported by the record, and the record justified the determination that appellant should be indeterminately committed as an SDP. Appellant needed to address the psychological issues that contributed to his history of sexually deviant behavior and he needed to understand his sex offense cycle, to learn relapse strategies, and to avoid getting into situations that could lead to re-offense. Multiple experts concluded that appellant's behavior demonstrated a habitual course of misconduct, and appellant had threatened to kill a victim and the victim's parents if the victim told anyone about being photographed naked. Additionally, appellant failed to meet his burden of demonstrating a less-restrictive alternative under Minn. Stat. § 253B.185, subd. 1 (2004).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
